# MCNF ‚Äî Worklist

The single durable tracker. Tasks lifted from `docs/COMPLIANCE.md` (sweeps 1 & 2, 2026-06-09).
Status: `[ ]` open ¬∑ `[>]` in progress ¬∑ `[‚úì]` done. Each task carries its finding id + verdict.
Ordered by priority ‚Äî security lock first, then largest structural debt, then mechanical/doc cleanup.

**Operator decisions (2026-06-09):** A1/A2 ‚Üí **DELETE** the labwc/sway surface ¬∑ B1/H6/H3/H4 ‚Üí **BUILD/WIRE** them ¬∑ C1 ‚Üí **implement Phase-G** ¬∑ E1 ‚Üí **retarget tests to Nebula**.

## DRAIN-ENGINE ‚Äî keep the build going until the worklist is clear (operator 2026-06-24; design: docs/design/autonomous-drain.md)
Methods so the autonomous drain can't be derailed by the mechanical failures that halted it (disk wedges 4√ó, sequential grinding, stalling on blockers). Locks: **Hybrid engine** (FARM-AUTO reconciler builds; AI supervises) ¬∑ **Hard enforcement** (local builds impossible) ¬∑ **Park + keep draining** (never stall on one item).
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-1: cargo-farm-guard ‚Äî make local builds impossible.** `install-helpers/cargo-farm-guard.sh` installs AS `cargo`; `build/test/check/clippy/run` exit 97 with a farm redirect, `fmt/metadata` pass through. **Acceptance:** a dev-host `cargo build` exits non-zero with the redirect; `xcp-build.sh` (farm) unaffected. *(verified standalone 2026-06-24: build‚Üí97.)*
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-2: disk-watchdog ‚Äî auto-heal disk pressure.** `install-helpers/disk-watchdog.sh` reclaims stray `target/` + aged logs when free `<` threshold; **active-safe** (never nukes a live agent's worktree). **Acceptance:** below-threshold free space triggers reclaim; a live agent's worktree survives.
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-3: install-drain-guardrails ‚Äî operator-run activator.** `install-helpers/install-drain-guardrails.sh {--install|--uninstall}` installs the guard + a 5-min watchdog systemd timer; reversible (real toolchain preserved as `cargo-real`). **Operator runs it** (self-installing persistence is not agent-authorized). **Acceptance:** `--install` makes the guard live + the timer active; `--uninstall` restores.
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-4: FARM-AUTO reconciler ‚Äî the no-AI mechanical build half.** A timer reads open units tagged `@farm:{crate,verify}`, builds the slice on the farm, opens a PR, flips the task to needs-review ‚Äî no AI tokens in the build loop (¬ß10 / build-platform.md). **Acceptance:** an `@farm`-tagged open unit produces a farm-green PR with zero AI tokens spent; red builds raise a triage task.
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-5: park-and-continue ‚Äî never stall on a blocker.** A unit hitting a live-infra/artifact/gate blocker becomes `[!]` + a `docs/NEEDS-OPERATOR.md` entry; the loop continues with the next unblocked unit. **Acceptance:** a blocked unit appears in NEEDS-OPERATOR.md and the loop advances ‚Äî zero whole-loop stalls attributable to one item. ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-25): `install-helpers/park-blocker.sh <ID> "<reason>"` flips the first open bullet for `<ID>` to `[!]`, annotates it `_(BLOCKED: ‚Ä¶ ‚Äî see NEEDS-OPERATOR.md)_`, surfaces it under "Parked by the drain loop" in `docs/NEEDS-OPERATOR.md`, and exits 0 so the loop continues. Idempotent; word-boundary id match (FAKE-1 ‚âÝ FAKE-10); not-found ‚Üí exit 1; self-tested green. (The prior NEEDS-OPERATOR "blocked: ¬ßC.4 absent" note was itself stale ‚Äî ¬ßC.4 exists ‚Äî now removed.)
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-6: coordinator pattern in /ship.** Encode: pre-flight disk-watchdog ‚Üí saturate N farm agents (disjoint crates, farm-only) ‚Üí on each completion merge+reclaim+relaunch (no batch-wait) ‚Üí park-don't-stall ‚Üí no-flinch. **Acceptance:** with the loop running, N agents stay in flight until the open+unblocked queue is empty; a completed agent is merged+replaced within one tick. ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-25): `install-helpers/drain-coordinator.sh {plan|slots|next|preflight}` encodes the tick (preflight `disk-watchdog.sh` ‚Üí free-slot compute over the REAL `.50/.90/.130` topology, caps 2/2/3 ‚Üí next N open-unblocked unit ids); the ship skill gained a "coordinator loop (DRAIN-5/6/7)" section wiring drain-coordinator + park-blocker + assert-own-worktree with the rearm-don't-batch-wait + park-don't-stall + no-flinch discipline, and its stale `.50/.51/.52` topology table is corrected to `.50/.90/.130`. `slots` verified live (free 2/1/3 ‚Üí 6).
- [‚úì] **DRAIN-7: worktree-isolation discipline.** A subagent strayed into the shared `calm-ray-dcr8` worktree + its work was wiped (2026-06-24). Agents must operate ONLY in their assigned isolated worktree. **Acceptance:** an agent's STEP-0 verifies it is in its own worktree (not the shared one) and refuses to edit/reset the shared checkout. ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-25): `install-helpers/assert-own-worktree.sh` is the agent STEP-0 guard ‚Äî REFUSES (exit 3) the shared `calm-ray-dcr8`/primary checkout, PASSES (exit 0) only from an isolated worktree; `--coordinator` asserts the inverse. Verified: refuse-from-shared, pass-from-isolated (incl. a real `wf_*` worktree), coordinator-from-shared. The ship skill mandates it as every isolated subagent's STEP-0.

## INCIDENT ‚Äî mde-bus broker resilience (BROKER-RESILIENCE-1, diagnosed live 2026-06-25)
A missing/skipped `ntfy` broker (`<overlay_ip>:8443`) was design-"non-fatal" but FATAL in practice: mackesd kept publishing to the unreachable `:8443` (every publish persisted to the `/run/mde-bus` spool, which grew unbounded ‚Äî observed boot-readiness 25M + audit 19M + compute 13M ‚âà 77M of a 190M tmpfs) and the broker-unreachable path starved the 60 s systemd watchdog ‚Üí `status=6/ABRT` ~every 3 min (NRestarts climbing on both lighthouses). The broker client was `reqwest::Client::new()` with NO timeout.
- [‚úì] **BROKER-RESILIENCE-1: a skipped/unreachable broker is truly non-fatal.** Four-part fix: **(1)** the outbound-publish reqwest client now has a CONNECT (3 s) + overall REQUEST (5 s) timeout via a shared `hooks::publisher::broker_client()` used by both the webhook listener and the `mde-bus publish` CLI, so a publish to a dead broker fails FAST instead of hanging ~60 s. **(2)** when `broker::evaluate_prereqs` returns `Skip`, the daemon binds the webhook listener in a new persist-only mode (`ListenerConfig::persist_only_for_overlay_ip`) ‚Äî it still ingests + persists + audits but skips the doomed outbound POST entirely (mirrors `--no-broker`), so a known-absent broker drives no outbound retries. **(3)** a conservative per-topic `/run` cap (`TOPIC_RUN_CAP_BYTES` = 8 MiB + 20k-entry backstop) now bounds EVERY non-audit topic to its most-recent window every retention pass (the analogue of the existing `audit/*` cap), so a down broker can never fill the tmpfs. **(4)** verified the sd_notify watchdog ping rides its own 250 ms timer in mackesd, sharing no task with any broker/spool call. **Acceptance:** a publish to a dead broker returns within the timeout (not ~60 s); a skipped-broker daemon persists without retrying outbound; the spool stays bounded under sustained no-broker publishes. *(build + clippy + new tests GREEN on the farm, slot `brokerfix`.)*
- [‚úì] **BROKER-RESILIENCE-2 / WATCHDOG-2: the watchdog ping was STILL being starved ‚Äî real root cause + fix (11.0.11, 2026-06-27).** BR-1 part (4)'s claim ("the ping rides its own 250 ms timer, sharing no task with any broker/spool call ‚Üí can't be starved") was **false in practice**: both production lighthouses kept watchdog-aborting every ~90 s for ~40 h (lh1 1355 / lh2 1348 `status=6/ABRT`), across 11.0.8‚Üí11.0.10, which blocked every enrollment (`:4243` only up between crashes). The ping rode `tokio::time::sleep` **on the runtime**, and on a **1-vCPU droplet** `new_multi_thread` defaults to a SINGLE worker that also owns the **tokio time driver**; when that worker reaches a blocking bridge (`substrate::peers::block_on` ‚Üí `block_in_place` for an etcd round-trip) the time driver **freezes**, the sleep never fires, and systemd SIGABRTs a healthy daemon. A missing broker reliably triggered it via extra `block_in_place` churn. Fix: **(a)** floor the runtime at 4 worker threads even on 1 vCPU (`bin/mackesd.rs`), so a second worker keeps timers alive while another blocks; **(b)** move the heartbeat to a **dedicated OS thread** gated on an async liveness beacon the serve loop stamps every 250 ms (`sd_notify::watchdog_should_ping`) ‚Äî kernel-scheduled (unstarvable) yet still reflects true liveness (a genuine wedge stops the beat ‚Üí ping withheld ‚Üí systemd restarts). Released as signed **11.0.11** (RSA-4096 d0921c73 verifies on F43) ‚Üí GitHub Release + gh-pages dnf channel (fedora-43/44). **Acceptance:** lh1/lh2 stop crash-looping after upgrade (NRestarts stops climbing, zero new ABRT, `:4243` stays up) ‚Äî the live deploy/verify is the remaining step (operator-gated channel `dnf upgrade`). *(farm: 7/7 lib tests incl. new beacon tests, clippy+fmt clean, `cargo check --bin` exit 0.)*

## LIGHTHOUSE-MIGRATION ‚Äî 3 new lighthouses, retire old 2, move Eagle (DONE 2026-06-27)
Goal: "Create 3 new Lighthouses, Delete the existing 2, move Eagle to the new Lighthouses." **COMPLETE + live-verified.** Live topology is now Eagle (10.42.0.2) + **nyc3 (10.42.0.4) / fra1 (10.42.0.5) / sfo3 (10.42.0.6)**; old lh1 (167.71.247.150) + mcnf-lh2 (68.183.55.253) droplets deleted; etcd = 4 healthy voters; Eagle's roster dials only .4/.5/.6; cross-mesh connectivity verified. Three turn-key code gaps were found+fixed live and shipped (signed, gh-pages dnf channel):
- [‚úì] **11.0.11 WATCHDOG-2** ‚Äî the watchdog crash-loop (see INCIDENT above).
- [‚úì] **11.0.12 LIGHTHOUSE-ENROLL-SELF-CERT** ‚Äî a joined lighthouse self-generates its `/enroll` endpoint cert at startup (CA key present + cert absent), so `:4243` binds and it can SERVE enrollment, not just sign. Proven: a new node enrolled against nyc3.
- [‚úì] **11.0.13 MULTI-LH-IP-ALLOC** ‚Äî overlay-IP allocation now consults the global etcd directory (`allocate_overlay_ip_excluding`), not just the local cert-store, so a joined lighthouse no longer hands a new node a colliding `.1`. Proven: re-test node via nyc3 got 10.42.0.7 (unique).
### Follow-ups (turn-key sharp edges found during the migration)
- [‚úì] **MIG-1: `mackesd remove-peer` must delete the etcd `/mesh/peers/<host>` directory key.** It removes the etcd MEMBER + revokes + bans, but leaves the directory row, so the roster reconcile kept re-adding the dead node until the key was `etcdctl del`'d by hand. Decommission must drop the directory entry too.
- [‚úì] **MIG-2: atomic cross-lighthouse overlay-IP allocation.** _(shipped 11.0.14, d6e6f20)_ 11.0.13 reads the directory at sign time (closes the systematic collision), but two lighthouses signing in the SAME instant can still race (the parallel sfo3+fra1 provision hit a `(overlay_ip,epoch)` UNIQUE collision). Make allocation atomic via an etcd CAS/lease, or serialize signing per mesh.
- [!] **MIG-3: provision the CA-backup passphrase on a joined lighthouse.** _(folds into the operator-run DR ‚Äî see EPIC-DRIVE #4; CA off-fleet push is classifier-blocked for the agent)_ A joined lighthouse holds the CA key but has no backup passphrase credential ‚Üí `SEC-7/ENT-11: the CA is UNBACKED-UP` error each boot. The add-lighthouse flow should seal+distribute (or generate) the backup passphrase so every CA holder is backed up.
- [‚úì] **MIG-4: provision a sequential lighthouse-add (no parallel) or fix MIG-2 first.** _(resolved by MIG-2 ‚Äî atomic alloc landed, so the sequential-only constraint is lifted)_ `do-lighthouse-join.sh` runs must be sequential until MIG-2 lands (parallel runs collide on IP allocation).

## FARM-AUTOSCALE ‚Äî demand-driven elastic build farm (operator 2026-06-24; design: docs/design/farm-autoscale.md)
Tofu auto-scaling + full lifecycle of VM **and** POD resources: each dom0 runs EITHER one hardware-maxing big build VM OR several small VMs/agent pods, created/destroyed by tofu to fit the live build queue ‚Äî best on-demand hardware use. Locks: **demand-driven** (the @farm queue is the signal) ¬∑ **FARM-AUTO reconciler orchestrates** (no AI in the loop) ¬∑ **warm pool, scale-to-zero + snapshot-reset** ¬∑ **mutually-exclusive shapes per dom0, demand wins**.
- [‚úì] **FA-1: tofu shape model.** **As** the farm, **I want** a per-dom0 `shape` var (`big`/`small`/`off`) + `small_count` driving `infra/tofu/build-vms.tf`, **so that** `tofu apply` provisions one hardware-maxing big VM, N standard small VMs, or nothing. **Acceptance:** `shape=big` on BigBoy provisions ~10vCPU/26GiB `mcnf-build-big-52`; `shape=small,count=2` provisions 2 standard VMs; `shape=off` destroys them (scale-to-zero); idempotent re-apply.
- [‚úì] **FA-2: golden `clean` snapshot + fast reset.** **As** the autoscaler, **I want** each toolchained build VM to carry a post-toolchain `clean` snapshot and a `farm-vm reset <vm>` that `xe snapshot-revert`s it, **so that** inter-job state returns to baseline without a full re-clone. **Acceptance:** a build dirties the VM, `reset` reverts to clean (toolchain + sccache priming intact, job state gone), verified on a reset drill.
- [‚úì] **FA-3: the farm-autoscaler reconcile step (no AI).** **As** the FARM-AUTO reconciler, **I want** a step that reads the `@farm` queue, classifies each pending job big/small, computes the desired per-dom0 shape, writes the tofu vars, and `tofu apply`s ‚Äî scaling to zero when idle, **so that** the farm matches demand with zero AI tokens. **Acceptance:** a queued whole-workspace build ‚Üí big VM provisioned + the build runs + scaled down after; many per-crate jobs ‚Üí small√óN provisioned + run in parallel + scaled to zero; no AI tokens spent.
- [‚úì] **FA-4: mutual-exclusion drain/preempt + hysteresis.** **As** a dom0, **I want** to run EITHER big OR small (never both), switching only after draining current jobs, with a min-dwell debounce, **so that** shape changes don't thrash against tofu's ~minutes apply latency. **Acceptance:** a big job queued while smalls run ‚Üí smalls drain, then destroy+provision big; a dom0 never hosts big+small simultaneously; no flip within the dwell window.
- [‚úì] **FA-5: POD-level scaling.** **As** the autoscaler, **I want** to cap agent/build podman pods per VM to its vCPU/RAM budget and fold pod demand into the shape choice, **so that** many queued agent pods provision small√óN rather than starving one big VM. **Acceptance:** pod count per VM never exceeds its core budget; a pod-heavy queue biases the dom0 toward the small shape.
- [‚úì] **FA-6: route builds/agents by shape.** **As** a build job, **I want** `xcp-build.sh` + the drain coordinator to target the autoscaler-provisioned VM matching my shape (big‚ÜíBigBoy's big VM, small‚Üíthe small pool), **so that** jobs land on the right elastic resource. **Acceptance:** a whole-workspace build routes to the big VM; per-crate builds spread across the small pool; routing degrades to BigBoy if the autoscaler is paused.
- [‚úì] **FA-7: lifecycle observability.** **As** an operator, **I want** the autoscaler to log every create/destroy + publish the live farm topology (per-dom0 shape + utilization) to a CLI/Workbench surface, **so that** on-demand use is auditable. **Acceptance:** each scale event is logged with the reason; `farm topology` (CLI + panel) shows current shapes, running VMs, and per-dom0 utilization.

## ENTERPRISE FIT-AND-FINISH (2026-06-11) ‚Äî toward an enterprise-class deliverable

Lifted from a 5-pass parallel fit-and-finish evaluation (reliability ¬∑ security ¬∑ observability ¬∑ packaging/release ¬∑ quality/UX) for an enterprise deliverable **within the stated ‚â§8-peer flat-trust envelope** (¬ß8 ‚Äî NOT a zero-trust/hyperscale product). `EFF-#` ids. P1 = blocks a credible enterprise/production cut.

> **DRAIN STATUS (2026-06-12):** the tractable EFF backlog is drained ‚Äî ~30 items closed this session (EFF-1..17, 19..23, 25..28, 32, 33, 35, 36, 39..44, 46..49) plus the AUD2/AUD3 audit-fix sets and 6 audit cycles (converged CLEAN). **ZERO EFF items remain open ‚Äî the ENTERPRISE FIT-AND-FINISH program is fully drained** (49 items closed/resolved). The only remaining tracker content is the PEERS feature epic (feature backlog, not fit-and-finish). EFF-18 (resolved: operator chose to keep the correct serial CI) and EFF-31 (resolved: hard coverage gate at 84.84%/80) are now closed. The PEERS epic below is feature backlog, not fit-and-finish. Resuming the GUI items is a deliberate next step, not a quick drain.

### P1 ‚Äî blockers for a production cut

- [‚úì] **EFF-1 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ FileXfer Send-To path traversal (target).** `ipc/files.rs:265` joins the `peer:<target>` selector raw into `inbox_root(target)` ‚Äî `peer:../../etc` escapes the QNM root (`create_dir_all` + write anywhere mackesd can). Reject `target` with `/`,`..`,`\0`,non-`[A-Za-z0-9._-]`; assert the resolved dest is under `<qnm>/inbox/`. *(Regression from AUD-1 this session.)*
- [‚úì] **EFF-2 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ FileXfer Send-To arbitrary-file read (sources).** `ipc/files.rs:290` copies caller-supplied absolute `sources` verbatim ‚Üí a Bus writer can exfil `/etc/shadow`/keys into a peer's replicated inbox. Confine sources to an allowlisted root (operator home / declared share); refuse symlinks + paths outside it. ‚Äî DONE: `FileXfer` gained a `share_root` (defaults to the operator home, canonicalized; `with_share_root` override). `allowed_source()` canonicalizes each source (resolving symlinks + `..`), requires a regular file, and refuses anything not `starts_with(share_root)` ‚Äî refused sources are skipped + warn-logged + counted in the reply's `refused` field. Two regression tests: a source outside the root is refused while an in-root one delivers, and a symlink-under-root ‚Üí outside is refused.
- [‚úì] **EFF-3 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ FileXfer rollback path traversal.** `ipc/files.rs:338` removes files from `inbox_root(target).join(host).join(f)` off forgeable outbox rows. Same target/basename validation + canonicalize-and-contain before `remove_file`.
- [‚úì] **EFF-4 ¬∑ REL ¬∑ Supervisor doesn't restart on worker PANIC.** `workers/mod.rs:481` matches only `Ok/Err`; a panicking `run()` becomes a logged `JoinError`, never restarted. Wrap each `worker.run()` so a panic ‚Üí restartable `Err` (feed the back-off/breaker).
- [‚úì] **EFF-5 ¬∑ REL ¬∑ Worker-loop `Mutex.lock().expect()` poisons ‚Üí permanently kills the worker** (compute_expose/firewall_monitor/compute_registry/peer_join). With EFF-4 this silently downs workers. Use poison-tolerant locks (`PoisonError::into_inner`) or `parking_lot`.
- [‚úì] **EFF-6 ¬∑ REL ¬∑ `mackesd healthz` GUI refresh has no timeout** (`panels/mesh_control.rs:606`) ‚Äî a hung daemon spins the panel forever. Run with a timeout wrapper + render "healthz timed out".
- [‚úì] **EFF-7 ¬∑ REL ¬∑ Bus responder threads have no restart + reply closures no `catch_unwind`** (`bin/mackesd.rs:6146`, `ipc/files.rs:64`) ‚Äî one panicking request downs Fleet.Files/Settings/file surfaces for the session. Wrap reply dispatch in `catch_unwind` ‚Üí `err()` body.
- [‚úì] **EFF-8 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ `healthz` returns a hardcoded `HealthReport::empty()`** (`bin/mackesd.rs:1500`, `ipc/shell.rs:102`) ‚Äî never live state (leader/node-count/applied-revision all unset). Populate from the store via one shared fn used by CLI + IPC. *(Highest-value ops gap.)* ‚Äî DONE: `HealthReport::from_store(conn)` populates real node_count + healthy/degraded/unreachable buckets + audit_chain_intact (Break‚Üífalse, Empty/Intact‚Üítrue); wired into CLI `Cmd::Healthz` + `ShellService::build_healthz` (both open the store per call, fall back to `empty()` if no store). Remainder: `is_leader`/`applied_revision` stay defaulted pending leader-lease + applied-revision query plumbing.
- [‚úì] **EFF-9 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ Prometheus textfile exporter built but never written.** `metrics::write_textfile` has zero callers. Add a periodic worker snapshotting control-plane counters (revisions, drift, reconcile failures, breaker trips, peer health, cert-days). ‚Äî DONE: new `metrics_exporter` worker (Lighthouse-tier, 30s cadence) snapshots store-derivable gauges (mesh node-health buckets, audit-chain-intact, applied-migration count) via `snapshot_counters(conn)` reusing `HealthReport::from_store` (single source of truth with healthz), atomically writes `<textfile_collector>/mackesd.prom`. Remainder (follow-ups appending to the same file): runtime in-process counters (drift/reconcile-failures/breaker-trips) need a shared process registry the workers increment; cert days-remaining is EFF-11.
- [‚úì] **EFF-10 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ Structured-logging plane logs human text, not the documented JSON.** `bin/mackesd.rs:1469` uses `fmt()` not `.json()`; `LogContext`/correlation-id unused. Switch the subscriber to JSON (env/flag-gated for TTY) + a span layer for the fields.
- [‚úì] **EFF-11 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ No certificate-expiry monitoring/alert.** Certs store `expire_at` but nothing computes days-remaining; a ‚â§8 mesh silently loses every cert at turnover. Add a periodic check ‚Üí `healthz`/metrics/alert under a threshold. ‚Äî DONE: new `ca::expiry` module probes the **CA cert** (the real cliff ‚Äî peer certs are epoch-lifetime sentinel `0` by design, so per-peer expiry was a non-target) via `nebula-cert print -json` ‚Üí `details.notAfter` ‚Üí days-remaining (pure `parse_not_after_unix` is unit-tested). Wired into the `metrics_exporter` worker: each tick emits `mackesd_ca_cert_days_remaining` (clamped ‚â•0) + `mackesd_ca_cert_expiry_warning` (1 at/under the 30-day threshold) and logs a warn under threshold (the alert). Remainder: surfacing days-remaining on `healthz`/HealthReport would need `from_store` to take the CA path + run the subprocess (it's store-only today) ‚Äî Prometheus alert-rule on the metric covers the operational need; the healthz field is a thin follow-up.
- [‚úì] **EFF-12 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ systemd units have no sandboxing.** `packaging/systemd/*.service` set only `NoNewPrivileges`. Add `ProtectSystem=strict`, `ProtectHome`, `PrivateTmp`, `ReadWritePaths`/`StateDirectory`, `RestrictAddressFamilies`, `MemoryMax`/`CPUQuota`, `LockPersonality`.
- [‚úì] **EFF-13 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ RPM license contradicts the workspace license + copyleft deps.** generate-rpm `license = "proprietary"` vs workspace `GPL-3.0-or-later` + MPL/GPL pop-os deps. Reconcile the license string; add root `LICENSE`/`COPYING` + a `NOTICE` for bundled deps.
- [‚úì] **EFF-14 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ No RPM scriptlets** ‚Äî daemon never enabled, no `systemctl daemon-reload`, no icon/desktop cache, no `/etc/mackesd` dir. Add `post_install`/`preun`/`post_uninstall` (daemon-reload + role-policy enable + `gtk-update-icon-cache` + `update-desktop-database`).
- [‚úì] **EFF-15 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ `mackesd.service` won't start without the encrypted credential** (`LoadCredentialEncrypted=‚Ä¶/backup-passphrase.cred`, never created) ‚Äî fresh install = dead unit. Make the credential optional (Condition/wrapper) + create `/etc/mackesd` (0700) in a scriptlet.
- [‚úì] **EFF-16 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ No supply-chain gating.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): `deny.toml` (advisories deny-level w/ unmaintained=workspace-only; license allow-list scoped to what the tree ships, per-crate exceptions for rsip's X11-swapped text, clarifies for the license-field-less pop-os git crates; bans deny openssl/native-tls per ¬ß3, multiple-versions warn pending EFF-34; sources locked to crates.io + the pinned pop-os tree). Validated GREEN locally (cargo-deny 0.19.8: advisories/bans/licenses/sources all ok) so the new `supply-chain` CI job is a HARD gate; it also emits a CycloneDX SBOM artifact (cargo-cyclonedx). Bonus hardening en route: migrated mackes-nebula-https-tunnel off unmaintained `rustls-pemfile` (RUSTSEC-2025-0134) onto rustls-pki-types' PemObject; added the missing `license` field to 5 workspace crates; RUSTSEC-2023-0071 (rsa Marvin) ignored with written justification (keygen-only usage, no remote timing oracle ‚Äî ring does wire sign/verify).
- [‚úì] **EFF-17 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ `magic-mesh-release` repo RPM referenced but never defined** (`packaging/repo/magic-mesh.repo:11`) ‚Äî so `dnf install <url>` leaves no repo for upgrades + the `gpgkey=` URL has no key. Define the release sub-package shipping the `.repo` + committed `RPM-GPG-KEY-magic-mesh`. ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): generated the project signing key (Ed25519, 2y expiry; private key in the operator's `~/.gnupg`, revocation cert in `openpgp-revocs.d`); committed the public key at `packaging/repo/RPM-GPG-KEY-magic-mesh`. One-RPM design (no sub-package): the main RPM now ships the `.repo` ‚Üí `/etc/yum.repos.d/` + the key ‚Üí `/etc/pki/rpm-gpg/`, so a one-shot install leaves a working gpgcheck'd upgrade channel. Signing the RPM itself stays operator-gated at /release; the gh-pages publish of the key matches the gpgkey URL when stood up.
- [‚úì] **EFF-18 ¬∑ QA ¬∑ `set_var` env-race forces serial mackesd CI.** ‚Äî RESOLVED (2026-06-12, operator decision: option 3 ‚Äî keep the serial flag). The `--test-threads=1` run is CORRECT and green; mackesd's ~61 `set_var`/`remove_var` test sites mutate process-global env, which races the parallel harness. This was a CI-SPEED optimization only, and both alternatives carry flakiness risk (inject-config = large production ripple; `serial_test` = must annotate every env *reader*, not just writers). Operator chose to accept the safe serial suite rather than trade correctness for speed. WON'T-DO unless mackesd test latency becomes a real CI pain point, at which point option 1 (inject config) is the path. The CI job comments already document the serial requirement + this rationale.
- [‚úì] **EFF-19 ¬∑ CLI ¬∑ `magic-fleet` is a hand-rolled CLI** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): full clap derive port (real `--help`/`-V`, typed flags, unknown-flag errors with usage; `--root=`/`--hostname=` syntax the fleet_reconcile worker shells stays accepted). `--json` added to apply/heal/converge/elect/reconcile emitting one stable outcome object ({verb, drift, ok, changed, failures, unreachable, converged}; error form {verb, error, converged:false}); exit codes unchanged. Smoked: help, bad-flag rejection, apply --json round-trip; 49 tests green.

### P2 ‚Äî enterprise ratchet

- [‚úì] **EFF-20 ¬∑ REL ¬∑ ~8 daemon workers shell out blocking, no timeout** (firewall_preset/mesh_dns/mesh_firewall/cups_sync/netassess/peer_cap/netdata_aggregator/ssh_pubkey_gossip) ‚Äî a hung child pins a runtime thread. Route through the existing `subprocess_tick` timeout helper. ‚Äî DONE: new `workers/proc.rs` with `output_with_timeout`/`status_with_timeout` (blocking, dependency-free poll+kill) for the sync `tick_once` helpers and `status_with_timeout_async` (tokio) for the already-async workers, all killing the child at a 15s deadline. Routed every shell-out in all 8 workers (firewall_preset √ó5, cups_sync central run_lpadmin/run_capture + systemctl/lpoptions/hostname, netassess run_stdout/binary_present/ping, mesh_firewall, mesh_dns, netdata_aggregator systemctl, peer_cap + ssh_pubkey_gossip async). A hung child is now bounded to the timeout instead of pinning forever. Helper has 5 tests (kills a `sleep 60` promptly, captures fast output, surfaces spawn failure, async variant). Minor follow-up hygiene: the sync `tick_once`es still run on the runtime thread (now bounded, not infinite) ‚Äî wrapping them in `spawn_blocking` would also keep a slow-but-not-hung child off the scheduler.
- [‚úì] **EFF-21 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ Secrets via env-var + argv.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): (1) **daemon env scrub** ‚Äî run_serve captures `MDE_BACKUP_PASSPHRASE` once at boot, hands it to the backup worker via `with_passphrase`, and `remove_var`s it immediately, so the dozens of worker subprocesses (nebula-cert, df, firewall-cmd‚Ä¶) never inherit the secret; the exporter's backup-posture gauge rides a boot-time flag OR the systemd-creds file instead of a per-tick env read. The creds path (ENT-11, never env-borne) is untouched and stays preferred. (2) **stdin intake** ‚Äî `ca export`/`ca import` gained `--passphrase-stdin` (import requires `--input` since its default bundle source is stdin); `enroll` gained `--passcode-stdin`/`--token-stdin` with full clap conflict rules; shared `read_secret_line` helper, empty-secret rejected. Argv/env forms remain as documented fallbacks with prefer-stdin help text. Smoked: stdin passcode read+validation, help text, conflict rejection. 1448 serial green.
- [‚úì] **EFF-22 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ Netdata `:19999` web UI not confined to the overlay** (aggregator rewrites only `[stream]`). Set `[web] bind to = <overlay-ip>`/127.0.0.1 and/or land the firewalld rule (the open NET-plane item). ‚Äî DONE: generalized the conf rewriter to `rewrite_named_section` and added `build_web_block` ‚Äî the aggregator now also writes a `[web] bind to = 127.0.0.1 <overlay-ip>` block each tick (loopback-only pre-enrolment), so the dashboard never binds the default `0.0.0.0`/underlay. Also fixed a latent non-idempotency in the rewriter (it grew a blank line per pass ‚Üí would have churned a netdata reload every tick); the trailing blank run is now collapsed so an unchanged conf is a true no-op. Tests: web block confines to overlay+loopback / loopback-only, a stock `0.0.0.0` bind is rewritten away, and re-running is idempotent.
- [‚úì] **EFF-23 ¬∑ SEC ¬∑ No body-size cap on Bus responders** ‚Äî `from_str` on unbounded bodies; cap inbound length + `sources`/row counts before parse. ‚Äî DONE: shared `ipc::MAX_RPC_BODY_BYTES` (64 KiB) + `body_within_cap()` + `body_too_large_reply()`. Applied at every body-parsing responder loop (files generic `poll_once`, fleet, settings, jobs, directory lifecycle-result/lifecycle/wake) ‚Äî an over-cap body is refused with an `{"error":‚Ä¶}` envelope + warn, never reaching `from_str`. send-to also caps `sources` at 1024 rows. Tests: over-cap body suppressed + within-cap dispatched.
- [‚úì] **EFF-24 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ No readiness probe / per-worker liveness.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): supervisor maintains a shared `WorkerStatusMap` (alive / restarts / breaker_tripped / last_exit_ok, updated at every lifecycle transition incl. ENT-6 trips); `HealthReport` gains serde-defaulted `workers_alive/workers_total/breaker_tripped/ready`; the Bus healthz (daemon in-process) folds live worker status into `ready` = audit-intact AND all-alive AND no-trip, while the CLI's store-only view reports the store half. Tests: lifecycle/restart tracking, alive-while-running, readiness fold (dead worker or trip ‚áí not ready). Honest remainder: 'leader known' stays out of `ready` until the EFF-8 leader-lease plumbing lands.
- [‚úì] **EFF-25 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ Wire or remove the dead alert layer.** `events.rs`/`AlertHook`/`dispatch_alerts` have no live callers; only `Reconcile` of 5 `EventKind`s is emitted. Wire it + emit the missing kinds, or delete + document Netdata+firewall_monitor as the only sources. ‚Äî DONE (wired, 2026-06-12): `MackesdConfig` gained `[[alert_hooks]]` (kind + command, fail-open TOML; typo'd kind drops the hook with a warn ‚Äî never widened to fire-on-everything; empty command skipped) + `alert_hooks()` resolving to `events::AlertHook`. `apply_repair_rows` now returns its emitted `Event`s and the reconcile tick fires `dispatch_alerts` post-commit (a rolled-back event can never alert). Tests: TOML‚Üíhook resolution incl. drop/skip cases. Remainder (honest): only `Reconcile` events are emitted today; emitting `ConfigChange`/`Auth`/`Lifecycle`/`AdminAction` at their natural sites flows through the same dispatch automatically.
- [‚úì] **EFF-26 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ Headless alert path + disk/breaker/backup alerts.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): (1) alert_relay now journals EVERY alert at its severity level (`target: mackesd::alert`, error/warn/info) unconditionally and FIRST ‚Äî on a headless Lighthouse/Server the journal is the alert surface; Bus-FDO/notify-send toasts are additive. (2) The metrics exporter gained the continuous checks, each a gauge + a `mackesd::alert`-target journal alert: worker liveness/breaker (`mackesd_workers_alive/total`, `mackesd_breaker_tripped`; trip = repeated crit ERROR), disk headroom per monitored fs via bounded `df` (`mackesd_disk_available_bytes{path}`; warn <10% free; QNM root + store fs wired), and backup posture (`mackesd_backup_passphrase_set`, `mackesd_backup_age_seconds`; warns on passphrase-unset, >48h staleness, and enabled-but-no-bundle). Operators alert off either the journal (`journalctl -t ‚Ä¶ mackesd::alert`) or the Prometheus series.
- [‚úì] **EFF-27 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ No day-2 admin guide.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): root `ADMIN.md` walks the full lifecycle (install/first-boot ‚Üí mesh-init + enroll ‚Üí backup provision incl. the unset-passphrase alert behavior ‚Üí observability table (healthz/doctor/journal-alerts/metrics/hooks) ‚Üí dnf + fleet upgrade ‚Üí fleet rollback + node exceptions ‚Üí state-restore/ca-import DR ‚Üí cert lifecycle (days-remaining cliff, rotate, decommission, passcode) ‚Üí troubleshoot), cross-linking every docs/help runbook. All cited commands verified against the live CLI. Ships in the RPM at /usr/share/magic-mesh/.
- [‚úì] **EFF-28 ¬∑ OPS ¬∑ DR path untested + manual.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): (1) `mackesd state-restore --verify` ‚Äî dry-run that dearmors + unseals + reports the bundle (mesh id, exported_at, CA/peer counts, meshfs presence) and stops before ANY mutation; exit 0 = restorable with this passphrase. (2) `tests/dr_drill.rs` walks the mesh-recovery runbook against the real library surfaces: surviving sealed+armored bundle ‚Üí fresh empty store (the rebuilt box) ‚Üí wrong-passphrase rejected ‚Üí restore lands every CA/peer row (values asserted) ‚Üí post-restore a new single-use enroll bearer mints (43-char base64url contract verified) ‚Üí export-after-restore re-seals + round-trips (the backup chain re-establishes). Plus a tampered-ciphertext rejection test. Both green.
- [‚úì] **EFF-29 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ Daemon runs as root, no service identity.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12, decided + documented + hardened): root is INTENTIONAL ‚Äî mackesd is the node's system-management plane (writes /etc/nebula + /etc/hosts + voice configs, drives firewalld/systemctl/CUPS/sshd/dnf); DynamicUser or a %pre user breaks every one of those paths or re-grants them via a sudo/polkit matrix wider than root. The decision now lives in the unit itself, alongside the containment: `CapabilityBoundingSet=~` drops the never-needed cap classes (module/rawio/boot/time, audit, MAC, suspend/lease/immutable, pacct/tty/ipclock) + ProtectKernelModules/ProtectClock/SystemCallArchitectures=native on top of the EFF-12 set. `systemd-analyze verify` clean (also dropped the removed CPUAccounting option).
- [‚úì] **EFF-30 ¬∑ PKG ¬∑ RPM GPG signing + ISO checksum/signature undefined.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): `install-helpers/sign-release.sh` (operator-gated, invoked from /release, never CI) ‚Äî rpmsign-embeds the project signature into any .rpm argument, then writes `SHA256SUMS` + a detached armored `SHA256SUMS.asc` covering every artifact (the ISO path). Fails early without the secret key. **Smoked end-to-end with the real project key:** checksum validates, `gpg --verify` returns Good signature. Release skill updated to invoke it.
- [‚úì] **EFF-31 ¬∑ CI ¬∑ Coverage gate is advisory (`continue-on-error`).** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): flipped to a HARD gate (removed `continue-on-error`). The denominator is now the meaningful **library-logic** set ‚Äî the 7 iced/libcosmic GUI crates `--exclude`d (render code, correctness via mde-theme tokens + the lifted visual gate, not headless line-coverage) and the binary entrypoints (`src/bin/*.rs`, `src/main.rs` ‚Äî CLI dispatch + daemon bootstrap glue; mackesd.rs alone is ~5.7k integration-level lines) `--ignore-filename-regex`'d. Measured 84.84% lines on that denominator (cargo-llvm-cov 0.8.7) ‚Üí an 80 floor with ~5% margin; mackesd runs `--test-threads=1` (EFF-18 env-race). Floor ratchets up as coverage grows; lowering needs a deliberate edit.
- [‚úì] **EFF-32 ¬∑ CI ¬∑ Build on the real target.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12, scoped): new `fedora` CI job builds+tests the workspace in a `fedora:44` container with the documented dnf dev libs AND the platform binaries (nebula, ansible-core) present, using Fedora's shipped rustc ‚Äî exactly the mock/RPM build reality. Advisory until soaked on the runner fleet (the ubuntu gates stay required). MSRV check: already enforced (every required job pins 1.85 and builds the full workspace ‚Äî EFF-33). Honest remainder: **aarch64** needs an arm64 runner or a full ALSA/GTK cross sysroot ‚Äî tracked, deliberately not faked with a check-only cross job.
- [‚úì] **EFF-33 ¬∑ DEPS ¬∑ MSRV drift.** `rust-toolchain.toml` 1.94 vs `rust-version`/CI 1.85. Reconcile + enforce with the MSRV job. ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-12): not a conflict ‚Äî the two bound opposite ends, now documented at both sites: `rust-version = 1.85` is the MSRV **floor**, already enforced (every ci.yml job builds+tests the full workspace on pinned 1.85 ‚Äî that IS the MSRV job); `rust-toolchain.toml` 1.94 is the dev/build **ceiling** (softbuffer 0.4.8 breaks on 1.95; drop when softbuffer 0.5 lands).

FINISH ‚Äî rewrite the header to the shipped reality (NAT-class is the only honest remaining gap).

## MESH-BRINGUP ‚Äî findings from the live 4-node bring-up (2026-06-13)

Surfaced standing up a fresh `magic-mesh` across 2 public-IP cloud lighthouses + 2 NAT'd LAN peers (operator-directed test). Both are real; logged before continuing the hand-assembled test mesh.

- [‚úì] **MESH-1 ¬∑ DESIGN/SEC ¬∑ enrollment has no network bootstrap ‚Äî remote/NAT'd peers can't self-join.** `nebula_enroll` is *QNM-Shared-mediated only*: the peer writes `pending-enroll.json` to the shared volume, the lighthouse auto-signer writes the bundle back (error path literally says "Check QNM-Shared is mounted + writable"). A fresh peer must therefore *already* share QNM-Shared (LizardFS/NFS) with the lighthouse ‚Äî but QNM-Shared rides the overlay, and you can't reach the overlay until enrolled ‚Üí chicken-and-egg with no built-in resolver. The join token carries the lighthouse's public addr but enroll never uses it for the *signing handshake* (only for the later `static_host_map`). bed-mesh "worked" only because the co-located cloud pair NFS-shared QNM-Shared out-of-band; the LAN peers needed a `fuse-sshfs` bridge hack. **FINISH:** add a network enrollment path ‚Äî lighthouse exposes a CSR-sign endpoint on its public IP (reuse the nebula-https-tunnel :443 / bearer-authed) so a remote peer submits its CSR + gets the signed bundle over the network, *then* mounts QNM-Shared over the overlay for steady state. The shared-FS path is fine for co-located nodes; it cannot be the only path for a public-lighthouse mesh.
- [‚úì] **MESH-2 ¬∑ BUG ¬∑ peer materialized the lighthouse `static_host_map` with a LOCAL interface IP.** On the `fedora` peer, `nebula_supervisor` rendered `/etc/nebula/config.yaml` as `"10.42.0.1": ["192.168.122.1:4242"]` ‚Äî `192.168.122.1` is the peer's own libvirt `virbr0`, not the lighthouse's public `45.55.33.179`. The received bundle was CORRECT (`external_addr: 45.55.33.179:4242`); the render clobbered it with a locally-detected address ‚Üí nebula dials a dead end, overlay never forms (100% loss). The co-located cloud peer `.51` rendered correctly (it has no libvirt/global-scope local IP to mis-pick). **FINISH:** root-cause the static_host_map render ‚Äî the lighthouse entry must use `bundle.lighthouses[].external_addr`, never a locally-detected interface address; add a render test pinning a non-self lighthouse entry to the bundle's external_addr even when the local host has a global-scope private IP (libvirt/docker bridges).

## ONBOARD ‚Äî Magic onboarding: network enrollment + zero-friction join (design: docs/design/magic-onboarding.md, 2026-06-13)

Fixes MESH-1 by promoting cert-signing from a shared filesystem to a lighthouse network service, + collapses setup to two verbs with a TUI. ¬ß1: Nebula control plane only (no Tailscale/Headscale/DERP). Locks: dedicated rustls HTTPS `/enroll` endpoint ¬∑ token-pinned cert fingerprint ¬∑ `found`+`join` verbs ¬∑ ratatui TUI.

- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-1: join token v3 ‚Äî embed the endpoint cert fingerprint + enroll port.** Done ‚Äî `nebula_enroll.rs` `JoinToken` gained `fp: Option<String>` (`#[serde(default, skip_serializing_if)]`, additive); wire form `mesh:<id>@<ip>:<port>#<bearer>?fp=<sha256-hex>`; `parse_join_token` splits `?fp=` off the bearer + validates 64-char lowercase hex; `encode()` round-trips the suffix; `JOIN_TOKEN_MAX_LEN` 120‚Üí200 (fits the +68-char fp, still QR-friendly). v2.5 tokens parse with `fp: None`. 36/0 lib tests (added `parse_round_trips_a_token_with_fp` + `parse_rejects_malformed_fp`). *(Mint-side fp injection lands with the endpoint in ONBOARD-2/4 ‚Äî the fp is the endpoint cert's, which doesn't exist until `found`.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-2: lighthouse rustls `/enroll` endpoint.** Done. New `nebula_enroll_endpoint` module: self-signed endpoint identity (`generate_endpoint_identity` ‚Üí cert/key PEM + SHA-256 `fingerprint` of the DER, the value tokens pin), minimal HTTP/1.1 framing (`parse_request`, 64 KiB body cap), and the pure `handle_enroll` (parses a `PendingEnrollment`, signs via the new shared `sign_csr_into_bundle` core, redeems the single-use bearer, returns the bundle JSON; maps SignCsrError ‚Üí 400/401/403/409/500). New `workers::nebula_enroll_listener` rustls worker (default `:4243`, ring provider, per-conn timeout, spawn_blocking signing) wired into `run_serve` ‚Äî spawns only when the endpoint cert is present (same gate as the covert :443 listener; peer-role boxes skip), roster reuses the csr-watcher external-addr probe so bundles advertise the PUBLIC addr (MESH-2 guard). `sign_pending_csr` refactored to delegate to the shared core (file flow unchanged, 13/13 sign tests green). **Real end-to-end TLS test:** a fp-pinning rustls client POSTs a CSR ‚Üí 200 + bundle ‚Üí bearer spent. 54/0 nebula_enroll tests. *(`found`-time cert generation + token-fp injection wire up in ONBOARD-4; the cert-gen + fp primitives they need are built here.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-3: peer network-enroll client (fingerprint-pinned).** Done ‚Äî new `nebula_enroll_client` module. `PinnedCertVerifier` (rustls `ServerCertVerifier`): accepts ONLY the cert whose SHA-256 == token fp AND verifies the TLS handshake signature via the ring provider (so a MITM can neither swap the cert nor replay the public cert without its key ‚Äî fail-closed). `enroll_over_network` opens a fp-pinned TLS conn, POSTs the CSR to `/enroll`, parses status+bundle (maps non-200 ‚Üí `Refused{status,message}`). `network_enroll` builds identity+CSR from the token, enrolls, and `persist_bundle`s ‚Äî materializes `/etc/nebula` via the supervisor's `materialize_config` (`static_host_map` from `external_addr`, MESH-2 guard) + drops the bundle at QNM-Shared `bundle_path` for steady-state. **Full-stack tests** (real pinned client ‚Üî real `serve_connection`): happy path ‚Üí bundle + bearer spent + config.yaml carries the PUBLIC `203.0.113.7:4242`; **fp-mismatch ‚Üí fail-closed, bearer NOT spent**. 60/0 nebula_enroll tests. *(`serve`‚Üíoverlay dial is exercised live in ONBOARD-8; the materialized config that drives it is verified here.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-4: `found` + `join` verbs.** Done ‚Äî two new CLI verbs in `bin/mackesd.rs`. `mackesd found <mesh-id> [--external-addr auto] [--role] [--enroll-port]`: detects the primary outbound IPv4 (UDP-connect trick; behind-NAT operators pass it explicitly), generates + persists the `/enroll` endpoint identity (`/etc/nebula/enroll-endpoint.{crt,key}`, key 0600), runs `mesh_init` (role pin + CA + self-sign + bundle + bearer), then re-expresses the minted bearer as a **v3 token** pinning the endpoint fp + enroll port pointing at the public IP, and prints a ready-to-paste `mackesd join '<token>'` line. `mackesd join <token> [--role] [--name]`: parses the token, pins the role (if unpinned), and ‚Äî when the token carries `fp` ‚Äî runs the fingerprint-pinned `network_enroll` (ONBOARD-3) materializing `/etc/nebula`; fp-absent tokens fall back to the legacy QNM-Shared `enroll_with_token`; no token ‚Üí launches the `mde-enroll` TUI (ONBOARD-5) with a clear fallback message. The `nebula-enroll-listener` activates on the next `serve` (the cert now exists). Smoked: `found --help`, `join` bad-token ‚Üí "invalid join token", `join` no-token ‚Üí TUI-fallback guidance. The found‚Üíjoin token/enroll path is the exact shape ONBOARD-3's full-stack test exercises end-to-end. 60/0 enroll tests, clean clippy.
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-5: ratatui enrollment TUI (`mde-enroll`).** Done ‚Äî new `crates/mesh/mde-enroll` crate (ratatui 0.29 + crossterm 0.28). Full-screen TUI: a lighthouse-IP override field + a token field (paste target, Tab to switch), Enter to join, a live 5-step progress tracker (Validate ‚Üí Pin cert + send CSR ‚Üí Receive bundle ‚Üí Write /etc/nebula ‚Üí Bring up overlay) with `[ ]`/`[>]`/`[‚úì]`/`[‚úó]` glyphs, a status strip (red on error/fail, green on done), and a footer of keybindings; `r` retries, `q`/Esc quits. The enroll runs on a worker thread driving the real ONBOARD-3 stages (`build_identity`‚Üí`build_pending`‚Üí`enroll_over_network`‚Üí`persist_bundle`‚Üí`systemctl`) and streams progress to the UI over an mpsc channel, so the UI stays responsive. Pure state machine in `app.rs` is fully unit-tested (6/0: typing/focus, validation incl. fp-less + IP-override, step progression, failure+retry, frozen-during-enroll). Terminal-native colors (no ¬ß4 `from_rgb` ‚Äî carbon lint clean). `mackesd join` with no token launches it; shipped in the RPM at `/usr/bin/mde-enroll`. Runs headless over SSH. *(`persist_bundle` made pub so the TUI shares the client's building blocks rather than reimplementing them.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-6: QNM-Shared over the overlay (steady state).** Done. The shared-state plane (leader lease, peer directory, fleet/health, CA) lives on QNM-Shared, which the code always assumed was a mounted LizardFS volume but no deployment ever provisioned ‚Üí multi-node meshes silently showed NO LEADER + empty directory. Built: (1) `install-helpers/setup-qnm-shared.sh` ‚Äî reproducible, boot-durable LizardFS over the overlay (`--master` lighthouse-only ¬ß8, `--chunkserver` ‚â•2 for goal 2, `--client` mfsmount at `/root/QNM-Shared`); generates systemd units (master drop-in `After=nebula` + ExecStartPre stale-lock clear so unclean shutdown self-heals; chunkserver drop-in; `qnm-shared.service` oneshot mount `After=nebula` `Before=mackesd` with master-reachability wait + `Restart`; mackesd ordered after it). All listeners overlay-bound (FS master never public). (2) `workers/leader_election.rs` ‚Äî continuous lease renewal every 20s (the election primitive existed but only the upgrade-watcher ever called it, and only mid-upgrade ‚Üí steady-state meshes never elected). **Live 4-node result:** LizardFS master(.179)+2 chunkservers(.179,.51)+4 client mounts over the overlay, cross-node replication verified, **leader elected (`peer:Lighthouse-02`)**, `mackesd peers` shows all 4 online+healthy from every node, all qnm/lizardfs services `enabled` (boot-durable). F44 LAN boxes use the F43 `lizardfs-client` RPM (runs on F44, like mackesd).

### ONBOARD-6 follow-ups (the audit-gap process fixes the operator requested 2026-06-14)
- [‚úì] **OB6-FIX-1: multi-node integration test.** Done ‚Äî `crates/mesh/mackesd/tests/mesh_shared_state.rs` points TWO node-instances at ONE shared dir (the faithful stand-in for the gap, which was the *absence* of sharing) and asserts the cross-node invariants the old per-tempdir tests never could: exactly one node wins leadership on the shared lock (the other follows), a heartbeat on node A is visible in node B's directory, and healthz `node_count`/`is_leader` reflect the shared mesh (not an empty local store). 3/3 green. (Real nebula transport stays covered by OBS-1's container suite; the LizardFS deploy by `setup-qnm-shared.sh`.)
- [‚úì] **OB6-FIX-2: audit check for unprovisioned preconditions.** Done ‚Äî new audit pass #7 in `.claude/skills/audit/SKILL.md` ("Unprovisioned infrastructure preconditions" ‚Äî flag features that read a shared path/mount/daemon whose only coverage is a single-instance tempdir/mock; require a multi-node assertion + a fail-loud runtime check) + `install-helpers/lint-shared-substrate.sh` (tripwire: the watchdog mount-assert + the multi-node test must stay; advisory list of shared-root readers). ¬ß7 = necessary, not sufficient.
- [‚úì] **OB6-FIX-3: health assertion QNM-Shared is a real mount.** Done ‚Äî `mesh-health-check.sh` now checks `/root/QNM-Shared` is a fuse mount (not a silent local dir) and recovers `qnm-shared.service` + alerts loudly if not. Fail-loud, not silent.
- [‚úì] **OB6-FIX-4: wire healthz `node_count`/`is_leader`.** Done ‚Äî `leader::read_current_lease` (read-only holder), `HealthReport::with_mesh`, and `DirectoryService::mesh_health_counts` (counts from the LIVE directory + leader lease, the same peer set `mackesd peers` shows). Both healthz paths apply it (the CLI + `ipc::shell::build_healthz`; `ShellState` gained `workgroup_root`+`node_id`). **Live:** `.179` reports `is_leader:true, node_count:4, healthy_nodes:4`; `.13` `is_leader:false, node_count:4, healthy:4` ‚Äî the Mesh-Control card now matches the Inventory. *(Note: the CLI healthz still shows `workers_alive:0` ‚Äî worker liveness is the daemon's in-memory view, surfaced only on the bus path the Workbench uses, per EFF-24; not a regression.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-7: portable build for older-glibc (F43) lighthouses.** Done ‚Äî `install-helpers/build-rpm-fedora43.sh` rolls a Fedora-43 RPM inside a `fedora:43` podman container (the F44 binaries *run* on F43 unchanged; the blocker was the RPM's auto-generated `GLIBC_2.43` Requires, which a container build keyed to F43's glibc fixes). The script installs the workspace build deps (incl. `opus-devel` for the audio link) + the rust-toolchain.toml-pinned rustup toolchain (1.94.0), reuses the host's `~/.cargo` caches, builds the full workspace release, and runs `cargo generate-rpm`. **Validated:** the resulting `magic-mesh-10.0.0-1.x86_64.rpm` Requires only unversioned `libc.so.6` (no GLIBC_2.43), `dnf install`s cleanly in a fresh fedora:43 (`Complete!`), and `mackesd`/`mde-enroll`/`found` all run there. This is the `--rpm-url` portable build Option A needs for older DO images / the F43 droplets. *(Serving it via a gh-pages `fedora-43-x86_64/` channel dir + signing stays operator-gated under `/release`.)*
- [‚úì] **ONBOARD-8: live multi-node enroll test.** Done ‚Äî proven on a **real 4-node mesh** (2026-06-14): lighthouse re-founded on the F43 droplet `45.55.33.179` with the new build (the `/enroll` endpoint live on `:4243`, endpoint fp `077d5378‚Ä¶`), then three peers network-enrolled via a single `mackesd join '<v3-token>'` each ‚Äî the F43 droplet `159.65.183.51` (headless server, `10.42.0.2`), the F44 dev host behind NAT (`10.42.0.3`), and the F44 UNIT-EAGLE LAN box behind NAT (`10.42.0.4`). **Full any-to-any overlay connectivity, 0% packet loss** (incl. cross-peer LAN‚Üîdroplet via lighthouse relay); the materialized `static_host_map` correctly advertised the lighthouse's **public** `45.55.33.179:4242` (MESH-2 guard held in the wild). Mixed F43/F44 binaries interoperated. The fp-mismatch refusal is covered by the full-stack unit test (ONBOARD-3). This is the MESH-1 fix working end-to-end across the public internet + NAT.

## SETUP ‚Äî full-lifecycle `magic-setup` wizard (design: docs/design/magic-setup-wizard.md, 2026-06-14)

Single verbose ratatui wizard from `dnf install` ‚Üí running mesh member. Locks: one `magic-setup` binary (grown from mde-enroll) ¬∑ console first-run unit + MOTD ¬∑ hybrid Ansible (verbs bootstrap, Ansible converges) ¬∑ **up to 3 lighthouses + 9 peers (12 nodes)** ¬∑ mesh identified by lighthouse IP ¬∑ all Full/most Headless behind hostile NAT.

- [‚úì] **SETUP-0: governance ‚Äî raise the envelope to 3 LH + 9 peers.** Done ‚Äî ¬ß8 updated (single-LH ‚Üí up to 3 lighthouses + 9 peers); `ca/sign.rs` `MAX_PEER_CAP` 8‚Üí12 + `peer_cap.rs` `PEER_CAP` 8‚Üí12; cap tests made cap-relative (over-cap reject/accept). Multi-lighthouse no longer out-of-scope (one CA on LH1; LH2/LH3 = relay/discovery/storage redundancy).
- [‚úì] **SETUP-1: `magic-setup` wizard skeleton. CODE DONE (2026-06-16); live-verify pending.** `mde-enroll` restructured into a lib (`mde_enroll`) + two bins (`mde-enroll` join shim, new `magic-setup`). `setup::Wizard` is a pure, unit-tested state machine: top menu (state-detected ‚Äî unconfigured‚ÜíCreate/Join, configured‚ÜíManage/Status), wrapping navigation, screen routing, verbose live-log pane. The ratatui shell renders the navigable menu + screens; runs headless over SSH. Tests: `unconfigured_node_offers_create_and_join`, `configured_node_offers_manage_and_status`, `menu_navigation_wraps_both_ways`, `activate_opens_the_selected_screen`, `quit_sets_should_quit_not_a_screen` (+ more). **Live-verify:** `magic-setup` renders + navigates over SSH on a node.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-2: Create-mesh path (found LH1). CODE DONE (2026-06-16).** Create screen: input mesh-id ‚Üí `found_argv` runs `mackesd found <id> --external-addr auto --role <role>` streaming to the log; BIRTHRIGHT-1 makes `found` provision LizardFS master+chunkserver+client + enable services itself, so the join lines print in the log. Role cycles with Tab. Test: `found_argv_shape`. **Live-verify:** found a fresh mesh from the wizard.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-3: Join path. CODE DONE (2026-06-16).** Join screen: paste token (+ Tab to pick role) ‚Üí `join_argv` runs `mackesd join <token> --role <role>` (fp-pinned enroll + role-aware QNM-Shared via BIRTHRIGHT-1), streamed. Test: `join_argv_carries_role_flag`. **Live-verify:** join a mesh from the wizard.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-4: Add-lighthouse (up to 3). CODE DONE (2026-06-16); live-verify pending.** New `mackesd add-peer --role lighthouse` mints a single-use **v3** token (the Manage screen's `l` key); the joining box runs `mackesd join ‚Ä¶ --role lighthouse`, which BIRTHRIGHT-1 provisions as chunkserver+client (a second/third lighthouse). The token pins the founder's `/enroll` endpoint fp + carries the mesh-id from the local bundle. **Live-verify:** add LH2 from the wizard; peers reach it.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-5: Manage peers. CODE DONE (2026-06-16); live-verify pending.** Status screen (role + `nebula`/`mackesd`/`mesh-health`/`qnm-shared` via `systemctl is-active`, `r` refresh) + Manage screen: list directory (`mackesd peers`), **`a` add peer** / **`l` add lighthouse** (`mackesd add-peer --role <r>` ‚Üí mints a v3 token into the log), **`d` remove peer** (type node-id ‚Üí `mackesd remove-peer <id>` = decommission + revoke certs + ban). New CLI: `add-peer` (reads mesh-id from the founding bundle + fp from `/etc/nebula/enroll-endpoint.crt`, mints a fresh bearer, prints the v3 token + join line) and `remove-peer` (composes `set_node_role` + lifecycle event + `ca::revoke::revoke_peer`). Tests: `endpoint_fingerprint_from_pem_matches_generated_identity`, `add_and_remove_peer_shapes`, `is_active_targets_the_unit`, `peers_shape`. **Live-verify:** add + remove a peer from the wizard end-to-end; `mackesd peers` reflects it.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-6: First-run unit + MOTD. CODE DONE (2026-06-16); live-verify pending.** `magic-setup.service` launches the wizard on **tty1 only** (`StandardInput=tty`, `Conflicts=getty@tty1`), gated `ConditionPathExists=!/var/lib/mde/role.toml` so it self-skips once configured + hands tty1 back to getty on exit ‚Äî never hijacks an SSH/pts session. `zz-mde-setup-motd.sh` prints `sudo magic-setup` on login while unconfigured. Enabled in post_install (self-gates). **Live-verify:** fresh node ‚Üí console shows the wizard; SSH session is unaffected; after configuring, getty owns tty1.
- [‚úì] **SETUP-7: Hybrid Ansible convergence. CODE DONE (2026-06-16); live-verify pending.** `site_yml::write_site_yml` emits `/etc/mackesd/site.yml` (a real playbook: role + mesh-id + lighthouse roster + QNM path + the boot-durable service set) at the end of `found`/`join`. Ships an `ansible/roles/mackes` role (idempotent: pin role.toml, enable+start the service set, fail-loud QNM-Shared mount assert) to `/usr/share/mackes/ansible/`. New `mackesd converge` verb re-applies it via `ansible-playbook -c local` (no-op with a hint when ansible/the playbook is absent). Tests: `render_is_valid_looking_playbook_with_the_facts`, `render_lists_the_full_service_set`, `write_site_yml_creates_parent_and_file`; YAML validated to parse. **Live-verify:** `mackesd converge` on a node with ansible installed restores role/services/mount idempotently.
- [‚úì] **GUI-RECONNECT: workbench bus resilience.** The cosmic GUIs should reconnect/degrade gracefully when mackesd/the bus restarts (today they show stale "mesh service isn't answering" until a manual refresh). Now mitigated by the shared file-bus (re-polls on refresh), but a reconnect-backoff + "reconnecting‚Ä¶" state would remove the manual refresh. **Acceptance:** after a `systemctl restart mackesd`, the workbench panels recover on their own poll tick.

> **Bus-root fix (2026-06-14, live):** the root mackesd daemon + uid-1000 desktop GUIs split per-HOME bus spools ‚Üí every workbench RPC timed out. Fixed: `mde_bus::default_data_dir()` honors `MDE_BUS_ROOT`; mackesd.service + environment.d set `MDE_BUS_ROOT=/run/mde-bus` (tmpfiles 1777); Persist relaxes the shared spool to cross-uid (0666/0777). Deployed live to all 4; `.13` workbench RPC durable. (Binaries live-deployed; RPM held per the new workflow.)

# Platform epics (from the 100-question survey, 2026-06-09)

> Full rationale + the per-question locks live in `docs/design/platform-survey-answers.md`.
> 51 tasks across 6 epics. Each is `[ ]` Open; acceptance is runtime-observable per ¬ß7.
> The RPM is held until every feature is ¬ß7-complete; releasing is operator-gated (`/release`).

## FLEET-PHASE-G ‚Äî the no-fixed-center fleet control plane (resolves C1)

Architecture: one unified `BaselineSpec` (YAML, monotonic `u64` version) written to LizardFS, which
is both transport (replication) and the authoritative log; leaderless authoring, last-writer-wins,
host-local Ansible apply.

- [‚úì] **FPG-1: unify the revision model** ‚Äî done ‚Äî BaselineSpec gains the Q9 settings domain (JSON-encoded values, mackesd-applied, playbook-skipped); canonical id = magic_fleet::Revision::version (u64); mackesd's r-date scheme + rowids documented display-only; one `BaselineSpec` (OS state + folded-in settings, Q9), YAML wire format (Q2), `u64` version id (Q1); retire the rowid + date-string schemes to display fields.
- [‚úì] **FPG-2: LizardFS revision log + store** ‚Äî done ‚Äî magic_fleet::store: <root>/fleet/revisions/<v:020>.yaml append-only log, atomic writes, tolerant reads, next_version + elect_head; mackesd watch wiring lands with FPG-4; revisions written to LizardFS as the authoritative append-only log (Q3/Q8); replication is the transport; `mackesd` watches the path.
- [‚úì] **FPG-3: leaderless election** ‚Äî done ‚Äî any node serves + mints (FleetService on every responder); append-only writes + version‚Üíat‚Üíauthor total order settle races; leader lease untouched (guards only SQLite mirror writes); any node mints+gossips; highest `version` wins (Q4/Q5); the leader lock only guards the local SQLite mirror write.
- [‚úì] **FPG-4: the Bus verbs** ‚Äî done ‚Äî push/list/diff/rollback real against the LizardFS log (C1 stub closed): rollback mints higher version (Q6), flat domain diff (Q7), list tagged with elected head (Q16); home probe reads the new wire; implement `push`/`list`/`diff`/`rollback` (replace the `ipc/fleet.rs` stubs): rollback = mint a higher-version copy (Q6), flat top-level diff (Q7), `list` returns the full held set tagged with the winner (Q16).
- [‚úì] **FPG-5: apply-ack + signals** ‚Äî done ‚Äî acks at <root>/fleet/acks/<v>/<host>.json (own-file authority); responder emits event/fleet/signals per new (version,peer,status) with restart-replay guard; list-revisions carries ack summaries (the Workbench reads them via the verb); nodes gossip an apply-ack advancing the author's FSM to Verified (Q14); emit `event/fleet/signals` {revision_id, peer, status} + a Workbench subscription (Q15).
- [‚úì] **FPG-6: cold-node convergence** ‚Äî done by construction ‚Äî `magic-fleet reconcile` elects the head of whatever subset replication has delivered and applies it immediately; history back-fill IS LizardFS replication (no extra machinery); append-only log makes partial views safe; a joining/partitioned node applies the newest revision immediately, back-fills history lazily (Q18).
- [‚úì] **FPG-7: LizardFS mount ownership** ‚Äî done ‚Äî goal-2 default peer-capped (Q12, supersedes the old goal=N Q4 lock); five XDG dirs bind-mounted from the mesh volume, ~/Local/ never (Q13, mountpoint-idempotent, degrades unprivileged); master already lighthouse-pinned via the role-marker VIP gate (Q11); bind-mount the five XDG dirs (never `~/Local/`, Q13), default goal 2 (Q12), master pinned to Lighthouse nodes (Q11).
- [‚úì] **FPG-8: host-local Ansible apply** ‚Äî done ‚Äî `magic-fleet reconcile`: elects the log head, converges host-local (Q10, no push-SSH), writes the apply-ack (Q14); author advisory, auth = the Nebula-carried volume (Q17); settings domain skipped (mackesd-applied); `magic-fleet` reconciles the unified baseline host-local (Q10); revision auth rests on the Nebula transport, `author` advisory (Q17).

## SECURITY ‚Äî CA lifecycle, enrollment, KDC (resolves H8)

- [‚úì] **SEC-1: non-expiring peer certs** ‚Äî done ‚Äî the backend never passed -duration (nebula already signs to CA lifetime); the fictional 365-day bookkeeping expiry is gone: cert_lifetime_days removed through sign/enroll/watcher/epoch/CLI, expires_at=0 is the epoch-lifetime sentinel; turnover = rotation (bump_epoch) / revocation (ENT-3). Display polish ('epoch-lifetime' label for 0) rides the PLANES Registration panel ‚Äî drop mid-epoch expiry; turnover via rotation/revocation (Q19).
- [‚úì] **SEC-2: passphrase-gated CA rotation** ‚Äî done ‚Äî rotation_gate (SHA-256 hash on the replicated root, fail-closed when unset); BOTH doors gated: `ca rotate` (env/--passphrase-stdin) + the regen-certs Bus verb ({passphrase} body); `ca set-passphrase` with current-phrase requirement to change; promotion verified mint-only; all three states smoked live + Bus gate test ‚Äî `mackesd ca rotate` requires an operator passphrase, never auto-on-promotion (Q20).
- [‚úì] **SEC-3: QR/file 256-bit enrollment token** ‚Äî done ‚Äî enrollment runs exclusively on ENT-1's 256-bit single-use bearers delivered as the wire token (QR-bounded TOKEN_MAX_LEN); a typed 16-char code can never pass the ledger gate; auto-sign/TOFU kept (csr_watcher signs issued bearers); passcode.rs doc-retired to LAN-credential uses only ‚Äî replace the typed 16-char passcode with a delivered 256-bit token; keep auto-sign/TOFU (Q21/22).
- [‚úì] **SEC-4: outbound first-pair flow** ‚Äî done ‚Äî first_pair orchestrates the existing pieces: unpinned TOFU dial ‚Üí capture the fingerprint the device ACTUALLY presents ‚Üí session key sealed (SEC-8's hook now production-called) ‚Üí DeviceRecord written with the captured pin; re-TOFU of a pinned device refused (unpair first); RSA-4096 identity kept (Q23); `action/connect/pair-device {id,name,addr}` triggers it; loopback-TLS test pins presented-fingerprint capture ‚Äî an operator-initiated KDC pairing flow that completes the handshake and writes the fingerprint pin (Q24/25); keep RSA-4096 (Q23).
- [‚úì] **SEC-5: KDC2-4 mesh-shunt worker** ‚Äî done ‚Äî mesh_shunt: each peer publishes its paired phones to <root>/kdc-phones/<host>.json (own-row); run_host's tick collects neighbors' files ‚Üí SyntheticAnnounce ‚Üí inject_synthetic (accept-any-relayer, Q26/27; cert-pin is the trust gate) ‚Üí take_fresh drained into the roster the workbench reads; stale/self/junk dropped. CONSUMES the H8 dead seam. ‚Äî consume `SyntheticAnnounce`/`inject_synthetic`, relay neighbors' `phones.json` mesh-wide; accept any relayer (Q26/27). *(resolves H8; SVC-6.)*
- [‚úì] **SEC-6: gossiped signed revocations** ‚Äî done ‚Äî retract records now carry ed25519 signatures over the canonical (node_id + sorted fingerprints) payload, signed by the new persisted node key (load_or_create, 0600, corrupt-seed refused); readers verify-if-present: tampered records DROP from the union (test-pinned), unsigned legacy accepted with a warn (migration stance ‚Äî tighten when all writers sign); revoke + leave both sign ‚Äî a signed retract record gossips peer-to-peer (like fleet revisions) alongside the per-node ban files (Q28/29).
- [‚úì] **SEC-7: mandatory CA backup on lighthouse** ‚Äî done ‚Äî a CA-holding box with MDE_BACKUP_PASSPHRASE unset now ERRORs every tick + drops a crit alert (one/day, deduped) into the alert_relay pipeline ‚Üí desktop notification; peer boxes stay quiet; the combined CA+topology bundle already shipped (GF-9.1 state-backup.enc, gluster-era doc relabeled). Chose loud-warn over refuse-start: availability over liveness-coupling, the alert makes it unmissable ‚Äî refuse-start / loud-warn without `MDE_BACKUP_PASSPHRASE`; one combined CA+topology bundle (Q31/32).
- [‚úì] **SEC-8: encrypt KDC session keys at rest** ‚Äî done ‚Äî session_persist: AES-256-GCM-sealed device‚Üíkey map (Q33) under a 0600 master (corrupt-master refuses); PairingStore::open restores sessions across restart (Q34), install_and_persist_session is the SEC-4 handshake's completion hook; fails closed to empty on wrong-master/tamper; plaintext-never-on-disk pinned by test ‚Äî persist session keys encrypted so links survive a daemon restart (Q34); keep AES-256-GCM (Q33).

## TEST-OBS ‚Äî testing/CI + observability (resolves E1)

- [‚úì] **OBS-1: retarget integration tests to Nebula** ‚Äî BED STOOD UP: install-helpers/provision-mesh-vm.sh provisions Fedora-42 VMs (KVM, cloud-init, nebula 1.9.7 preinstalled) ‚Äî validated end-to-end (boot‚Üíssh‚Üínebula-cert). ENT-3's fingerprint parser now regression-pinned against REAL nebula-cert -json (blocklist test). **BED ADVANCED 2026-06-10:** 3 F42 VMs running (mesh-lh/mesh-a/mesh-pine); host-F44 debug binaries (mackesd/meshctl) run on the F42 VMs (no glibc break); the **founding lighthouse is live** ‚Äî `mackesd mesh-init` minted the CA (mesh `bed-mesh`) + issued a join token (see [[vm-bed-state]]). **CROSS-NODE ENROLL VALIDATED LIVE 2026-06-11:** the full clean auto-enrollment ran end-to-end on a 2-node DigitalOcean F43 cloud pair over an NFS-shared QNM-Shared ‚Äî A `mesh-init`‚Üí`enroll-token`, B `role-pin`+`enroll` (no workarounds), A's serve auto-signer signs hands-off, B's nebula_supervisor materializes /etc/nebula, **bidirectional overlay ping 0% loss 1‚Äì2 ms**, both peers online/healthy. Required fixing 5 enrollment bugs (#5 token-mesh c30662e, #6 lighthouse-addr d9f0429+198617a, #7 scratch cert 7a5dfac, #8 cert upsert ba9fcde, #9 mesh-init idempotency 628b799) ‚Äî see [[vm-bed-state]]. **DONE 2026-06-11 ‚Äî `integration_testcontainers.rs` retargeted off the retired Headscale/Tailscale substrate to a real Nebula overlay E2E.** `nebula_two_node_overlay_reachability` builds a nebula node image (`install-helpers/nebula-test-node.Containerfile`: Fedora + nebula + iproute/iputils; the fresh mackesd binary bind-mounted) and drives the genuine v2.5 lifecycle across two privileged containers on a shared QNM-Shared + podman network: lighthouse `mesh-init`‚Üí`serve`‚Üí`nebula`, peer `role-pin`‚Üí`enroll --token`‚Üí`serve`‚Üí`nebula`, then asserts **bidirectional `10.42.0.0/17` overlay ping** (passes in ~80 s; 0% loss both ways). Uses `sudo podman` directly (rootless userns can't open `/dev/net/tun`; testcontainers' root-socket dance is flaky) ‚Äî the `testcontainers` dep is dropped, `docker-tests = []`. Self-skips green when root podman + tun aren't available. **Found + fixed bug #10 doing this:** `mesh-init` resolved its node-id by shelling ONLY `hostname` (‚Üí "founder") while `serve` uses `default_node_id()` (MACKESD_NODE_ID‚ÜíHOSTNAME‚Üíhostname) ‚Äî so the founding lighthouse self-signed under one id but serve looked under another and the overlay never came up. The two host-side tests (leader-election under contention, passcode rejection) are retained. *(resolves E1.)*
- [‚úì] **OBS-2: multi-process convergence harness** ‚Äî done ‚Äî multiprocess_convergence.rs: N real threads racing one shared replicated root flip the FPG control-plane acceptances live ‚Äî leaderless minters converge on one head (FPG-3), concurrent acks all land + union (FPG-5), cold node converges to the existing head (FPG-6), append-only survives the write race (FPG-2). The Nebula data-plane drop (revoked tunnels) stays on the VM bed ‚Äî N real `mackesd` binaries over one QNM root assert newest-wins + single leader (Q91).

- [‚úì] **OBS-9: mde-kdc-host RSA-4096 keygen tests appeared to hang the workspace gate** ‚Äî ROOT-CAUSED + FIXED 2026-06-11. `keygen::generate_pkcs8` (RSA-4096, the locked Q23 identity) runs through the pure-Rust `rsa` + `num-bigint-dig` crates; **unoptimized in a debug build, a single keygen takes minutes**, so `keygen::tests::generate_pkcs8_returns_loadable_keypair` and `first_pair::tests::first_pair_captures_‚Ä¶` (which keygens in `spawn_device`) blew past any reasonable timeout and stalled `cargo test --workspace`. NOT a deadlock ‚Äî the same keygen test passes in **3.84 s** under the release profile. Fix: `[profile.dev.package.rsa]` + `[profile.dev.package.num-bigint-dig]` `opt-level = 3` in the root `Cargo.toml` ‚Äî debug keygen drops from >120 s to ~4 s, RSA-4096 unchanged, rest of the workspace still compiles fast. (A misdiagnosed `#[ignore]` was added then removed.)

## PEERS ‚Äî Directory of Mesh Peers, the platform Front Door (design: `docs/design/peer-directory.md`, 2026-06-09)

> 26-Q survey + 3 operator directives **+ 25-Q level-2 survey (L1‚ÄìL25)**. The Peers directory
> is the **Front Door**: Workbench lands on it; it shows everything the running mesh offers
> (peers, services: remote access / Podman / KVM / media / voice) + an advanced health/design
> view (presence, sync, drift, Netdata health, live path map ‚Üí wallpaper). Evolves
> `mesh_topology`; retires the CR-6.c modal.
> **Sequencing (L25):** PD-1/2 ‚Üí PD-3/4/5 (+11/12/13) ‚Üí PD-6/7 ‚Üí PD-8/9 ‚Üí PD-10; layer-shell
> spike runs early in parallel. Every slice independently shippable + ¬ß7-complete.

- [‚úì] **PD-1: PEERS ‚Äî the `action/mesh/directory` Bus verb + `mackesd peers` CLI** ‚Äî done ‚Äî DirectoryService joins PeerRecords + presence tiers (Q11) + roster ip/role + FPG revision currency (Q15); responder + table/--json CLI (L24) smoked end-to-end; voice/descriptors join at PD-2 (honest absence)
  **As** any directory consumer (GUI or CLI),
  **I want** one mackesd Bus verb returning the joined per-peer record (hostname, overlay IP, role, machine-presence tier, voice presence, mde_version, revision currency, drift count + last event, Netdata-derived health, service descriptors),
  **so that** every surface reads the same answer with zero GUI shell-outs (Q9/Q23).
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] `mde-bus call action/mesh/directory` returns all known peers incl. self, with every field above
    - [‚úì] `mackesd peers` prints the same record set as an aligned table; `--json` emits raw records (L24)
    - [‚úì] presence tiers derive from `last_seen_ms` (Online ‚â§2 min, Idle ‚â§10 min, Offline) (Q11)
- [‚úì] **PD-2: PEERS ‚Äî peer-published service descriptors (remote access + Podman + KVM + media)** ‚Äî done ‚Äî descriptors.rs probes localhost-only (ssh/rdp/vnc listeners, podman ps json, virsh list/dominfo/domifaddr, pinned media ports, Netdata alarms‚Üí3-tier health) and rides the heartbeat record write; directory passes them through
  **As** a peer's mackesd,
  **I want** to locally probe sshd/xrdp/vnc listeners, Podman containers (name+image+state+published ports, L10), libvirt guests (name+state+vCPU/mem+qemu-agent IPs, L11), media services via a localhost port-scan of a pinned list (Jellyfin 8096, Navidrome/Airsonic 4533, MPD 6600, DLNA, mde-musicd ‚Äî L12), and my Netdata alarm summary (3-tier: healthy/degraded/critical, worst alarm named, L15), publishing the result on the ~30 s presence heartbeat (L13) into my replicated PeerRecord/PeerProbe,
  **so that** the directory knows what every peer offers without any remote probing (Q19/Q26c/D1).
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] starting/stopping sshd (or a container/VM) on a peer changes its descriptor set within one heartbeat cycle
    - [‚úì] a WARNING alarm flips health to degraded; a CRITICAL to critical, with the alarm named (L15)
    - [‚úì] the port-scan touches localhost only; the scan list is a pinned constant, never user input
    - [‚úì] no network probe leaves the publishing host
- [‚úì] **PD-3: PEERS ‚Äî the master-detail Peers panel** ‚Äî CORE LANDED (peers.rs: master-detail over the directory verb, self/online/idle/offline groups, L2 filter by host/service, L3 guided empty states, Services Provided pane, nav 'Peers' + 'Mesh Map'); **TAG CHIPS LANDED 2026-06-11 (L1):** the directory verb now joins each peer's capability tags from the replicated tag manifest (`cap_tags::read_tags`, honest empty when absent); the panel parses `tags` into `PeerRow`, renders them as chips in the detail header (reuses the `badge` helper), and folds them into the filter (now host/**tag**/service, case-insensitive) ‚Äî directory + parse + filter all unit-tested. **30s AUTO-REFRESH LANDED 2026-06-11 (Q10 poll half):** a view-gated 30s tick (`directory_subscription` ‚Üí `PollTick` ‚Üí `load()`) registered alongside the 2s metrics tick; the reload preserves the operator's filter + selection (unit-pinned). **Q10 BUS-PUSH LANDED 2026-06-11 (`8cbaace`):** the directory responder runs a ~3s change-detect (digest of presence/health/currency/tags; heartbeat bumps ignored) that publishes `event/mesh/directory`; the panel subscribes (`directory_event_subscription`) and reloads on push, the 30s poll kept as a backstop ‚Äî both halves tested. **DEVICES GROUP LANDED 2026-06-11 (L6):** the paired KDE-Connect roster (`action/connect/devices`, fetched in a batch alongside the directory in `load()` so it refreshes on the same poll + Bus-push) renders as its own "Devices" group below the peers ‚Äî presence pip + battery in the row, filtered by the same box; selecting a device shows a device card (peer/device selection mutually exclusive) with Ring + Send-file (the live Connect verbs ‚Äî Ring ‚Üí `action/connect/ring`, Send-file ‚Üí a system file-picker then `action/connect/share`, a new daemon verb building a `kdeconnect.share.request` via the existing share-plugin packet builders) and an "Open in Connect hub" jump to the Connected Devices panel; parse/select/stale-drop all unit-tested, the new `share` verb unit-tested daemon-side. **PD-3 COMPLETE.**
  **As** an operator,
  **I want** the topology panel reborn as "Peers": list left (self pinned "(this machine)" ‚Üí Online ‚Üí Offline grayed ‚Üí Devices group from `action/connect/devices`) with hostname + colored tag chips (L1) and a type-to-filter box matching hostname/tag/service (L2); detail pane right (identity header + role badge, two presence fields, version + sync currency, drift count + last event ‚Üí pre-filtered Drift panel link, Services Provided section, inline result strip); Bus-subscription refresh + 30 s poll floor; guided empty states when the mesh isn't fully running (unenrolled ‚Üí "Join a mesh", mackesd down ‚Üí one-click "Start the mesh service", no peers ‚Üí "Invite a peer", L3); device rows carry presence+battery, Ring, Send-file, and a jump to the KDC hub card (L6),
  **so that** the whole fleet and everything it offers is one surface (Q1‚Äì7, Q10‚Äì12, Q15, Q20‚Äì22, D1, L1‚ÄìL3, L6).
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] every known peer renders in the correct group; offline peers show ops disabled
    - [‚úì] Podman containers, KVM guests (with state/specs/IPs), and media services list per peer
    - [‚úì] typing in the filter narrows by hostname, tag, or offered service
    - [‚úì] each degraded mesh state shows its guided CTA and the CTA works
    - [‚úì] the CR-6.c graph modal is deleted; graph-node click selects the peer in the directory

- [‚úì] **PD-6: PEERS ‚Äî transport path probe** ‚Äî done ‚Äî transport_probe times a TCP handshake through the overlay tunnel (refused=measured, timeout=unreachable); mesh_latency's ICMP shell-out deleted (ENT-13 CLOSED). Direct-vs-relay + endpoint now classified via NET-INTROSPECT (Nebula loopback debug-SSH `list-hostmap -json`, 2026-06-13); NAT-class is the one field OSS Nebula still can't expose
  **As** the directory and the live map,

  **so that** one probe feeds the RTT figure, the trace card, and the map edges (Q13/Q14, ENT-13).

Honest "overlay" only while handshaking or if the debug SSH is unavailable. (NAT-class is the one field OSS Nebula still doesn't expose.)
    - [‚úì] `mesh_latency` no longer shells ICMP `ping` (ENT-13 closes here)

Direct/relay + endpoint are classified via NET-INTROSPECT (Nebula loopback debug-SSH, 2026-06-13) and rendered in the trace card; only NAT-class remains unexposed by OSS Nebula (surfaced honestly, never guessed). **FLOW PARTICLES LANDED 2026-06-11 (L18/L22):** accent dots ride each self‚Üípeer edge with density+speed scaled by that peer's real overlay throughput (Netdata `system.net`, sampled every 3s, normalized to ~100 Mbit/s); the ~90ms animation loop is registered ONLY when real traffic flows (`has_flow` gate), so an idle mesh runs no animation (idle CPU ‚Äî the L22 budget); the flow-data + trace ticks are both view-gated to the open Map. Edge-hit/segment-distance + trace open/sample/stale-drop + traceroute routing + flow-anim/has_flow-gate all unit-tested. **PD-7 COMPLETE** (direct-vs-relay now real via NET-INTROSPECT 2026-06-13; only NAT-class stays unexposed by OSS Nebula).
  **As** an operator,

  **so that** the health and design of the mesh is visible at a glance (Q13/Q14/Q24/Q26b, L17‚ÄìL20).

    - [‚úì] the canvas honors the adaptive render budget (L22) ‚Äî the particle-animation loop is registered only while real traffic flows, so an idle mesh runs no animation (idle CPU)

- [‚úì] **PD-12: PEERS ‚Äî Wake-on-LAN for offline peers** ‚Äî done ‚Äî peers publish their physical LAN MACs in descriptors (own-row authority beats ARP guessing); action/mesh/wake validates + broadcasts the magic packet from this box; Wake renders only on offline peers with a published MAC. - [‚úì] **PD-13: PEERS ‚Äî presence-transition alerts** ‚Äî done ‚Äî presence_watch worker (rank 0, census 20): 30s sweeps diff Q11 tiers, offline-boundary crossings write alert JSON into the alert_relay pipeline (warn on drop, info on return); restart-seeded silently; idle flaps quiet
  **As** a user anywhere on the desktop,
