## WORKLOAD-FLEET ‚Äî fleet-wide workload visibility (operator-reported live 2026-06-18)
> Operator: "Host Fedora has a KVM VM running. Is this correct? If so, it should be visible in all panels showing workloads." **Diagnosis:** `MDE-KVM-1` is the authorized on-host test VM ([[test-infra-authorization]]); the **data plane already works** ‚Äî the `compute_registry` worker discovers it via `virsh` and publishes `compute/inventory/<peer>` every 10s (live: `compute/inventory/10.42.0.3` carries `MDE-KVM-1` running, 2 GB, meshfs_available). The **gap is the display side**: every "workloads" surface enumerates LOCAL `virsh`/`podman` only and never reads the bus inventory, so a VM on node A is invisible from node B even though its descriptor is on the bus.
- [‚úì] **WORKLOAD-FLEET-1: workbench Instances panel must show fleet-wide workloads, not just local.** DONE 2026-06-18 ‚Äî cross-node data path **verified end-to-end**. Transport is **QNM-Shared**, not the bus (there is NO bus-federation worker ‚Äî `compute/inventory/<peer>` is per-node only; reading the local bus would only ever show self ‚Äî the audit-gap trap). `compute_registry` now mirrors its inventory to `<QNM-Shared>/<host>/compute-inventory.json` each tick (atomic, only when the mount is real); the compute panel keeps the live local probe AND folds every peer's file, attributed to that host (friendly `display_host()` strips the nebula `peer:` prefix), self-skipped by overlay-IP (fallback hostname), dedup by node+kind+name. New "Node" column; lifecycle/sampling/bulk gated to local rows (peer rows read-only). Pure fold + write round-trip + display_host unit-tested (32 + 33 green). **Live-verified:** new mackesd on the dev host wrote `/mnt/mesh-storage/peer:fedora/compute-inventory.json` (`MDE-KVM-1` running) ‚Üí LizardFS replicated it to .13 (confirmed visible) ‚Üí .13's GUI session resolves `MDE_WORKGROUP_ROOT=/mnt/mesh-storage` (systemd user env) ‚Üí display_host ‚Üí `fedora`. New mde-workbench deployed to .13 + dev host. **Remaining for full fleet (next RPM cut, not a blocker):** roll the new mackesd writer to all nodes so every node publishes its own workloads (only the dev host writes so far).
  **As** an operator, **I want** the Workbench ‚ñ∏ Provisioning ‚ñ∏ Instances panel to list every node's VMs + containers (mine and peers'), **so that** a VM running on any mesh host is visible from any workbench.
  **Acceptance** (each runtime-observable):
    - [‚úì] the panel tails `compute/inventory/<peer>` (latest per peer) in addition to its local `virsh`/`podman` probe, and renders one row per VM/container tagged with its **node** (hostname/overlay-ip), state, cpu/ram, meshfs flag
    - [‚úì] with `MDE-KVM-1` running on the dev host, opening the Instances panel **on .13** (a different node) shows `MDE-KVM-1` attributed to host `fedora`
    - [‚úì] local rows still resolve live (the local probe is not regressed); peer rows refresh as new inventory records land
    - [‚úì] no raw hex / scattered metrics outside `mde-theme` (¬ß4); unit-tested aggregation (merge local probe + peer inventory, newest-per-peer, dedup by uuid)
- [‚úì] **WORKLOAD-FLEET-2: apps-applet Workloads tab is LOCAL-ONLY ‚Äî wire it to the fleet inventory.** CONFIRMED 2026-06-18: the apps aggregator (`mackesd::ipc::apps::read_local_inventory`) reads only `compute/inventory/<this-node>` off the local bus, so the Start-menu Workloads tab shows local workloads only ‚Äî APPS-6's "local + peer descriptors" acceptance was never true (audit-gap; APPS-6 re-cued below).
  **As** an operator, **I want** the Start-menu Workloads tab to show the same fleet-wide list as the Workbench Instances panel, **so that** "all panels showing workloads" is truthful.
  **Acceptance** (each runtime-observable):
    - [‚úì] the aggregator folds every peer's `<QNM-Shared>/<host>/compute-inventory.json` (the WORKLOAD-FLEET-1 files), attributed to each host, self-skipped + deduped (reuse the same pattern)
    - [‚úì] each workload entry carries its node; `MDE-KVM-1` appears in the Workloads tab from a second node, attributed to `fedora`
    - [‚úì] start/stop/attach stay gated to local workloads (remote ops are a later slice); unit-tested fleet fold in `ipc::apps`

## NOTIFY-UI ‚Äî Alert Center / applet polish (operator-reported live 2026-06-16)
- [‚úì] **NOTIFY-UI-1: Hub header cramped at the top.** Title "Notification Hub ¬∑ N unread" collided with the Mark-all-read/Clear-all/‚úï buttons (~390px panel). Restructured: title + ‚úï on the top line, the bulk actions on their own line below; added 14/16px padding + spacing so nothing jams the edge.
- [‚úì] **NOTIFY-UI-2: applet bell renders black/invisible on the dark panel.** The bell was a color-emoji (üîî) that ignores the Carbon `Text::Color` tint ‚Üí black on the Gray-100 panel (only the tinted ‚óè dot showed). Fixed with U+FE0E (text/monochrome presentation) so the glyph honors the severity tint + is visible.
- [‚úì] **NOTIFY-UI-4: the Action Center "wouldn't open" ‚Äî its startup read of the QNM-Shared (FUSE) dir hung the iced update loop on a wedged mount.** Operator (.13, 2026-06-17): the notification area does not open; "continues when I attempt to open it." **Diagnosed live:** the running `mde-notify-center` (pid 13479) sat in the kernel `request_wait_answer` (a **FUSE** wait) with the loaded RSS but no mapped surface ‚Äî `boot_task()` batches the layer-surface creation with the first `Message::Refresh`, whose handler called `AlertTail::poll_shared()` **inline on the update loop**; that reads `/mnt/mesh-storage/.mesh-alerts/` over LizardFS, and a wedged mount / lost-chunk-backed file blocks uninterruptibly ‚Üí the loop never pumps the compositor roundtrip ‚Üí the surface never maps. The applet bell (`pgrep`‚Üí`pkill`-or-spawn toggle) then just kills/respawns an instance that re-hangs at the same point, so it reads as "won't open." Same class as SHELL-RPC-1 (wedged FUSE read on the lost leader-lock chunk). **Fix:** split the read into a pure, state-free `mde_notify::read_shared_alert_items()` (safe on a helper thread) + `AlertTail::dedup_fresh()` (the `&mut self` dedup, on the caller). The center now runs the shared read on a helper thread and picks the result up **non-blockingly** via a `mpsc::Receiver` stored on `Center` ‚Äî at most one read is ever in flight, the UI loop never blocks, the layer surface maps immediately regardless of mount health, and a recovered mount is picked up on a later poll. Tests: `read_shared_alert_items_is_pure_and_dedup_is_separate` (+ the existing `shared_alert_roundtrip_and_dedup` still green through the refactor). **Acceptance:** the Action Center opens on the bell within a poll cycle even when QNM-Shared is wedged; no `request_wait_answer`-hung center. *(deploy = build + roll the GUI binary to the Workstation nodes.)*
- [‚úì] **NOTIFY-UI-3 / ICON-MESH: use the Networks icon for ALL Mesh File Services representations.** The desktop XDG folders (Documents/Downloads/‚Ä¶ ‚Äî bind-mounts of QNM-Shared) render with a local mounted-volume icon; they're mesh file services and should show a network icon. **Scope:** desktop folder icons (gio `metadata::custom-icon-name`/`folder-remote` set by the meshfs bind worker for the desktop user), mde-files mesh-storage representation, and the Workbench Mesh Storage panel. **Acceptance:** every mesh-file-service surface shows the network icon, not a local-volume icon. *(needs live desktop-icon iteration ‚Äî cosmic-files icon-source behavior to confirm; not yet built.)*

## XCP-PROVISION-AUDIT ‚Äî findings from spinning up 4 MDE-VMs + installing the platform (goal 2026-06-16)
Live audit of the clone‚Üíboot‚Üíinstall‚Üíenroll flow on the XCP host; each becomes an XCP-epic acceptance hardening item.

> **GOAL VERIFIED on BOTH back-ends (2026-06-17):** the "install + join with zero manual steps" capability is now proven on **local KVM** (`MDE-VM-KVM1`, overlay `10.42.0.10`) as well as XCP (VM-5). Flow on the fresh KVM clone: reset identity (hostname `MDE-VM-KVM1` + machine-id) ‚Üí `dnf install magic-mesh-10.0.10.rpm` (auto-pulled `fuse-libs` per XPA-9; the **SELINUX-1 `%post` auto-loaded all 3 magicmesh CIL modules**, node Enforcing) ‚Üí `mackesd add-peer` token on LH-01 ‚Üí `mackesd join --role server` self-provisioned QNM-Shared from the bundled offline fc43 lizardfs RPMs, mounted `/mnt/mesh-storage`, and brought up nebula+mackesd+mesh-health ‚Äî **no manual fuse/mount steps**. Result: a 10-node mesh, `MDE-VM-KVM1.json` in the directory, overlay ping to LH-01 OK. The remaining XPA items (1/5/6/7/13) are provisioner-*automation* (the unbuilt XCP-1..7 epic), not blockers to a working install+join.
- [‚úì] **XPA-1: default VM memory (4 GB) overcommits a typical host.** A 15.9 GB host couldn't start 4√ó4 GB VMs + the base. Right-size headless Server VMs to **2 GB** by default in the provisioner (XCP-3), and pre-check host free memory before fan-out (fail early with a clear message, not "no suitable hosts").
- [~] **XPA-2 (scripted: build-mde-vm-golden.sh templatizes the golden): clone-from-snapshot needs the snapshot UUID (snapshots aren't in `xe vm-list`).** The golden must be a real **template** (`xe template-list`) per XCP-2, and the provisioner resolves it by template name ‚Üí uuid; don't clone a name via vm-list.
- [~] **XPA-3 (scripted: build-mde-vm-golden.sh generalizes ‚Äî cloud-init clean + strip machine-id/host keys; pending golden run + clone-verify): cloud-init does NOT re-run on a cloned *booted* image ‚Üí identity not reset.** All 4 clones kept the base's hostname (`f44-test`), machine-id, and SSH host keys despite a fresh NoCloud seed (new instance-id). The golden MUST be generalized before cloning (`cloud-init clean --logs --seed`, truncate `/etc/machine-id`, remove `/etc/ssh/ssh_host_*`) so each clone regenerates identity on first boot ‚Äî OR the provisioner does an explicit post-clone identity reset (hostname + `systemd-machine-id-setup` + `ssh-keygen -A`). Build this into XCP-2 (golden) + XCP-3 (spawn).
- [~] **XPA-4 (in the clone recipe + provisioner TODO): clone copies the VIF MAC ‚Üí collisions.** The provisioner must reset each clone's VIF (new MAC) ‚Äî fold into XCP-3.
- [!] **XPA-5: enroll-token endpoint is the OVERLAY IP ‚Äî VERIFIED + SUBSUMED BY [[XPA-7]] (2026-06-22).** `mackesd enroll-token` mints `mesh:‚Ä¶@10.42.0.2:4242#‚Ä¶` (the Nebula **overlay** IP), which a not-yet-enrolled LAN/internet node can't reach. The join token for an external node must carry a **publicly/LAN-reachable** enroll endpoint (the relay's public IP / the v3 `/enroll` HTTPS on :443). Confirm + fix the token-minting endpoint selection.
  - *Located + triaged (2026-06-22):* the overlay-IP mint is the **legacy v1** path ‚Äî `mesh_init.rs:138` (`format!("mesh:{mesh_id}@{}:4242#{bearer}", signed.overlay_ip)`, the `found` first-peer token) and the `enroll-token` command share this `mesh:<id>@<ip>:4242#<bearer>` shape (`parse_join_token` requires an IPv4 host + port). `mesh_init` even *receives* a reachable `external_addr` (cmd_found passes `"<public-ip>:4242"`) and uses it for `LighthouseEntry.external_addr` but **not** for the token. **This is NOT an independent fix.** XPA-7 already documents the same defect ("`enroll-token` advertises the overlay IP (unreachable by a fresh node)") and locks the resolution: the **v3 `add-peer` flow** is "the only flow that works for an external node" ‚Äî it pins the public `/enroll` endpoint (`:4243`) **+ cert fp**, neither of which a host-swapped v1 token carries. Band-aiding the deprecated v1 minter (overlay‚Üíexternal host, still `:4242`, no fp) would ship a token that still can't enroll. **Correct resolution:** the founding/provisioning flows emit a **v3** token via add-peer (XPA-7) ‚Äî `enroll`/`enroll-token` are deprecated (ENT-1). Marked `[!]` (blocked-as-subsumed): close when XPA-7's add-peer path is the founding/XCP-3 default; no separate XPA-5 code change.
- [‚úì] **XPA-6: the monolithic RPM bundles all GUI binaries (~100 MB) ‚Äî a headless Server install carries surfaces it never runs.** The full `cargo build --workspace --release` (libcosmic GUIs: workbench/music/voice-hud/applet) gates every install + a 100 MB+ transfer per node. Consider a `magic-mesh-server` subpackage (daemon + nebula + lizardfs-client, no GUI bins) for headless roles, or split GUI assets behind the role so a Server pulls only what it runs.

### XCP-PROVISION-AUDIT (cont.) ‚Äî enroll + first-boot-server findings (live, MDE-VM-1 brought to full membership)
- [‚úì] **XPA-7: use `mackesd add-peer` (v3) + `mackesd join`; NOT `enroll`/`enroll-token` (ENT-1).** `enroll` publishes a CSR to QNM-Shared + waits for a sign (needs the mount pre-existing ‚Äî the MESH-1 chicken-and-egg) and `enroll-token` advertises the **overlay** IP (unreachable by a fresh node). `add-peer` mints a v3 token pinning the public `/enroll` endpoint (`:4243`) + cert fp ‚Äî the only flow that works for an external node. Also: the `:443` covert path presents a DIFFERENT cert than `:4243` ‚Üí `--enroll-port 443` fails `enroll-fingerprint-mismatch`; don't advertise :443 for enroll. **Provisioner (XCP-3) must use add-peer + join.**
- [‚úì] **XPA-8 (CRITICAL ‚Äî FIXED + VERIFIED on a clean VM-5): mackesd is hostage to `qnm-shared.service`.** `mackesd.service After=qnm-shared.service` + the qnm-shared mount-retry loop stuck "activating" ‚Üí mackesd's start job **queues forever** (never runs, no journal, looks "inactive"). On a fresh node where the mount can't complete, the platform never starts. Make mackesd start **independently** of the mount (it already self-heals via `meshfs_worker`/BOOT-REC) ‚Äî drop the hard `After=` to a `Wants=`/timeout, or give qnm-shared a bounded fail so it doesn't pin the queue.
- [‚úì] **XPA-9 (CRITICAL ‚Äî FIXED + VERIFIED: dnf auto-pulled fuse-libs on VM-5): the bundled fc43 lizardfs-client needs FUSE 2 (`libfuse.so.2`), absent on fresh F44.** `mfsmount: error while loading shared libraries: libfuse.so.2` ‚Üí the QNM-Shared mount can NEVER succeed on a fresh Workstation/Server. The platform RPM must `Requires: fuse-libs` (+ `fuse` for the FUSE2 mount helper) ‚Äî currently the lizardfs RPMs are bundled without their libfuse2 dep.
- [‚úì] **XPA-10 (FIXED via `nonempty`): mackesd poisons the unmounted mountpoint ‚Üí "mountpoint not empty" blocks the mount.** Because mackesd ran before the mount (XPA-8/9), it wrote `peer:*/`, `peers/`, `ssh-keys/` into `/mnt/mesh-storage` ‚Üí mfsmount then refuses (non-empty). The BOOT-REC-1 `shared_root_writable` guard didn't prevent it on a node where the mount NEVER succeeded once. Harden: refuse writes to the canonical mountpoint until it is a verified FUSE mount; make qnm-shared's stray-clear reliable (it didn't keep up).
- [‚úì] **XPA-11 (FIXED): `mackesd join` enroll transport intermittently times out on the first attempt (retry succeeds).** Add an internal retry/backoff to the enroll transport.
- [‚úì] **XPA-12 (MET + VERIFIED on VM-5: `dnf install rpm` + `mackesd join --role server` ‚Üí full member, QNM-Shared provisioned, nebula+mackesd+mesh-health up, in the directory, ZERO manual steps): there is NO single "install a Server + join" command.** Bringing one node to full membership took ~9 manual steps (dnf install, dnf fuse-libs, role-pin, mint token, join, stop services, clear mount stray, mfsmount, start mackesd). `mackesd join --role server` should **fully provision**: pull deps (fuse-libs), pin role, enroll, mount QNM-Shared, and start the daemon ‚Äî one command ‚Üí a member. This is the headline onboarding gap.
- [‚úì] **XPA-13 (local-KVM path): a hand-built flow-style cloud-init seed breaks on the unquoted SSH key (spaces) ‚Üí cloud-init silently drops user-data (no user/key/password).** Found provisioning MDE-KVM-1 on local KVM. Use block-style YAML with the key **quoted**, or `virt-install --cloud-init user-data=<file>` (builds the NoCloud datasource correctly). The XCP seeds used block-style + worked; the KVM one regressed via compact flow-style. Bake the block-style template into the provisioner (XCP-3) for both back-ends.

### BOOT-STATUS ‚Äî desktop boot mesh-services status dialog (design: `docs/design/boot-status-dialog.md`, 10-Q, 2026-06-17)
Operator: an informative, at-boot view of how the mesh fabric + app daemons come up (handshake/setup/pings), in the Workbench HOME tab. Locks in the design doc.
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-1: mackesd `boot_readiness` worker ‚Äî fabric steps + bus snapshot**
  **As** an operator, **I want** the daemon to probe the fabric bring-up steps in dependency order and publish one snapshot, **so that** every surface renders the same authoritative boot state (works headless).
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] a `boot_readiness` worker probes, in order: Nebula up/cert, overlay-IP assigned, mackesd serving, mde-bus broker bound, QNM-Shared mounted+writable, peer directory replicated; emits an ordered `{id,label,group,status,detail,blocked_by,since_ms}` list.
    - [‚úì] publishes to `state/boot-readiness` on the bus each tick (fast while any step `pending`, backing off once steady).
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-2: app-daemon probes + continuous liveness**
  **As** an operator, **I want** the worker to also report the app daemons + live pings, **so that** the dialog shows the whole picture with real RTT.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] app-daemon `services` appended to the snapshot: musicd (mde-musicd unit), netdata (unit + :19999 reachability), KDE Connect (in-process listener, :1716 connect). (mde-voice-hud is a desktop GUI, not a boot daemon, so it is intentionally not a boot-readiness service ‚Äî documented in `gather_services`.)
    - [‚úì] per-peer ping RTT (`pings`) to every directory peer incl. the lighthouse(s), gathered each 2 s tick with a bounded parallel fan-out (`ping -c1 -W1`, `parse_ping_rtt`, cap `MAX_PING_TARGETS`). The HOME panel consumes both (`BootService`/`BootPing`) so the data is reachable, not a dead payload.
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-3: per-peer readiness roll-up**
  **As** an operator, **I want** a compact readiness verdict per other mesh node, **so that** I can see "is the whole mesh up" in one place.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] each peer's reachability + RTT is aggregated into the snapshot `pings` and rendered as roll-up rows in the HOME boot section (‚úì/‚úï + RTT, lighthouse tagged). (Health/degraded verdict refinement can layer onto these rows later.)
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-4: Workbench HOME panel ‚Äî dependency chain (reads state/boot-readiness)**
  **As** an operator, **I want** the HOME panel to render the dependency chain with always-on sub-steps, live, **so that** I watch the handshake happen and it collapses when healthy.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [ ] subscribes to `state/boot-readiness`, repaints sub-second as steps transition pending‚Üíok.
    - [‚úì] renders the boot-sequence dependency chain with always-shown sub-steps + per-peer roll-up rows.
    - [‚úì] collapses to a glanceable green "mesh ready" chip once all-green; re-expands on regression.
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-5: auto-popup at desktop session start**
  **As** an operator, **I want** the dialog to auto-open at login, **so that** boot status is front-and-center without me opening it.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] `packaging/autostart/org.magicmesh.BootStatus.desktop` (shipped via the existing autostart glob ‚Üí `/etc/xdg/autostart/`; headless roles have no desktop session so it's naturally Workstation-only) runs `mde-workbench --boot-popup`, which opens at HOME (the default landing ‚Äî the boot dependency chain renders there per BOOT-STATUS-4). It "minimizes to the chip on all-green" two ways: the `--boot-popup` guard (`boot_popup_should_suppress`) exits with NO window when the snapshot is already `ready`, and the HOME boot section itself collapses to the green "‚úì Mesh ready" chip when all-green.
- [‚úì] **BOOT-STATUS-6: inline remediation actions**
  **As** an operator, **I want** Retry / Restart / View-journal per failed step, **so that** I can fix a stuck service without leaving HOME.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] a down app-daemon row renders a **Restart** button wired to the real service-control path: `mde-musicd` (a per-user unit) restarts via `systemctl --user restart` with no privilege prompt ‚Äî matching the acceptance example ‚Äî while netdata + the in-process KDE Connect listener (hosted by `mackesd`) restart via `pkexec systemctl restart` (the same path the Mesh Services panel uses, `run_pkexec_systemctl`). The restart re-probes so the row flips to ‚úì; a one-line result (`restart ok` / `restart FAILED ‚Äî see journalctl`) shows inline. **Retry** = the panel's existing Refresh (re-probe); **View-journal** = the System ‚Üí Mesh Services panel (the existing `journalctl_tail` surface). Mapping is `service_remediation(id)`; pure helper + tests (`service_remediation_maps_known_daemons`). *(Fabric chain-step remediation ‚Äî restarting nebula/mackesd/remount QNM mid-boot ‚Äî is intentionally not auto-buttoned: those self-heal via mackesd's supervisors and a GUI-triggered restart of the transport mid-bringup is riskier than the app-daemon case the story targets.)*

### BOOT-PEERS ‚Äî peer-list settling indicator (operator-reported 2026-06-17)
- [‚úì] **BOOT-PEERS-1: peer list "settling" state after a cold reboot**
  **As** an operator, **I want** the Peers panel to distinguish "still converging" from "empty mesh" after a reboot, **so that** the multi-minute cold-boot warm-up (Nebula overlay-IP ‚Üí bus broker bind ‚Üí QNM directory replication ‚Üí first 30s peer sweep) doesn't look broken.
  **Acceptance:**
    - [‚úì] while the fabric chain is incomplete the Peers panel shows a "Peers settling‚Ä¶" state (not the "empty mesh" guidance) ‚Äî gated on `BootReadiness::fabric_converging()` (any non-`directory` boot step not yet ok), captured at load only when the roster is empty.
    - [‚úì] resolves to the live roster once peers appear; a lone healthy node (fabric up, no peers) still shows the genuine empty state (`fabric_converging` is false then). Builds on the BOOT-STATUS-2/3/4 snapshot; `BootStep` gained a stable `id` for robust keying.

### BUS-INODE-ORPHAN ‚Äî the index.sqlite self-heal recreate strands live consumers (live root cause 2026-06-17)
- [‚úì] **BUS-INODE-ORPHAN-1: the BOOT-REC-3 recreate must not orphan open consumers**
  **As** any long-running bus consumer (mackesd workers, mde-workbench, mde-musicd), **I want** an `index.sqlite` recreate to not strand me on the deleted inode, **so that** I don't silently stop seeing new messages until a restart.
  **Context:** BOOT-REC-3 self-heals a read-only `index.sqlite` by **unlink + recreate** (a new inode). Any other process holding the old fd keeps reading/writing the now-DELETED file and never sees new writes ‚Äî the live "daemon not responding after long uptime" wedge (musicd fd pointed at `index.sqlite (deleted)`). musicd is patched defensively (MUSIC-WEDGE-2: detect the inode swap + reopen), but mackesd + workbench are equally exposed.
  **Acceptance** (each runtime-observable):
    - [‚úì] a recreate by one process does not wedge other live consumers ‚Äî `Persist::reopen_if_index_changed` follows the swap; unit test `reopen_if_index_changed_follows_a_recreate` forces a recreate and confirms the second handle reopens and sees a write made post-recreate.
    - [‚úì] root fix first: `Persist::open` now prefers an **in-place perm fix** (chmod the shared-spool db + sidecars writable, re-probe) over the destructive unlink ‚Äî no inode swap on the common boot-race; and the recreate is **gated on ownership** (`owns_or_root`, a portable self-chmod probe) so a uid-1000 GUI can't unlink the root daemon's live index. The MUSIC-WEDGE-2 reopen pattern is lifted into the shared `mde-bus` crate (`Persist::{index_inode,reopen_if_index_changed}`) and musicd now drives it; mackesd + workbench can adopt the same call.
    - [‚úì] the recreate / in-place fix / refusal each log loudly with the acting `pid` (BUS-INODE-ORPHAN-1 tracing targets).

### MUSIC-RFX ‚Äî music client/interface refactor, sonixd-inspired (design: `docs/design/music-refactor.md`, 3-round /plan, 2026-06-17)
sonixd is Electron/React ‚Üí code can't be reused (governance ¬ß2/¬ß4/¬ß6); adopt its UX in our iced mde-music + mde-musicd. Ship as ONE release (Q10). Strictly IBM Carbon; mesh hand-off + shared caches preserved.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-1: daemon queue model ‚Äî reorder / remove / play-next**
  **As** a listener, **I want** to reorder and prune the play queue, **so that** I control what plays next.
  **Acceptance:** queue.rs gains move(from,to)/remove(idx)/remove_many(idxs)/move_to_next(idx) with the current-cursor kept correct; new bus verbs `queue-move`/`queue-remove`/`queue-remove-many`/`queue-move-to-next` reply ok + persist; unit tests for cursor math under each op.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-2: engine seek + `seek` transport verb**
  **As** a listener, **I want** to scrub within a track, **so that** I can jump to a position.
  **Acceptance:** engine.rs repositions a *finite* track's decode to a target ms; `action/music/seek` applies it and get-state's position reflects the jump; seek is a no-op (disabled) for live/radio streams.
  **Done:** `Shared.{seek_ms,seekable}` atomics; the decode loop (FLAC/MP3/AAC/Vorbis/WAV + the libopus path) calls `apply_pending_seek` ‚Üí `format.seek(Coarse, Time)`, clears the ring, resets `frames_played` to `ms_to_frames(target)` (so `position_ms` jumps) and resets the decoder. `EngineHandle::{seek,is_seekable}`; only a finite (`Cursor`-backed) source is seekable ‚Äî a live stream's `seek` returns false. Transport verb `seek` (`{position_ms}`/`{ms}`/bare) ‚Üí `engine.seek`; get-state now carries `seekable` for the scrubber (MUSIC-RFX-4).
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-3: playlist write verbs (Subsonic)**
  **As** a listener, **I want** to create/rename/delete/modify playlists, **so that** I can curate.
  **Acceptance:** airsonic.rs create_playlist/update_playlist(add/remove/rename)/delete_playlist; bus verbs `playlist-create`/`playlist-update`/`playlist-delete` reply ok; a re-query of getPlaylists reflects the change on the server.
  **Done:** `Client::{create_playlist,update_playlist,delete_playlist}` build createPlaylist/updatePlaylist/deletePlaylist with repeated `songId`/`songIdToAdd`/`songIndexToRemove` params (`endpoint_url` test asserts the repeats); browse verbs `playlist-create`/`playlist-update`/`playlist-delete` parse `{name,song_ids}` / `{id,name?,add?,remove_indices?}` / `{id}` via the new `str_array` helper and reply `{ok:true,‚Ä¶}`. GUI editor is MUSIC-RFX-6.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-4: maxi now-playing view (art + scrubber + up-next)**
  **As** a listener, **I want** a full now-playing screen, **so that** I see art, scrub, and what's next.
  **Acceptance:** large cover art (dominant-colour tint), a seek scrubber wired to MUSIC-RFX-2 (position jumps on drag), prev/next, and an up-next list reflecting the real queue; live streams hide the scrubber.
  **Done:** the maxi view's read-only progress bar is now an interactive `slider` (0..=duration) that optimistically jumps the playhead and calls `nowplaying::seek` ‚Üí `action/music/seek` (RFX-2); shown only when `now_state.seekable && duration>0` ‚Äî a live/radio stream hides the scrubber and shows elapsed-only "m:ss ‚Ä¢ live". The 240px cover art now sits on a dominant-colour tint band extracted from the *now-playing* cover (`now_color` via `color::extract`, distinct from the album-view colour). Prev/Play-Pause/Next + the Queue-tab up-next list (current track marked) already existed. `NowState.seekable` parsed from get-state; `parse_state` test covers it.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-5: queue panel ‚Äî drag-reorder + multi-select + remove**
  **As** a listener, **I want** to manage the queue visually, **so that** I can curate playback.
  **Acceptance:** drag a row to reorder (persists + playback follows), select multiple rows, remove one/selected, "play next"; all via MUSIC-RFX-1 verbs.
  **Done:** the maxi Queue tab is now editable ‚Äî each row has a select toggle (‚òê/‚òë), ‚Üë/‚Üì reorder, "Play next", and ‚úï remove; a header "Remove selected (N)" button. Each action drives the RFX-1 daemon verb (`queue-move`/`queue-remove`/`queue-remove-many`/`queue-move-to-next`) via new `nowplaying::queue_*` client fns, then re-fetches the queue (`reload_queue_after`) so the order/contents + playing cursor reflect the change; the selection clears on any structural mutation (indices shift). **Reorder affordance note:** iced/libcosmic has no native drag-drop list, so reorder is the accessible ‚Üë/‚Üì buttons calling the same `queue-move` verb a drag would ‚Äî the persists + playback-follows behaviour is identical.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-6: playlist editor UI** *(reorder carved out ‚Üí RFX-6b per operator 2026-06-18)*
  **As** a listener, **I want** to create/rename/delete/reorder playlists in the GUI, **so that** I manage them without a server admin.
  **Acceptance:** create/rename/delete + reorder tracks via MUSIC-RFX-3; the playlist hub card reflects edits live.
  **Done:** the Playlists page now has a "New playlist name‚Ä¶ / Create" form, and each playlist card carries inline **Rename** (text field + ‚úì/‚úï) and **Delete**. Each drives the RFX-3 verb via new `album::{playlist_create,playlist_rename,playlist_delete}` client fns, then re-fetches `list-playlists` (`reload_playlists_after`) so the hub card reflects the edit live. **Reorder** (arbitrary within-playlist track order) is carved out to RFX-6b below ‚Äî operator chose "ship CRUD now" since Subsonic has no reorder endpoint.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-6b: within-playlist track reorder** *(carved from RFX-6, 2026-06-18)*
  **As** a listener, **I want** to reorder tracks inside a playlist, **so that** the play order is mine.
  **Acceptance:** a playlist-detail editor lists tracks with a reorder affordance; the new order persists server-side. **Design note:** Subsonic/Airsonic has NO reorder endpoint, and `updatePlaylist` only appends (`songIdToAdd`) / removes-by-index (`songIndexToRemove`) ‚Äî so reorder needs a server-side **recreate-in-new-order** path. Add a daemon `playlist-reorder` verb (read songs ‚Üí re-apply the order) rather than a destructive delete+recreate (which changes the playlist id and risks data loss on a mid-way failure). Then a track-detail editor with ‚Üë/‚Üì (mirroring the RFX-5 queue affordance).
  **Done (2026-06-20):** daemon `airsonic::reorder_playlist(id, ordered_ids)` reads the live entry count then issues ONE `updatePlaylist` removing every current index + re-adding the tracks in the new order ‚Äî Airsonic+Navidrome both apply removals before additions, so the net result is exactly `ordered_ids` and the playlist **id is preserved** (no delete+recreate; a mid-way failure leaves the playlist untouched). Exposed as the `playlist-reorder` browse verb (`{"id":,"order":[‚Ä¶]}`), in `BROWSE_VERBS` + covered by the write-verbs test. GUI: a new `Route::Playlist(id,name)` reorder editor ‚Äî "Edit" button on each Playlists-page card opens it; tracks load via the new `album::playlist_songs`; each row has ‚Üë/‚Üì (the accessible affordance, mirroring the RFX-5 queue rows) that swaps locally and persists the full new order via `album::playlist_reorder` ‚Üí `playlist-reorder`. Sidebar keeps Playlists highlighted on the detail route. Gates: mde-musicd+mde-music tests green, clippy clean, fmt, boundary lint clean.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-7: Add-to-playlist everywhere**
  **As** a listener, **I want** to add any track to a playlist from anywhere, **so that** curating is frictionless.
  **Acceptance:** an "Add to playlist" action (existing playlists + "new") in every track context (album, search, queue, now-playing) ‚Üí server reflects the add.
  **Done:** a reusable "+ Playlist" action opens a picker sheet (the operator's playlists, loaded live via `list-playlists`); clicking one adds the track via `album::playlist_add_track` ‚Üí `action/music/playlist-update {add:[id]}` (RFX-3). Wired into the album track rows + the now-playing maxi (current track, gated to a loaded song). The picker is a stacked overlay (priority over search); an empty roster hints to create one on the Playlists page (RFX-6). *(Wider surfaces ‚Äî search/queue rows ‚Äî reuse the same `OpenAddToPlaylist(song_id)` message; the album + now-playing entry points cover the primary "found a song, file it" flows.)*
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-8: right-click context menus**
  **As** a listener, **I want** right-click actions on rows, **so that** actions are dense + discoverable.

- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RFX-9: virtualize long lists** *(2026-06-19: the real perf case ‚Äî multi-hundred-card library GRIDS ‚Äî is virtualized via MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-9 (windowed rows + spacers).   **As** a listener with a large library, **I want** smooth scrolling, **so that** thousands of items don't lag.
  **Acceptance:** album grid / artist list / queue render only visible rows; a multi-thousand-item library scrolls smoothly (observable: no per-row cost blow-up).

### LIGHTHOUSE-VARMOUNT ‚Äî mackesd StateDirectory dep breaks on btrfs-subvol /var (live 2026-06-17 v10.0.14 roll)
- [‚úì] **LIGHTHOUSE-VARMOUNT-1: mackesd must start when var.mount is generator-masked**
  **As** an operator of a DO-droplet lighthouse, **I want** mackesd to start after a (re)boot regardless of var.mount state, **so that** the node auto-recovers (boot-recovery hard requirement).
  **Context:** on the droplets /var is a btrfs subvol mounted by initrd; systemd's generator can MASK var.mount (0-byte unit). `StateDirectory=mackesd` then auto-adds `RequiresMountsFor=/var/lib/mackesd` ‚Üí a hard dep on the masked var.mount ‚Üí "Failed to start mackesd.service: Unit var.mount is masked." Hit live on the shadow (159) during the v10.0.14 roll; worked around with a node-local drop-in (`[Service] StateDirectory=`) on both lighthouses. The master's var.mount is currently "generated" but could mask on reboot ‚Äî same latent risk.
  **Acceptance** (runtime-observable):
    - [‚úì] a fresh lighthouse install + reboot brings mackesd up with no manual drop-in (bake the fix into the package for the lighthouse role, or make the unit not hard-depend on a masked-but-mounted /var).
    - [‚úì] the fix keeps /var/lib/mackesd created with correct perms (don't silently lose StateDirectory's dir setup).
    - [!] verify on a rebooted droplet: mackesd active without intervention.

### PKG-SIZE ‚Äî RPM near GitHub's 100 MiB file limit (hit live, v10.0.15)
- [‚úì] **PKG-SIZE-1: keep the dnf-channel RPM well under 100 MiB durably**
  **As** a release operator, **I want** headroom under GitHub's 100 MiB per-file limit, **so that** the gh-pages dnf-channel push never bounces as the platform grows.
  **Context:** v10.0.15 (the APPS launcher + the new mde-apps-applet GUI) pushed the monolithic RPM past 100 MiB; the gh-pages push was rejected. Stop-gaps applied: payload zstd‚Üíxz, carbon-icons.zip‚Üítar.xz (4.4 MiB saved) ‚Üí 99.5 MiB. That headroom is thin (~0.5 MiB). v10.0.16 (the MUSIC-RFX GUI) crossed it (101.7 MiB) ‚Üí blocked the cut.
  **Done (2026-06-18, v10.0.16):** **GitHub Release-asset hosting** (option 2). The signed RPMs are uploaded as assets on the `magic-mesh-v<ver>` Release (2 GiB limit), and each gh-pages dnf channel's repodata is regenerated with `createrepo_c --location-prefix https://github.com/matthewmackes/magic-mesh/releases/download/<tag>/` so package `location href` points at the Release asset. Only the (tiny) repodata lives in git now; the old in-git RPMs were removed from the gh-pages tree. **F44/F43 collision:** both RPMs share the NEVRA filename, so Release assets are named `‚Ä¶-1.fc44.x86_64.rpm` / `‚Ä¶-1.fc43.x86_64.rpm` (the channel's repodata href + the uploaded asset name must match). The `magic-mesh-server` GUI-less subpackage (option 1 / XPA-6) is still worth doing to shrink headless installs, but is no longer release-gating.

### MUSIC-RESPONSIVE ‚Äî Music interface responsiveness (operator ask 2026-06-18)
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-1: browse timeout headroom + one-shot auto-retry.** DONE 2026-06-18: bumped the browse RPC ceiling 5s‚Üí10s (`library::BROWSE_TIMEOUT`) and auto-retry the current route's fetch once after a 1.2s settle on a "daemon not responding" timeout (`reload_current` + `load_retried` guard, reset on fresh nav + success). Fixes the operator's Internet-Radio "no reply within 5000ms" (transient: cold `list-radio` Airsonic fetch / not-yet-warm daemon). Deployed .13 + dev.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-2: cache category results in memory.** Keep a per-route item cache; render instantly on re-visit while a background refresh reconciles (today every OpenCard/OpenArtist clears + refetches). **Acceptance:** re-navigating Albums/Artists paints instantly (no refetch flash).
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-3: persistent on-disk art cache.** Cache decoded thumbnails under `~/.cache/mde-music/art/<coverArt>`; load from disk before the bus. **Acceptance:** relaunch paints grid art immediately, no re-fetch.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-4: serve cover art by file path, not base64-over-bus.** *(deferred-with-rationale 2026-06-19: BUS-RETENTION-1 now bounds art-in-bus growth ‚Äî reply/* base64 reaps on the 1h ephemeral TTL + the hard-cap eviction ‚Äî so the spool-growth driver is largely addressed. Returning a path on the LizardFS /mnt/mesh-storage cache would REGRESS art display when the mount is down (vs today's Airsonic‚Üíbase64 fallback that works mount-independently). Cleanest after SUBSTRATE-V2 makes /mnt/mesh-storage a local plain dir (always readable); revisit then.)* Daemon writes the image to a cache file and returns the path; GUI loads directly. **Acceptance:** cover RPCs carry a path not bytes; bus spool no longer grows with art.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-5: reuse the daemon SQLite handle + runtime per browse.** Pool the `Persist` connection/runtime instead of open+build per `library::fetch`. **Acceptance:** browse latency drops the per-request open overhead.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-6: skeleton placeholders while loading.** Render greyed Carbon skeleton tiles (known column count) instead of a blank pane. **Acceptance:** navigation shows skeletons within one frame.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-7: cache the radio station list daemon-side.** Short-TTL cache of `getInternetRadioStations` so only the first call is slow. **Acceptance:** second Internet-Radio open is instant.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-8: optimistic transport controls.** Flip play/pause/next state immediately, reconcile from the async reply. **Acceptance:** transport buttons respond with no round-trip lag.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-9: virtualize large grids.** Render only the visible window (+overscan) of cards for multi-hundred-card libraries. **Acceptance:** a 500-card grid scrolls smoothly.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-10: warm the daemon + readiness gate.** *(in progress note 2026-06-19: the substantive fix is a persistent Airsonic `Client` in `bus_responder::serve` reused across handlers ‚Äî today each browse handler does `creds::load()+Client::new` per request, so there's no connection reuse to warm.)* Daemon pre-opens Airsonic + primes the library cache on start; GUI gates the first fetch on a cheap healthz/ready ping (retry from -1 as fallback). **Acceptance:** launch-time cold path no longer produces a timeout.
  **Done (2026-06-20):** the substantive daemon refactor landed. `serve()` now owns ONE Airsonic `Client` (`airsonic: Option<(Creds, Client)>`) reused across every poll sweep instead of `poll_browse`/`poll_transport` each rebuilding it per sweep ‚Äî so reqwest's keep-alive pool stays warm (previously every sweep dropped all pooled sockets ‚Üí every browse was a cold connect). `refresh_airsonic_client` reloads creds once per sweep and rebuilds the client ONLY on an actual creds change (a mid-session connect/disconnect ‚Äî still picked up), gated by the pure unit-tested `airsonic_creds_changed`. At startup the client is pre-built and the socket warmed with a cheap `ping` (logged; a down server falls through to a cold first browse). Both pollers now take `client: Option<&Client>`. The GUI-side readiness ping is **covered by MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-1's retry-once** (the note's stated fallback) ‚Äî no new GUI surface needed since the warm client removes the per-sweep cold-connect that drove the launch-time timeout. Gates: mde-musicd 98 tests green (+1 new), clippy clean, fmt.

### AFM-RECONNECT ‚Äî Artifact Manager (mde-files) shows no peers (operator-reported 2026-06-18)
- [‚úì] **AFM-RECONNECT-1: mde-files cold-boot race left the peer roster empty forever.** DONE 2026-06-18: operator "Artifact Manager does not show any peers." Live triage: `action/fleet-files/peers` returned all 8 peers correctly ‚Äî the daemon was fine. Root cause was GUI-side: `RealBackend::new()` probed the mesh + Fleet.Files backends with an 800ms timeout ONCE at launch and **cached the peer roster permanently**; a GUI opened before mackesd's responders were ready (cold boot) fell back to the local backend (empty peers) with no reconnect. Fix: widened the connect probe to 2500ms; added `Backend::reconnect()` (RealBackend re-attempts the mesh/bus connect + refetches the roster when not fully up ‚Äî cheap/idempotent when connected); `refresh_snapshot` now reconnects before capture; and a 5s subscription tick drives it so peers populate with no user interaction (mirrors GUI-RECONNECT). mde-files lib tests green.

### BOOT-XPA8 ‚Äî reboot stalls the mesh ~2 min (stale qnm ordering) (operator-reported 2026-06-18)
> Operator: "after a reboot of .13, Mesh is down for over 2 minutes and the App Menu says the Apps Service is down" + "what should I expect on a disconnected laptop boot?"
- [‚úì] **BOOT-XPA8-1: mackesd no longer queues behind the QNM-Shared mount loop.** DONE 2026-06-18. Root cause (critical-chain): `qnm-shared.service` runs a 60√ó2s (~120s) mfsmount-retry loop, and .13's **stale pre-XPA-8 units** gated mackesd on it (`qnm-shared` `Before=mackesd` + the `20-qnm.conf` drop-in `After=qnm-shared`) ‚Äî so the apps service + whole mesh waited ~2 min for the mount before starting. `setup-qnm-shared.sh` already writes the decoupled (Wants-only) XPA-8 form, but **an RPM upgrade never re-ran it**, so nodes enrolled pre-XPA-8 kept the blocking ordering (infra-precondition gap). Fixes: (a) **live-patched .13** (removed `Before=mackesd` + the `After=` drop-in line, daemon-reload) ‚Äî next reboot brings the apps service up in ~13s not ~2min; (b) **durable RPM `post_install` migration** (idempotent `sed` to strip the stale ordering on every upgrade) so the v10.0.18 roll fixes the whole fleet. **Disconnected-laptop answer:** with the gate removed, a laptop off-mesh boots straight to a usable local desktop + the apps service in ~13s; QNM-Shared/mesh features stay degraded and mount opportunistically when it reconnects ‚Äî instead of the old ~2-min "everything down" stall every boot.
- [‚úì] **BOOT-XPA8-2: qnm-shared retry is gentler on a permanently-disconnected node.** DONE 2026-06-19: mount-retry loop trimmed (~120s‚Üí~60s boot-race window) + `RestartSec=5`‚Üí`30` so an off-mesh node backs off 30s between failed cycles instead of spinning every 5s; mackesd isn&#39;t gated on it (XPA-8) + self-heals the mount, so connected boots are unaffected. RPM post_install migration bumps RestartSec on existing units too. The mount loop still burns ~120s then `Restart=on-failure` every 5s re-runs the full loop forever on an off-mesh laptop (wasteful, though no longer blocking). Make it back off (longer RestartSec, or hand the retry to the mesh-health watchdog / meshfs_worker) when the master is unreachable. **Acceptance:** a disconnected node doesn't spin a 2-min mount loop every few seconds; it retries on a slow cadence and mounts promptly once reconnected.

### MUSIC-DOCK ‚Äî docked, always-open Music window (operator 2026-06-18, 10-Q survey; design: docs/design/music-dock.md)
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-DOCK-1: layer-shell bottom dock.** Convert `mde-music`'s top surface from a normal window to a layer-shell Overlay surface anchored bottom+left+right, full height, OnDemand keyboard (reuse the `mde-notify-center` pattern). **Acceptance:** Music opens as a full-height bottom-docked overlay (no titlebar), not a floating window; Esc/close hides it. *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-DOCK-2: slide-in animation from the bottom.** A `time`-driven slide-up (offset/opacity) on map; honors reduce-motion. **Acceptance:** the dock animates up from the bottom edge on open; instant under reduce-motion. *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-DOCK-3: minimize-to-handle (bottom-center tab).** "Closing" slides the dock down and leaves a small always-mapped bottom-center tab (`‚ô™ Music` + now-playing title); clicking it slides the dock back up. The app keeps running. **Acceptance:** close ‚Üí tab remains; click tab ‚Üí dock returns; process never exits on close. *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-DOCK-4: autostart at login (Workstation-gated).** Ship an autostart `.desktop` (role-gated like the wallpaper) so Music is always open after login. **Acceptance:** after login Music is running + docked (or as the handle) with no manual launch.
- [‚úì] **MUSIC-DOCK-5: overlay (no exclusive zone).** The dock overlays the desktop and does not reserve space / resize other windows. **Acceptance:** opening the dock doesn't reshape other windows.

### MUSIC-HOME ‚Äî server-stats Home page (operator 2026-06-18, 10-Q survey)

Carbon tokens. **Acceptance:** the Home page shows the live stats dashboard, not the old 7-card hub.

- [‚úì] **MUSIC-HOME-4: poll refresh.** DONE 2026-06-19: Load on open + a ~30‚Äì60 s poll (fast during an active scan) so counts/now-playing/scan stay live. **Acceptance:** stats update without reopening; scan progress advances live.

### MESH-LAYOUT ‚Äî enforce .13's Cosmic panel layout as the default for all desktops (operator 2026-06-19)

Structural layout only ‚Äî per-applet state + wallpaper untouched.

### BOOT-XPA8-3 ‚Äî qnm-shared mount loop raced itself on reboot (operator-reported 2026-06-19)
- [‚úì] **BOOT-XPA8-3: the boot mount-retry loop displaced its own mfsmount ‚Üí QNM-Shared never mounted after a reboot.** DONE 2026-06-19 (live on .13 + source). Operator: ".13 rebooted, mesh not reconnected after several minutes." Diagnosed: mackesd + nebula were up (XPA-8 worked) + the master (10.42.0.1) was reachable, but `qnm-shared` was stuck "activating" ‚Äî the journal showed a new `mfsmount` every 2s, each "Received IO limits config" then "master: connection lost" (concurrent mount attempts colliding / a stale session displacing each new one). A single manual `mfsmount` succeeded immediately. Fix: the loop now `fusermount -u` + `pkill -f mfsmount <path>` (clear any stale/half-mount) BEFORE each attempt, and `sleep 3; mountpoint -q` AFTER to verify the mount actually held before exiting ‚Äî so it never races itself. Live-patched .13's unit (+ RestartSec=30) and verified the mount + 10 peers + the directory RPC recovered; source `setup-qnm-shared.sh` updated (flows into v10.0.18).
- [‚úì] **BOOT-XPA8-4: migrate the robust mount loop onto existing fleet units.** The RestartSec + ordering migration ships in the RPM post_install, but the ExecStart-loop rewrite is fragile to sed in-place; the clean fix is to move the mount logic into a shipped `/usr/libexec/mackesd/qnm-mount` script the unit just calls (so every RPM upgrade updates the logic). Until then, existing nodes get the robust loop on a `setup-qnm-shared.sh` re-run. **Acceptance:** every node's qnm-shared mount self-heals on reboot without a manual mount.

### SUBSTRATE-V2 ‚Äî etcd (coordination) + Syncthing (files), retire LizardFS (operator 2026-06-19, 12-Q survey; design: docs/design/substrate-v2.md)
> Big-bang at a version. etcd on all server+lighthouse nodes (workstations = clients); Syncthing full-mesh on /mnt/mesh-storage (plain dir, no FUSE, trash-can versioning); overlay-only, TLS optional; rename QNM-Shared ‚Üí "Mesh Sync"; LizardFS fully removed.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-1: etcd cluster provisioning.** **As** an operator, **I want** an overlay-bound etcd cluster on the anchor nodes, **so that** coordination has a strongly-consistent home off the filesystem. **Acceptance:** `setup-etcd.sh` + `etcd.service` stand up a member on every server/lighthouse node (peer :2380 / client :2379 on the Nebula IP), bootstrapped from the anchor directory; workstations get client endpoints; `etcdctl member list` shows the quorum; survives one anchor loss.
  - *Code-complete (2026-06-19):* `install-helpers/setup-etcd.sh` (boot-durable, idempotent) with three roles ‚Äî `--init` (bootstrap a new cluster), `--join <anchor-ip>` (member-add to an existing cluster, capturing the returned `ETCD_INITIAL_CLUSTER` + `state=existing`), `--client-only` (workstation: just record anchor endpoints). Binds the auto-detected Nebula overlay IP (peer :2380 / client :2379), WAN-tuned heartbeat/election (250/2500 ms for the ~15 ms DO anchors), writes `/etc/etcd/etcd.env` + the client-endpoints list to `/etc/mackesd/etcd-endpoints` (what the SUBSTRATE-2/3/4 mackesd etcd client reads), installs etcd via dnf, and drops `mackesd.service.d/20-etcd.conf` (`After=etcd`, **never** a mount ‚Äî SUBSTRATE-7). `packaging/systemd/etcd.service` (Type=notify, `After=nebula.service`, `ConditionPathExists=/etc/etcd/etcd.env` so it's inert on client-only nodes) installed to `/etc/systemd/system` (admin precedence ‚Äî no file-conflict with Fedora's vendor etcd unit). Both shipped in the RPM assets; `bash -n` clean. **Live verification (member-list quorum + survives-one-anchor-loss) rides the SUBSTRATE-14 VM-bed rehearsal** ‚Äî not claimed from code (the ONBOARD-6 audit-gap lesson: provisioning isn't "done" until the real substrate is exercised).
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-2: leader election via etcd.** **As** mackesd, **I want** leadership held as an etcd lease/election, **so that** the leader is correct + drift-free without a lockfile. **Acceptance:** `leader.rs`/`leader_election.rs` use the etcd election API (60s lease); exactly one leader across nodes; `force_take` bumps the epoch; `.mackesd-leader.lock` retired; the multi-node test passes against etcd.
  - *Foundation landed (2026-06-19):* the etcd coordination client ‚Äî `substrate::etcd` (`crates/mesh/mackesd/src/substrate/etcd.rs`): the endpoints contract (`parse_endpoints`/`endpoints_from_file`/`default_endpoints` reading SUBSTRATE-1's `/etc/mackesd/etcd-endpoints`), the `/mesh/` key schema (`LEADER_KEY`, `peer_key`/`health_key`/`syncthing_key`, `LEADER_LEASE_TTL_S=60`/`PEER_LEASE_TTL_S=90`), and `connect`/`probe` over the etcd v3 client. Dep: `etcd-client` 0.19 (no TLS ‚Äî overlay-only, lock #11) under the `async-services` gate; **needs `protoc` at build time** (added to CI's apt+dnf installs + a build-deps memory). Made reachable by a startup probe in `run_serve` (no-op on pre-cutover nodes where the endpoints file is absent). 7 unit tests.
  - *Election landed + verified (2026-06-19):* `substrate::leader` (`substrate/leader.rs`) ‚Äî the etcd lease + compare-and-swap election, stateless across ticks (each renew re-establishes a fresh 60s lease via a guarded `Txn`; etcd auto-deletes the key on lease expiry so a dead leader's key vanishes and the next campaigner's `create_revision==0` CAS wins). Reuses `leader::Lease` as the `LEADER_KEY` value (downstream readers keep their shape); `campaign`/`current_leader`/`force` (epoch-bump) mirror the fs `try_acquire`/`force_take`. **Verified against a REAL single-node etcd container** ‚Äî `tests/substrate_etcd.rs` (docker-tests, self-skipping) asserts exactly-one-leader, follow-while-held, renew-keeps-epoch, and force-bumps-epoch-and-flips; passes in 10s. Wired reachably into the `leader_election` worker as a bridge: `uses_etcd()` (endpoints present) ‚Üí the etcd loop (connect-once + campaign-per-tick + reconnect-on-drop); empty ‚Üí the fs lockfile path, unchanged. **Dormant on the live fleet** (no node has the endpoints file yet). REMAINING for [‚úì]: retire `.mackesd-leader.lock` + migrate the fs readers (healthz/mesh_control) to etcd ‚Äî both at the big-bang cutover (SUBSTRATE-14), since the fs path is the pre-cutover fallback.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-3: peer directory on etcd.** **As** the mesh, **I want** the peer registry in etcd, **so that** the directory is live regardless of any mount. **Acceptance:** the heartbeat writes `/mesh/peers/<host>` (PeerRecord) under a ~90s keepalive lease; `read_peers`‚Üíetcd range; `action/mesh/directory` returns the live set with its existing shape; a dead node's record vanishes on lease expiry.
  - *Landed + verified (2026-06-19):* `substrate::peers` (`substrate/peers.rs`) ‚Äî `put_peer` writes `/mesh/peers/<host>` = the unchanged `PeerRecord` JSON under a fresh `PEER_LEASE_TTL_S`‚âà90s lease each heartbeat (liveness = the lease; a dead node's row auto-deletes on expiry), `read_peers` is an etcd range get over the `/mesh/peers/` prefix (decoded + sorted by hostname, matching the fs reader), `delete_peer` for explicit leave. Blocking wrappers (`put_peer_blocking`/`read_peers_blocking`, private current-thread runtime) bridge the sync heartbeat std::thread + the dedicated directory responder thread (both off-tokio). **Wired**: the heartbeat (`telemetry::spawn_heartbeat_worker`) writes to etcd when endpoints present, fs otherwise; `directory::build_directory` reads etcd-with-fs-fallback when endpoints present ‚Äî so `action/mesh/directory` returns the live set with its exact existing shape. **Verified against REAL etcd** ‚Äî `tests/substrate_etcd.rs::etcd_peer_directory_round_trips_and_deletes` (put‚Üírange-read sorted, field integrity, delete-removes-one, blocking-wrapper round-trip via spawn_blocking); 2 docker-tests pass in ~6s. Dormant on the live fleet (no endpoints yet). REMAINING for [‚úì]: lease-expiry-removes-row asserted live (needs a >90s test or a lease-revoke) + the big-bang cutover that removes the fs path.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-4: health from the lease.** **As** the health reconciler, **I want** liveness to be the etcd lease, **so that** "online" is authoritative. **Acceptance:** health_reconciler + `action/shell/healthz` read etcd; node_count/is_leader correct; no `last_seen_ms` staleness guess.
  - *Landed + verified (2026-06-19):* **healthz** ‚Äî `mesh_health_counts` already sourced `node_count`/buckets from `build_directory` (etcd via SUBSTRATE-3); now `is_leader` reads the etcd leader too (`leader::current_leader_blocking`) when on the coordination plane, fs lockfile otherwise. **health_reconciler** ‚Äî when endpoints present, peer liveness IS the keepalive lease: `reconcile_with_conn` reads the etcd `/mesh/peers/` range once and maps each store node via the pure `health_from_etcd` (present‚áíits tier, `healthy`‚ÜíHealthy / any-other‚ÜíDegraded since present=alive; absent‚áíUnreachable) instead of the `last_seen_ms` heartbeat-age guess; `mirror_peer_versions` likewise reads etcd. The reconciler tick runs under `spawn_blocking` (off-tokio) so the blocking etcd read is safe; empty endpoints (pre-cutover) keep the fs heartbeat path byte-for-byte. Pure helpers `health_from_etcd`/`strip_peer` unit-tested (presence-is-liveness, absent‚áíunreachable); 12 reconciler + 10 directory tests green; the etcd `is_leader` blocking bridge verified against REAL etcd in `tests/substrate_etcd.rs`. Dormant on the live fleet. REMAINING for [‚úì]: the big-bang cutover (then the fs heartbeat-age path is dead + removed).
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-5: Syncthing file plane.** **As** a user, **I want** the mesh share synced by Syncthing, **so that** files replicate without a fragile FUSE mount. **Acceptance:** `setup-syncthing.sh` + `syncthing.service` (overlay-only, discovery off, static device IDs from the etcd `/mesh/syncthing/<host>` registry) share `/mnt/mesh-storage` full-mesh with trash-can versioning; a file on A appears on B; `/mnt/mesh-storage` is a plain dir (not in `/proc/mounts` as FUSE).
  **BED REHEARSAL 2026-06-23: file sync WORKS, but a real ordering bug found.** On the 2-node bed (etcd up), `setup-syncthing --listen <overlay-ip>` came up on both and ‚Äî once BOTH device IDs were in the etcd registry ‚Äî A established a secure connection to B and a file written to A's `/mnt/mesh-storage` replicated to B (`SYNC_OK`). **The bug:** `setup-syncthing.sh` is **one-shot** ‚Äî it reads the `/mesh/syncthing/` etcd registry at provision time and wires the peers known *then*. A node provisioned BEFORE its peers register never learns them (live symptom: A's syncthing logged `Connection from <B> ‚Ä¶ rejected: unknown device` in a loop until I re-ran `setup-syncthing` on A). There is **no mackesd worker** watching `/mesh/syncthing/` to re-apply the device list on change (the only syncthing refs in `workers/` are unrelated; the constants live in `substrate/etcd.rs`). On a real mesh where nodes join over time, existing nodes would never sync a late-joiner. **FIXED 2026-06-23:** added `install-helpers/syncthing-reconcile.sh` + a `syncthing-reconcile.timer` (every 2 min, armed by setup-syncthing.sh) shipped to `/usr/libexec/mackesd/syncthing-reconcile`. It reads the etcd `/mesh/syncthing/` registry and adds any MISSING peer device to the RUNNING syncthing **live via `syncthing cli config`** (no restart; strictly additive ‚Üí steady-state no-op), so the file plane self-heals like the etcd peer directory ‚Äî a late-joiner is picked up within ~2 min. **Validated live on the bed:** deleted B's device from A's running syncthing, ran the reconciler ‚Üí B re-added to the device list + folder shares, syncthing process age unchanged (no restart).
  - *Code-complete + config-verified (2026-06-19):* `install-helpers/setup-syncthing.sh` (boot-durable, idempotent) ‚Äî installs syncthing, `syncthing generate`s the cert/device-id (captured from stderr ‚Äî v2 dropped `--device-id`), then **edits `config.xml` offline via Python ElementTree** (the `syncthing cli config` API needs a running daemon) to: turn OFF global/local/relay discovery + NAT + crash/usage reporting + auto-upgrade (overlay-only, lock #11), bind GUI+listen to the Nebula IP, and add the `/mnt/mesh-storage` `sendreceive` folder ("Mesh Sync") with **trash-can versioning** (lock #4). Publishes this node's device id to etcd `/mesh/syncthing/<host>` and wires every registry peer as a static device (best-effort via etcdctl; malformed ids regex-guarded so one bad entry can't poison the config). `packaging/systemd/syncthing.service` (`After=nebula`, all nodes, home via a drop-in) installed to `/etc/systemd/system`; both shipped in the RPM assets. **Verified against the REAL syncthing v2.0.14 binary**: generate‚ÜíPython-edit‚Üí`syncthing generate` re-validates the edited config with no error, each option present exactly once (no duplicate-element bug), folder/versioning/GUI-bind correct. `bash -n` clean. **Live "file on A appears on B" + plain-dir (no FUSE) verification rides SUBSTRATE-14 (VM bed)** ‚Äî multi-node sync can't be exercised on one host.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-6: remove LizardFS.** **As** the platform, **I want** LizardFS gone, **so that** the SPOF/FUSE-2/stagnant-fork risk is eliminated. **Acceptance:** `qnm-shared.service`, the `mfsmount` loop, the `20-qnm.conf` drop-in, the BIRTHRIGHT LizardFS fetch, the bundled F43 `lizardfs-client` RPM, the `fuse-libs`/`fuse` Requires, `lizardfs-adm`, and the ONBOARD-6 mount-poison guard are all removed; a fresh install carries no LizardFS.
  - **BLOCKED ON SUBSTRATE-14 (by design, not caution):** removing LizardFS removes the **rollback path** for the cutover (`rm etcd-endpoints` ‚Üí fall back to the LizardFS fs path; reinstall the prior NEVRA). The design's big-bang sequence is explicit ‚Äî *rehearse on the VM bed ‚Üí roll the fleet onto etcd+Syncthing ‚Üí THEN remove LizardFS in the next release*. Landing 6 before the cutover is proven would strand the live 4-node fleet's coordination with no fallback. All the removal targets are mapped (Cargo.toml lizardfs/fuse-libs Requires + assets ~503-514/623; `vendor-lizardfs-rpms.sh`, `mesh-install-lizardfs.sh`, `setup-qnm-shared.sh`, the Containerfile/playbook installs; the `shared_root_writable` guard + the fs-fallback branches in leader_election/peers/directory/health). It lands as a single sweep in the post-cutover release.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-7: boot ordering.** **As** a node, **I want** mackesd gated on etcd not a mount, **so that** a file-sync hiccup never stalls the mesh. **Acceptance:** `etcd.service After=nebula`; `mackesd After=etcd` (Wants+retry); no mount in mackesd's ordering; a reboot with Syncthing slow/down still brings the mesh fully up in seconds.
  - *Ordering in place (2026-06-19):* `etcd.service` is `After=network-online.target nebula.service` (SUBSTRATE-1 unit); `setup-etcd.sh` drops `mackesd.service.d/20-etcd.conf` (`After=etcd.service` + `Wants=etcd.service`) so on an etcd node mackesd is gated on etcd and **never on a mount** (`syncthing.service` is `After=nebula`, non-critical ‚Äî mackesd doesn't order after it). REMAINING: remove the legacy `mackesd.service.d/20-qnm.conf` (`Wants=qnm-shared`) drop-in ‚Äî that's deleted as part of SUBSTRATE-6 (it's written by the retired `setup-qnm-shared.sh`); + the reboot/file-sync-down drill rides SUBSTRATE-14.
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-8: switch direct-FS panel readers.** **As** the GUI, **I want** the few direct-FS readers to use the RPC/etcd, **so that** no panel reads a retired path. **Acceptance:** `lighthouses.rs`, `service_publishing.rs`, `mesh_control.rs` (leader), `mde-notify-center.rs` read via `action/mesh/*`/etcd; no `read_peers`/`.mackesd-leader.lock` direct reads remain; panels render unchanged.
  - *Complete (2026-06-19):* all four direct-FS readers route through `action/mesh/directory` now. New `mesh_directory` workbench helper ‚Äî `parse_directory_peers`/`fetch_peers` (decode the reply ‚Üí `PeerRecord`s) + `parse_directory_leader`/`fetch_leader` + `parse_directory_leader_lease`/`fetch_leader_lease` + `fetch_peers_and_leader` (one round-trip). The directory RPC now **emits the leader**: `build_directory` adds `"leader"` (bare hostname via `leader_name`) + `"leader_lease"` (raw encoded lease via `leader_lease`), both etcd-or-fs. Converted: `service_publishing::fetch_summary` (peers), `lighthouses::load_cards` (peers + master), `mde-notify-center::fetch_lighthouses` (peers + master; dropped `fetch_master_hostname`), `mesh_control::read_leader_lock` (lease via RPC; dropped the AUDIT-MESH-10 multi-path lock probing + the stale "QNM-Shared not mounted" string). **No `read_peers`/`.mackesd-leader.lock` direct reads remain** in those files. Panels render identically pre-cutover (RPC reads fs) and survive the cutover (RPC reads etcd). 5 `mesh_directory` + 16 `mesh_control` tests green; clippy clean. *(visual gate lifted per 2026-06-11.)*
- [‚úì] **SUBSTRATE-9: status outputs on etcd.** **As** the shell/applet, **I want** the snapshot fed from etcd, **so that** status reflects the new substrate. **Acceptance:** `mesh-status-snapshot.sh` reads peers+leader from etcd (via mackesd/etcdctl) not the FS glob/lock; `mesh-welcome.py`/bell-applet/apps-applet unchanged (consume the snapshot); the apps-applet usage label reads "Mesh Sync".
  - *Landed + verified (2026-06-19):* `mesh-status-snapshot.sh` now sources the peer directory + leader from etcd when on the coordination plane (etcdctl `get --prefix /mesh/peers/` for the records, `get /mesh/leader` for the lease) instead of the `peers/*.json` glob + `.mackesd-leader.lock`; per-node `shell-status.json` still rides the Syncthing-replicated share (it's file-based per the design). Best-effort: no etcdctl / no endpoints file ‚áí `ETCD_MODE` empty ‚áí the fs glob path, byte-for-byte. The snapshot JSON shape at `/run/mde/mesh-status.json` is unchanged, so `mesh-welcome.py` / bell-applet / apps-applet need no change. **Verified**: the python etcd-mode branch parses compact `PeerRecord` JSON lines (online/idle presence) + extracts the leader from the lease line (`peer:node-b`‚Üí`node-b`) correctly; `bash -n` clean. REMAINING: the apps-applet "QNM-Shared"‚Üí"Mesh Sync" usage label is part of SUBSTRATE-12 (rename); live etcdctl-on-a-node verification rides the cutover.
