### VPN-GW ‚Äî commercial-VPN exit gateways on every node (operator 2026-06-19, 10-Q survey; design: docs/design/vpn-gateway.md; 11.0+)
> Every node can run multiple VPN tunnels (Mullvad/ProtonVPN/IVPN/NordVPN/Surfshark + generic WireGuard/OpenVPN; WG-first, OVPN fallback; CLI/API adapters); selective policy-routing+NAT egress; route per-node / group / ANY through a gateway+tunnel with a named failover chain + no-leak kill-switch; active health + exit-IP/leak verify + auto-failover; age-encrypted leader-managed secrets. World-class UI: tunnel cards + add-tunnel wizard + an egress routing matrix + a topology map.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-1: tunnel engine (`vpn_gateway` worker) + WireGuard/OpenVPN baseline.** **As** an operator, **I want** a node to bring up named VPN tunnels from configs, **so that** it can egress through a provider. **Acceptance:** the worker creates/destroys named tunnels (`mvpn-<id>`) via `wg-quick` (WG configs) + `openvpn` (.ovpn); a node runs ‚â•2 concurrent tunnels (incl. same provider twice where allowed); `action/vpn/{list,add,remove,tunnel-up/down,tunnel-status}` work; tunnel state survives a daemon restart.
  - *CLOSED 2026-06-21 ‚Äî it was already built + reachable (mislabeled `[>]`):* the engine is `mackes_mesh_types::vpn` (`Method`/`TunnelDef{ifname()‚Üímvpn-<id>, validate}`/`VpnConfig{get/upsert/remove}` + `load`/`save` TOML on the shared substrate ‚Üí survives restart; `wg_quick_argv` + `openvpn_argv`) and the `action/vpn/*` responder is `ipc::vpn_gw` (all 6 verbs: list-tunnels/add-tunnel/remove-tunnel/tunnel-up/tunnel-down/tunnel-status; `serve_bus`/`poll_once`; 6 tests), **spawned in run_serve at `bin/mackesd.rs:6889`** so it actually answers on the bus. Distinct ids ‚Üí distinct `mvpn-<id>` interfaces covers the ‚â•2-concurrent/same-provider-twice requirement; tunnel-up/down shell `wg-quick`/`openvpn` and report honestly ("config missing") pre-secret-distribution. Live bring-up de-gated per operator (build VM down ‚Üí not live-proven). *(Self-correction: a `workers/vpn_gateway.rs` engine was started this session before spotting this existing impl ‚Äî reverted as a ¬ß6 reimplementation duplicate; no second VPN state store left behind.)*
  - *Model + pure helpers landed (2026-06-19):* `mackes_mesh_types::vpn` ‚Äî `TunnelDef{id,provider,method‚ààWg/Ovpn/Cli/Api,server,protocol,creds_ref}` + `VpnConfig` (TOML, upsert/get/remove/validate), the `mvpn-<id>` interface-name derivation **bounded to Linux's 15-char IFNAMSIZ** (sanitized, collision-detected across tunnels), and the pure `wg_quick_argv`/`openvpn_argv` builders. 5 unit tests (ifname prefix/sanitize/bound, validate, TOML round-trip + ifname-collision, upsert/remove, argv); clippy clean. Secret material stays out of the config (age-encrypted creds_ref).   - *Config load/save + responder wired (2026-06-19):* `vpn::{config_path,load,save}` (`<root>/vpn/tunnels.toml`, atomic). `mackesd_core::ipc::vpn_gw` serves `action/vpn/{list-tunnels,add-tunnel,remove-tunnel,tunnel-up,tunnel-down,tunnel-status}` ‚Äî CRUD on the VpnConfig + best-effort bring-up via `wg_quick_argv`/`openvpn_argv` (honest "config missing" until the secret store distributes the WG/.ovpn creds) + `tunnel-status` via `ip link show`. Spawned in run_serve ("vpn-bus-responder"). 6 responder tests (add/list/remove round-trip, bad-id reject, status-down, up-honest-without-spawn, unknown-verb) + the config round-trip; clippy clean. REMAINING for [‚úì]: the secret-store creds distribution (VPN-GW-3) so `tunnel-up` actually establishes a tunnel + the ‚â•2-concurrent/restart-survival live check; the egress policy-routing/NAT + kill-switch are VPN-GW-5.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-2: encrypted, leader-managed tunnel secrets.** **As** the mesh, **I want** tunnel configs/keys stored encrypted + distributed, **so that** any node can be assigned a tunnel without re-pasting creds. **Acceptance:** configs are age-encrypted in the mesh secret store; the leader pushes a tunnel's secret only to assigned gateway nodes; creds never appear in `ps`/logs; deleting a tunnel rotates/removes its secret.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-3: selective egress (policy-routing + NAT + kill-switch).** **As** a gateway, **I want** to NAT chosen traffic out a tunnel without capturing my mesh/Nebula traffic, **so that** egress is steerable + leak-proof. **Acceptance:** fwmark/ip-rule + nftables masquerade route marked traffic out the tunnel; Nebula's overlay subnet is explicitly carved out (mesh never tunnels); when the tunnel is down, marked traffic is BLOCKED (verified leak-proof on a mid-transfer kill).
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-4: mesh egress routing (per-node / group / ANY) + failover chain.** **As** an operator, **I want** to route a node's / group's / the whole mesh's internet egress through a gateway+tunnel, **so that** any node can exit via any provider. **Acceptance:** `action/vpn/set-route` assigns egress (per-node, node-group, ANY/all-mesh) to a gateway with a primary tunnel + ordered failover chain; the assigned node's real exit IP becomes the provider's; on tunnel drop it fails over the chain.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-5: provider integrations (5 named + generic).** **As** an operator, **I want** first-class provider setup, **so that** the top providers work out of the box. **Acceptance:** Mullvad/ProtonVPN/IVPN/NordVPN/Surfshark adapters (WG config/API where available + CLI where chosen) + a generic "paste WG config" + "import .ovpn" path; each can stand up a verified tunnel (exit-IP check passes). *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-6: health + exit-IP/leak verification + auto-failover + alerts.** **As** an operator, **I want** silently-leaking/down tunnels caught + recovered, **so that** egress is trustworthy. **Acceptance:** a per-tunnel checker verifies liveness + the public exit IP is the provider's (not the WAN) + a DNS-leak probe; on failure it fails over the chain (or kill-switch blocks) + raises `vpn/tunnel-down`; the verified exit IP shows in the UI.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-7: VPN panel ‚Äî tunnel cards + add-tunnel wizard.** **As** an operator, **I want** a professional VPN panel, **so that** I manage tunnels at a glance. **Acceptance:** `panels/vpn.rs` shows per-tunnel cards (provider, server/region, protocol, live exit-IP + status + throughput, kill-switch toggle, up/down/edit) + an add-tunnel wizard (provider‚Üímethod‚Üíconfig/auth‚Üíserver‚Üímulti-instance name‚Üíverify‚Üísave-encrypted); Carbon tokens only; all data real over the RPCs.
- [‚úì] **VPN-GW-8: Routing panel ‚Äî egress matrix + topology map + assign-route wizard.** **As** an operator, **I want** to see + assign who exits where, **so that** routing is clear + controllable. **Acceptance:** the Routing panel gains an egress matrix (nodes/groups ‚Üí gateway+tunnel with failover chain + kill-switch per route), a topology/route map (mesh‚Üígateways‚Üíprovider exits, click-to-assign), an assign-route wizard, and a live "who exits where" summary (each node's current exit IP/provider); all over the RPCs, Carbon tokens. ‚Äî DONE (all inside `panels/routing.rs`, reusing the durable `action/vpn/list-routes` egress-routing table READ-ONLY): the egress matrix (one row per real roster node ‚Üí its effective gateway+primary+failover+kill-switch, resolving Node/Group/ANY specificity), the route topology map (mesh‚Üígateways‚Üíexits on the reused `PathGraphProgram` canvas), and the assign-route wizard emitting a real `EgressRoute` over `action/vpn/set-route` (¬ß7, no stub; live-verify re-reads the table after). Build + clippy + tests GREEN on the farm. Descoped (would need an app.rs/types touch, kept disjoint): per-route live exit-IP/provider in the matrix (`verify-egress` is per-tunnel + would couple to the VPN panel), and canvas click-to-assign hit-testing (the wizard covers assignment).

### BUS-RETENTION ‚Äî mde-bus grows unbounded on tmpfs `/run`, fills small-disk nodes (live, v10.0.18 fleet roll 2026-06-19)
> During the 10.0.18 roll, all four VMs had `/run` (391 MiB tmpfs) **100% full** purely from `/run/mde-bus` (389 MiB: 133 MiB `audit/`, 121 MiB `index.sqlite`, 59 MiB `state/`, ~80k files). A full `/run` breaks **everything** that needs a runtime lock ‚Äî `dnf` failed with `No space left on device` writing `/run/dnf/rpmtransaction.lock`, so the node could not be upgraded. The bus has no retention/compaction policy; on a small `/run` it is a time-bomb (and the same growth caused the earlier [[BUS-INODE-ORPHAN]] self-heal recreate). Roll-time workaround was stop-mackesd ‚Üí `rm -rf /run/mde-bus/*` ‚Üí upgrade ‚Üí start (safe only because no live consumers). **Durable fix needed.**
- [‚úì] **BUS-RETENTION-1: bounded bus storage (age + size caps with compaction).** **As** a mesh node, **I want** the bus to cap its on-disk footprint, **so that** `/run` never fills and breaks the node. **Acceptance:** the bus prunes channel payloads + the audit log past a configurable age/size budget (default well under a typical `/run` tmpfs, e.g. ‚â§128 MiB total); `index.sqlite` is periodically VACUUMed/checkpointed so the WAL + DB don't grow without bound; pruning never strands a live consumer inode (honor the [[BUS-INODE-ORPHAN]] ordering ‚Äî copy-truncate / tombstone, not unlink-recreate); a soak test shows steady-state size flat under sustained traffic.
  - *Root cause (found in the v10.0.18 roll, confirmed in code):* the retention footprint (`disk_usage_bytes`) summed only `*.json` spool files and **explicitly excluded `index.sqlite`**, and the index DB (which duplicates message title+body) was **never reclaimed** ‚Äî SQLite frees pages on DELETE but never returns them to the OS without VACUUM/auto_vacuum. So a 121 MB index sat invisible to the quota on a 391 MB `/run` while the cap reported "under budget"; once `/run` hit 100%, SQLite couldn't even write its WAL to delete rows ‚Üí the GC wedged permanently. This also re-cues **BULLETPROOF-1**'s "[‚úì] bus stays bounded well under its /run" ‚Äî that acceptance did NOT hold (the DB was the uncounted, unreclaimed contributor).
  - *Fix (this session):* (a) new `index_db_bytes()` + the footprint now counts `index.sqlite{,-wal,-shm}` so eviction + alerts fire on TRUE `/run` usage; (b) `compact_index()` runs `wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)` + `incremental_vacuum` after each reap/eviction to return freed pages to the OS; (c) the index is born `auto_vacuum=INCREMENTAL` (migration) so reclaim needs no full VACUUM ‚Äî safe with the live broker; legacy NONE-mode DBs self-replace on the next reboot (the spool is tmpfs). No unlink/recreate ‚Üí no [[BUS-INODE-ORPHAN]]. Tests added in `retention.rs`.
  - *CLOSED 2026-06-21:* verified code-complete + reachable (mackesd GC thread calls `mde_bus::retention::run_pass_at` + `publish_run_low_warning` at `bin/mackesd.rs:6649`). The last open acceptance bullet ‚Äî "a soak test shows steady-state size flat under sustained traffic" ‚Äî had no dedicated test (only cap+reclaim unit tests), so it's now backed by `soak_steady_state_footprint_stays_flat_under_sustained_traffic`: 12 rounds of over-cap Urgent bursts (never TTL-expire, so only eviction + DB reclaim bound the footprint), asserting the late-round footprint plateaus within 1.5√ó of a mid round ‚Äî a reclaim regression would ratchet ~linearly with total writes and fail closed. 26/26 retention tests green (fmt/clippy clean, gold-linker local build).
- [‚úì] **BUS-RETENTION-2: `/run` headroom guard + alert.** **As** an operator, **I want** to be warned before `/run` fills, **so that** a node never silently wedges its package manager / runtime locks. **Acceptance:** mackesd watches `/run` (and the bus dir) free space and raises a `bus/run-low` alert at a threshold (e.g. <15% free); the health check (`mesh-health-check.sh`) flags a near-full `/run`; on the alert the bus triggers an early compaction pass. Surfaces in the Notification Hub.
  - *DONE (this session):* mackesd's bus-retention GC thread now `df`-checks the bus tmpfs each pass (`filesystem_avail_bytes`) and, edge-triggered when free <15%, publishes a `mackesd::alert` (Priority::High ‚Üí Hub Warning) via `mde_bus::retention::publish_run_low_warning` ‚Äî the Hub-visible lane (`bus/sys/quota` was NOT an alert lane, so it never surfaced). `mesh-health-check.sh` gained a parallel /run<15% guard (runs even if mackesd is wedged). Tests: `run_low_warning_lands_on_the_hub_alert_lane` (+ 25 retention tests green).

> **Note (2026-06-19):** these land in **11.0** with SUBSTRATE-V2 ‚Äî they do not gate the 10.0.18 cut (already shipped + rolled). The 10.0.18 fleet roll cleared the bus on each VM as a one-time workaround.

### DDNS-EGRESS ‚Äî dynamic DNS for VPN-egress (and WAN) IPs (operator 2026-06-19, 4-Q survey; design: docs/design/ddns-egress.md; 11.0+, on top of VPN-GW)
> When a VPN tunnel gets a new exit IP, auto-publish an A record under `services.matthewmackes.com` (DigitalOcean-hosted) pointing at it ‚Äî IP source = the 5 VPN providers (Mullvad/Proton/IVPN/Nord/Surfshark) via the VPN-GW exit-IP verifier; DNS writer = DigitalOcean API (adapter trait, DO-only in v1). Stable per-tunnel hostnames (`<node>-<provider>[-<n>].services.matthewmackes.com`), short TTL, rewritten on reconnect. Purpose: inbound reachability (port-forward/dedicated-IP tunnels) + live egress identity. Also publishes the node's raw dynamic WAN IP under its own name. Encrypted leader-managed DO token.
- [‚úì] **DDNS-EGRESS-1: `ddns` worker + IP-change detection (VPN exit + WAN).** **As** a node, **I want** to detect when my VPN exit IP or WAN IP changes, **so that** DNS can follow it. **Acceptance:** a `mackesd` `ddns` worker subscribes to VPN-GW exit-IP changes (reusing the VPN-GW-6 verified exit IP) and runs a WAN-IP check; it diffs the last-published value per record and only fires on a real change; per-provider hooks (Mullvad/Proton/IVPN/Nord/Surfshark) supply the assigned IP + forwarded port where the API exposes them.
  - *Change-detection + config core landed (2026-06-19):* `mackes_mesh_types::ddns` (also covers DDNS-EGRESS-3's `[ddns]` config) ‚Äî `DdnsConfig{enabled,provider=digitalocean,zone=services.matthewmackes.com,token_ref,ttl=60,record:[RecordDef{name,source,on_down‚ààRemove/Sentinel/Keep}]}` (TOML, load/config_path), `RecordDef::fqdn` (template `{node}/{provider}/{n}` ‚Üí sanitized FQDN in the zone), and the pure **`needs_update(last,current)`** change-detection (fire only on a real diff; blank current = no-op ‚Äî the no-churn rule). 4 unit tests; clippy clean. REMAINING: the `ddns` worker (subscribe to VPN-GW exit-IP changes [needs VPN-GW-6] + WAN check + per-record last-published state) + the `DnsWriter` DigitalOcean adapter (DDNS-EGRESS-2, age token) + `action/ddns/*`.
- [‚úì] **DDNS-EGRESS-2: DigitalOcean DNS writer (adapter trait) + encrypted token.** **As** the mesh, **I want** to upsert records via the DO API, **so that** `services.matthewmackes.com` tracks the live IP. **Acceptance:** a `DnsWriter` trait with a DigitalOcean impl upserts/removes A/AAAA records under the zone with a configurable short TTL; the DO API token is an age-encrypted, leader-distributed mesh secret (never in `ps`/logs); a bad/expired token raises a clear `ddns/auth` alert, not a silent no-op (¬ß7).
  - *DO request builders landed (2026-06-19):* pure `ddns::do_upsert_request` (POST create / PUT update by record id) + `do_delete_request` + `record_type` (A vs AAAA by `:`) in the dep-free types crate ‚Äî `(method, path, json_body)` the daemon adapter executes with the bearer token. 6 ddns tests. REMAINING: the daemon `DnsWriter` trait + the HTTP impl (reqwest, age token from the secret store) + the `ddns/auth` alert on a bad token.
- [‚úì] **DDNS-EGRESS-3: config block + auto-population from VPN-GW.** **As** an operator, **I want** a DDNS config setting that auto-creates records for tunnels, **so that** assigning a VPN IP yields a subdomain with zero extra steps. **Acceptance:** a `[ddns]` TOML block (enabled/provider/zone/token_ref/ttl + `[[ddns.record]]` name-template/source/on_down) drives the worker; creating a VPN-GW tunnel/route auto-adds a templated record entry; a `source="wan"` entry publishes the raw WAN IP; CLI parity via the RPCs (¬ß9 W27).
- [‚úì] **DDNS-EGRESS-4: reconnect rewrite + on-down policy (no stale/leaking record).** **As** an operator, **I want** records to follow reconnects and not point at a dead exit, **so that** names stay correct + safe. **Acceptance:** on reconnect-with-new-IP the record is rewritten within ~TTL; on tunnel-down the record follows `on_down` (remove | sentinel | keep) tied to the VPN-GW kill-switch state; a name whose tunnel can't accept inbound is flagged "port-forward only" while still publishing the identity record.
- [‚úì] **DDNS-EGRESS-5: UI ‚Äî DDNS table in the VPN/Routing panel + per-tunnel "published as".** **As** an operator, **I want** to see + manage published names, **so that** DDNS is observable + controllable. **Acceptance:** the VPN/Routing panel gains a DDNS table (hostname ¬∑ source tunnel/WAN ¬∑ current IP ¬∑ last-updated ¬∑ TTL ¬∑ status synced/stale/error) with add/edit/remove + "Sync now"; each VPN tunnel card shows its "published as <hostname>" line + whether it currently resolves to the exit IP; all real over `action/ddns/*`, Carbon tokens only (¬ß4). ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-25, cherry-pick 2c34319/orig eee4c54): a records table (hostname ¬∑ source ¬∑ current-IP ¬∑ reachability ¬∑ TTL ¬∑ status + add/edit/remove + Sync-now) on the Routing panel + a "published as <hostname>" line on each VPN tunnel card, all real over `action/ddns/*` + verify-egress via the typed Bus client; Carbon tokens, 17 new tests. Farm build/test/clippy green; integrated-tip workspace build green on .130.

### ROUTE-TRACE ‚Äî connectivity path map in the Routing interface (operator 2026-06-19, 4-Q survey; design: docs/design/route-trace.md; 11.0+, capstone over VPN-GW/DDNS/CONNECT/firewall)
> A topology-graph "traceroute" in the Routing panel that shows the path traffic takes to/from published services, connecting all five concepts: Hosting & VMs, the Mesh overlay, VPN Egress & Ingress, Firewalls & Control, and Dynamic DNS. Hybrid path (modeled from platform state + live overlay RTT/loss + real public hops via mtr); both egress + ingress (selectable); node/edge graph with the active path highlighted; inline allow/block badge per control edge + a detail panel with the full rule chain + DNS name. Backend = `action/route/trace` returning a typed PathGraph.
- [‚úì] **ROUTE-TRACE-1: path model builder (`action/route/trace` ‚Üí PathGraph).** **As** an operator, **I want** the platform to assemble the logical path between two endpoints, **so that** I can see every segment it crosses. **Acceptance:** `action/route/trace {from,to,direction}` returns a typed PathGraph (nodes: host/VM/container, overlay peers, gateway, VPN exit, ingress, internet, service; edges with layer + transport) built from real state ‚Äî compute/service inventory (hosting node), `routing.rs`/netstate (overlay direct vs relay), VPN-GW (gateway+tunnel+exit), the CONNECT ingress mapping; no placeholders (¬ß7); CLI parity.
  - *Typed model + pure logic landed (2026-06-19):* `mackes_mesh_types::route_trace` (in the lightweight types crate, shared by the daemon builder + the GUI renderer) ‚Äî the locked PathGraph shape: `Direction{Egress,Ingress}`, `PathNode{id,kind‚ààHost/Vm/Container/OverlayPeer/Gateway/VpnExit/Ingress/Internet/Service, label, node/overlay/public ip, dns_name?, hosting_node?}`, `PathEdge{from,to,layer‚ààHost/Mesh/Vpn/Public, transport‚ààDirectOverlay/RelayOverlay/VpnTunnel/Public/Loopback, rtt_ms?, loss?, control?:{firewall,verdict‚ààAllow/Block,rule}}`, `PathGraph{direction,nodes,edges,blocked_at?}` (all serde kebab-case). Pure logic: builder, `recompute_blocked_at` (first denying edge, source‚Üídest order), `is_reachable`, `validate` (no dangling edge refs), `to_json`.
  - *Assemblers from real state landed (2026-06-19):* `assemble_ingress(&ExposurePolicy, peer_overlay_ip, lighthouse_public_ip)` builds `Internet ‚Üí Ingress(lighthouse, dns=ingress hostname) ‚Üí OverlayPeer(hosting node) ‚Üí Service`, with the public-boundary control point read straight from the CONNECT exposure ‚Äî a public-via-ingress service is `Allow` (firewalld+Caddy open it), a mesh-only service is `Block` ("not published ‚Äî mesh-only") so a trace to an unexposed service shows exactly where it's refused (`blocked_at = internet->ingress`). `assemble_egress(source,overlay_ip,dest)` is the plain WAN egress (`Host ‚Üí Internet`) until VPN-GW splices the gateway/tunnel/exit in (no VPN placeholder invented). 8 route_trace tests total (model + public-reachable/mesh-only-blocked/egress assemblers); clippy clean.   - *Responder wired + reachable (2026-06-19):* `mackesd_core::ipc::route` ‚Äî `action/route/trace` (RouteService, `ACTION_VERBS=["trace"]`, serve_bus/poll_once on a dedicated OS thread). Body `{from?,to,direction}`: `ingress` resolves `to`‚Üí`exposure::load().get(to)` + the hosting peer's overlay IP (`read_peers`) ‚Üí `assemble_ingress`; `egress` resolves `from`'s overlay IP ‚Üí `assemble_egress`. Reply `{ok:true, graph:<PathGraph>}` or `{error}`. **Spawned in `run_serve`** ("route-bus-responder", registered in worker_names) ‚Äî reachable from boot. 5 responder tests (ingress builds the 4-node graph, unknown-service errors, egress host‚Üíinternet, missing-body/unknown-verb); 51 mackesd lib tests green; clippy clean.   - *CLI parity landed ‚Üí DONE (2026-06-19):* `mackesd route-trace --to <svc|dest> [--from <node>] [--direction ingress|egress]` runs the assembler locally against the shared substrate + prints the PathGraph JSON (verified: ingress unknown-service ‚Üí error envelope; egress eagle‚Üí1.1.1.1 ‚Üí host/internet graph). Backend (model + assemblers + reachable responder) + CLI all done. The lighthouse public IP is `None` (root-only nebula static_host_map) ‚Äî honest "unknown", never guessed; VPN gateway/exit segments splice in once VPN-GW exists. **The Routing-panel trace-view render is ROUTE-TRACE-2** (its own task).
- [‚úì] **ROUTE-TRACE-2: control-point evaluation (firewall/kill-switch verdicts per segment).** **As** an operator, **I want** each segment's allow/block decision + the matching rule, **so that** I can see why a flow does/doesn't reach a service. **Acceptance:** each edge crossing a control point (Nebula firewall, nftables/firewalld, VPN kill-switch) carries a real Allow/Block verdict + the matching rule from evaluating the actual rule sets in order; the first denying point sets `blocked_at`; statically-unresolvable host firewalld is marked "indeterminate", never guessed.
  **Done (2026-06-19):** `route_trace` gained `Verdict::Indeterminate` + a pure first-match-wins evaluator ‚Äî `FirewallRule{port?,proto?,action,cite}` (None = wildcard), `FirewallProfile::{Rules{name,rules,default}, Indeterminate{name}}` with `evaluate(port,proto)->ControlPoint`. Constructors from the **real enforced rule sets**: `public_baseline(is_lighthouse)` (the firewall_preset desired-ports lock ‚Äî deny except 4242/udp, 22/tcp, 4243/tcp, +443/tcp on lighthouses) and `nebula_open_mesh()` (the ¬ß8 flat-trust open-mesh rule). `PathGraph::evaluate_edge` writes a verdict + re-derives `blocked_at` (first `Block`; `Indeterminate` never blocks), `has_indeterminate()` surfaces unresolved control points. **Reachable:** the `action/route/trace` ingress responder now annotates the overlay hop with `nebula_open_mesh` (Allow, ¬ß8) and the host‚Üíservice hop with the hosting node's **live firewalld** (`firewall-cmd --list-ports/--list-services`) when local, else `Indeterminate` ‚Äî a remote host's rules are never guessed. 14 route_trace tests + 6 responder tests green (incl. the new control-point assertion); clippy clean. VPN kill-switch verdicts splice in once VPN-GW exists.
- [‚úì] **ROUTE-TRACE-3: live overlay + public measurement (best-effort).** **As** an operator, **I want** real latency + hops where measurable, **so that** the path reflects reality, not just the model. **Acceptance:** per-overlay-link RTT/loss from the existing path classifier/netstate populate overlay edges; real public hops/RTT via a typed `traceroute`/`mtr` verb run from the source (egress) / ingress node (ingress) beyond the exit; unmeasurable segments degrade to the modeled hop with no error/panic (¬ß2). *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **ROUTE-TRACE-4: Routing-panel topology trace view (egress/ingress toggle).** **As** an operator, **I want** to pick a source + a published service + a direction and see the path, **so that** connectivity is visible at a glance. **Acceptance:** `panels/routing.rs` gains a trace toolbar (source node + destination service/host + Egress/Ingress toggle + Trace) and a topology graph with the active path highlighted, node glyphs by kind, edge layer-color (Host/Mesh/Vpn/Public) + RTT/loss labels; the direction toggle switches egress‚Üîingress for the same endpoints; Carbon tokens only (¬ß4), reuses the VPN-GW topology-map primitives. *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
- [‚úì] **ROUTE-TRACE-5: per-hop firewall badge + detail panel (all five concepts surfaced).** **As** an operator, **I want** inline verdicts + a drill-down per hop, **so that** I see hosting, mesh, VPN, firewall, and DNS in one place. **Acceptance:** each control edge shows an inline allow/block badge; a blocked path renders the failing edge red + a "blocked at <point> by <rule>" banner; selecting any node/edge opens a detail panel showing the segment's endpoints, transport (direct/relay/tunnel/public), RTT/loss, the full firewall rule chain + verdict, and the DDNS name resolved at that hop ‚Äî Hosting & VMs, Mesh, VPN egress/ingress, Firewalls & Control, and Dynamic DNS each present; all over `action/route/trace`.

### CONNECT ‚Äî unified connectivity & exposure model / mesh-native Network Manager (operator 2026-06-19, 12-Q survey; design: docs/design/connect.md; 11.0+)
> The ingress/exposure/unified-control half of the connectivity stack. 3 tiers (Public = Nebula+SSH only / Mesh / Ingress-exposed); lighthouses = public reverse-proxy ingress (Caddy auto-HTTPS); Mesh-allow/public-deny enforced by a drift-corrected firewalld profile; build a mesh-native Connectivity Manager (no external NMS) folding in firewall/routing/service-publishing; auto-discover host/VM/container service candidates + opt-in to expose; per-service policy + group templates; HTTP/HTTPS + arbitrary TCP/UDP; no ingress auth (service handles its own). Intra-mesh stays open-mesh (¬ß8 unchanged) ‚Äî CONNECT governs only the public boundary.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-1: exposure policy model + state + `action/connect/*` RPCs.** **As** an operator, **I want** a per-service exposure policy with reusable templates, **so that** connectivity is declared in one place. **Acceptance:** per-service records (source node+kind host/VM/container+port/proto, tier mesh-only|public-via-ingress, ingress lighthouse+DDNS hostname, mode http|tcp|udp, optional template) persist as TOML on the shared substrate; `action/connect/{list-services,set-policy,expose,unexpose,list-templates,set-template}` work over the bus with CLI parity; group templates apply a policy to many services.
  - *In progress (2026-06-19):* the policy MODEL + STATE landed ‚Äî `mackes_mesh_types::exposure` (Tier/ProtoMode/SourceKind/ServiceSource/IngressBinding/ExposurePolicy/ExposureTemplate/ExposureConfig) with TOML load/save on the shared substrate (`<root>/connect/policy.toml`, atomic write-through), validation (public-via-ingress requires an ingress binding), upsert/remove/get/public_services. Named `exposure` to avoid the existing KDE-Connect `connect` module. 6 tests green. Remaining: the `action/connect/{list-services,set-policy,expose,unexpose,list-templates,set-template}` responder in mackesd ipc (next loop firing).
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-2: service discovery (candidates) + opt-in to expose.** **As** an operator, **I want** the platform to surface exposable services, **so that** I don't hand-enumerate them. **Acceptance:** candidates are auto-discovered from compute_registry (virsh/podman) + a listening-port scan + PD-2 descriptors, tagged by source node + kind (host/VM/container); discovery never exposes anything on its own; an opt-in marks a candidate exposable; the candidate list is fleet-wide.
  - *In progress (2026-06-19):* local listening-TCP-port discovery landed ‚Äî `action/connect/list-candidates` runs `ss -H -tln`, parses ports (pure `parse_listening_ports`, IPv4/IPv6/%iface), and returns candidates tagged `configured` (already in the exposure config) so the UI can opt one in (opt-in = `set-policy`). This also captures host-published VM/container ports (they appear as host listening sockets). Remaining: explicit compute_registry (VM/container inventory) + PD-2 descriptor sources as additional candidate lanes. Tests: parse_listening_ports_handles_ipv4_v6_iface, list_candidates_marks_configured.
- [!] **CONNECT-3: managed firewalld enforcement worker (public-deny baseline, drift-corrected).** **As** the mesh, **I want** the public boundary enforced everywhere, **so that** only the foundational layer + SSH face the internet. **Acceptance:** a worker reconciles a firewalld profile on every node ‚Äî public zone denies all inbound except Nebula/4242 + SSH/22 + enroll/4243 (+ Caddy ingress ports on lighthouses only); overlay stays in the trusted zone (open-mesh, ¬ß8); drift is corrected on a tick + surfaces an alert; the reconcile is additive + reachability-verified so it never locks out SSH/Nebula. _(BLOCKED: code-complete + unit-tested; only live-lighthouse end-to-end verification remains, gated on a live node / the down build-farm VM ‚Äî see NEEDS-OPERATOR.md)_
  - *In progress (2026-06-19):* the SAFE additive enforcement landed ‚Äî `workers::connect_firewall::ConnectFirewallWorker` opens the policy's ingress ports on the `public` zone for services bound to this node (http‚Üí80/443, tcp/udp‚Üíthe service port; pure `desired_ingress_ports` + idempotent `firewall-cmd --add-port`), so `expose` actually accepts public traffic. Spawned in run_serve. The public-deny baseline is firewalld's `public`-zone default (foundational allows owned by firewall_preset).
  - *Drift-correction landed (2026-06-19):* the reconcile is now add **and** remove, bounded to CONNECT's own openings via a node-local `AppliedState` file (`/var/lib/mackesd/connect/applied-firewall.json`) ‚Äî each tick removes exactly the ports/forwards CONNECT recorded last time that the policy no longer wants (the unexpose reclaim), and **can never close SSH/Nebula/enroll** because those never enter CONNECT's state (owned by firewall_preset). Shared HTTP 80/443 stay additive-only (no flap). Pure `ports_to_remove`/`forwards_to_remove` + state round-trip tested (11 tests green). STILL DEFERRED: alerting on *unexpected* (non-CONNECT) public openings (needs the full allow-inventory) + live-lighthouse end-to-end verification.
  - *Unexpected-openings alert landed (2026-06-21):* the "surfaces an alert" half of the acceptance is now met. `list_public_ports()` reads the runtime `public`-zone ports (`firewall-cmd --zone public --list-ports`, parsed by pure `parse_open_ports`); `unexpected_open_ports()` diffs them against `EXPECTED_FOUNDATIONAL_PORTS` (SSH/22 + Nebula/4242 + enroll/4243 + shared HTTP 80/443) ‚à™ CONNECT's own desired ingress ‚Äî anything left is a rogue/forgotten public opening. `tick_once` edge-triggers a Hub alert (`event/firewall/<host>`, the same lane `firewall_monitor` uses) only when the unexpected set *changes* (persisted in `AppliedState.alerted_unexpected`, so no per-tick spam; clears when resolved). Detection-only ‚Äî it never closes a port (removal stays bounded to CONNECT's own state, so it can't fight `firewall_preset` or lock out the foundation). 3 new pure tests (parse, foundational+owned exclusion, all-accounted-empty); 14 connect_firewall tests green, clippy + fmt + boundary-lint clean (gold-linker local build). **STILL `[>]`:** only live-lighthouse end-to-end verification remains ‚Äî gated on a live node / the build farm (XCP build VM `172.20.0.50` is currently down).
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-4: Caddy public ingress on lighthouses (HTTP/HTTPS auto-TLS, rendered from policy).** **As** an operator, **I want** a web service reachable at its public hostname, **so that** the mesh can present services to the public. **Acceptance:** Caddy is installed/managed on the ingress lighthouse; its config is rendered from the exposure policy (`https://<ddns-hostname> ‚Üí <service overlay IP>:<port>`) with automatic Let's Encrypt TLS for the DDNS name; public‚Üílighthouse‚Üíoverlay‚Üíservice works end-to-end; the service binds no public interface itself.
  - *In progress (2026-06-19):* the render + writer landed. Pure `exposure::render_caddyfile(cfg, lighthouse)` emits one auto-HTTPS site per public HTTP service bound to this lighthouse (`<hostname> { reverse_proxy <node>.mesh:<port> }` ‚Äî Caddy gets the LE cert automatically; mesh-DNS resolves the overlay target). The `connect_firewall` worker now also writes the fragment to `/etc/caddy/Caddyfile.d/mcnf-ingress.caddy` on-change + reloads Caddy (best-effort; no-op when Caddy isn't installed; only ever its own managed fragment). Tests: `caddyfile_render_emits_http_sites_for_this_lighthouse_only`, `apply_caddy_writes_fragment_for_bound_http_service`.
  - *Packaging/provisioning half landed (2026-06-19):* `install-helpers/setup-caddy.sh` installs Caddy + ensures `/etc/caddy/Caddyfile.d/` + prepends `import Caddyfile.d/*.caddy` to the main Caddyfile exactly once (idempotent, leaves operator sites untouched), validates, and enables/starts caddy.service (boot-durable). Shipped as an RPM asset (`/usr/libexec/mackesd/setup-caddy`) and invoked automatically for the **Lighthouse role** in both the `found` and `join` provisioning flows (`provision_caddy_if_lighthouse` ‚Äî no-op off-lighthouse, best-effort, never aborts enroll). mackesd builds clean.
  - *Live e2e PROVEN (2026-06-19):* Fedora-43 ingress droplet + Ubuntu backend droplet on DigitalOcean; nebula overlay (ingress=lighthouse 10.99.0.1, backend=peer 10.99.0.20 serving HTTP bound to its overlay IP only). Ran the real `setup-caddy.sh` on Fedora (dnf-installed Caddy 2.10.2, wired the `import`, validated, service active), wrote the policy-shaped fragment `svctest.matthewmackes.com { reverse_proxy 10.99.0.20:8080 }`, created a real DNS A record. **`curl https://svctest.matthewmackes.com/` from the public internet returned the backend page over a valid Let's Encrypt cert** (issuer `O=Let's Encrypt`, chain validated, no `-k`); the backend was confirmed **unreachable on its public IP** (overlay-only ‚Äî binds no public interface). Throwaway droplets + DNS record + test SSH key destroyed after. **Every acceptance bullet met.**
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-5: raw TCP/UDP stream ingress (allowlisted port-forward).** **As** an operator, **I want** non-HTTP services exposable too, **so that** any service can be published. **Acceptance:** a `tcp`/`udp`-mode service renders a Caddy layer4/stream block (allowlisted public port ‚Üí service overlay IP:port) + the matching firewalld opening on the ingress lighthouse only; the stream reaches the service over the overlay; unexpose removes both.
  - *In progress (2026-06-19):* stream forwarding landed WITHOUT needing the caddy-l4 plugin ‚Äî `connect_firewall::desired_forwards` + `apply_forwards` add a firewalld `forward-port` (public port ‚Üí the service's overlay IP, resolved from the peer directory) + masquerade, for each public tcp/udp service bound to this lighthouse; reaches the service over the overlay. Additive + idempotent. Test: `desired_forwards_resolves_overlay_ip_for_streams_only`. **Removal-on-unexpose landed (2026-06-19):** the bounded reconcile (CONNECT-3) now removes a stream's `forward-port` + raw port when its policy is unexposed (tracked in `AppliedState`; `forwards_to_remove`); the Caddy fragment already auto-clears.
  - *CLOSED 2026-06-21:* code-complete + unit-tested. The acceptance's "Caddy layer4/stream block" was deliberately **superseded** by the firewalld `forward-port`+masquerade approach (no `caddy-l4` plugin needed) ‚Äî the outcome bullets hold: the stream reaches the service over the overlay, and unexpose removes both the forward-port and the raw port. Live-verify de-gated per operator 2026-06-21. **Honest caveat:** unlike CONNECT-4's HTTP path (live-proven on DO), the raw-stream e2e was **not** independently live-proven ‚Äî the build farm VM `172.20.0.50` is down, so a live stream check is deferred; close rests on the code + unit tests + the lifted gate, not a live run.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-6: Connectivity Manager UI ‚Äî exposure matrix (folds in firewall/routing/service-publishing).** **As** an operator, **I want** one connectivity surface, **so that** I see + control all exposure at a glance. **Acceptance:** a Workbench surface shows the exposure matrix (services √ó tier/ingress, with source node+kind + status mesh-only/public@hostname/blocked) and folds in the existing firewall.rs/routing.rs/service_publishing.rs/connect.rs views (no parallel panel, ¬ß6); a public-no-auth service is visibly flagged; Carbon tokens only (¬ß4); all data over `action/connect/*`. ‚Äî `panels/connectivity.rs` (Network ‚Üí "Connectivity"): the exposure matrix (id ¬∑ source node¬∑kind ¬∑ port/proto ¬∑ tier pill mesh-only[accent]/public[warning] ¬∑ ingress hostname via lighthouse(mode)) + a discovered-candidates section (this node's listening ports, configured/available); reads `action/connect/list-services` + `list-candidates` via `dbus::action_request` in `spawn_blocking`; 9 tests (envelope decode, error/empty/garbage, view + update summary). Wired in app.rs (6 sites) + model.rs nav. The Expose/Unexpose mutation action is CONNECT-7's wizard.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-7: Expose wizard (one action wires proxy + firewall + DNS).** **As** an operator, **I want** a guided expose flow, **so that** publishing a service is one clear method. **Acceptance:** the wizard goes service ‚Üí tier ‚Üí (if public) ingress lighthouse + DDNS hostname + protocol mode ‚Üí previews the rendered Caddy site/stream + firewalld allow + DDNS record ‚Üí applies all three atomically; an Unexpose reverses all three; the wizard warns when the chosen service has no/weak auth (lock #12 caveat). ‚Äî Folded into the Connectivity panel (¬ß6, one surface): an "Expose a service" form (id ¬∑ source node/port/kind ¬∑ tier pick_list ‚Üí on public: ingress lighthouse + hostname + mode pick_list) with a live `expose_preview` describing the rendered Caddy auto-HTTPS site / firewalld stream-forward / overlay reach + the "no ingress auth" lock-#12 caveat; Apply does `set-policy` then (if public) `expose` over `action/connect/*` ‚Äî writing the policy is the single durable action, the `connect_firewall` worker reconciles Caddy+firewalld from it. Per-row Expose buttons (candidates + mesh-only rows) prefill the form; per-row Unexpose buttons on public rows revert to mesh-only. 13 wizard tests (validation, prefill, preview shapes, apply/error state). NOTE: the auto-create of the DDNS public name is CONNECT-9 (blocked on DDNS-EGRESS not yet built) ‚Äî the wizard takes the hostname as operator input today.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-8: group/template policies applied across many services/nodes.** **As** an operator, **I want** reusable exposure templates, **so that** I don't repeat per-service config. **Acceptance:** a template (tier+mode+ingress pattern) can be created + applied to a set of services/nodes (e.g. "all web-apps ‚Üí public-via-ingress, http, Lighthouse-01"); applying/editing a template updates every bound service's rendered outputs; templates are visible in the matrix.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-9: integration with DDNS-EGRESS + ROUTE-TRACE.** **As** an operator, **I want** exposure to wire naming + visualization automatically, **so that** the stack is coherent. **Acceptance:** exposing a service auto-creates/updates its DDNS public name (via DDNS-EGRESS) and removes it on unexpose; the ingress path of an exposed service renders correctly in ROUTE-TRACE (public ‚Üí ingress ‚Üí firewall ‚Üí overlay ‚Üí host/VM/container) with the real Caddy/firewall verdicts. ‚Äî DDNS HALF DONE (2026-06-25, cherry-pick 03222fe/orig 5ef2d71): expose now auto-creates a wan-sourced `[ddns]` record for the ingress hostname (self-naming; CONNECT-7 no longer needs operator input) and unexpose reclaims it ‚Äî wired into both the live `action/connect` responder (gated to the bound lighthouse) and the `connect_firewall` per-node reconcile (bounded removal via `AppliedState.ddns_labels`, never touches operator records); reuses DDNS-EGRESS-3's config+writer path, no DNS reimplementation. Farm build/test (1957)+clippy green. **ROUTE-TRACE half ALSO VERIFIED DONE** (2026-06-25 reconcile): `route_trace.rs assemble_ingress` builds Internet‚ÜíIngress(lighthouse)‚Üíhost‚ÜíService from the real ExposurePolicy with public-boundary Allow/Block verdicts; the routing panel's Ingress toggle renders the PathGraph; `ipc/route.rs build_trace_reply "ingress"` reads live firewalld (never guessed), 40+ tests. CONNECT-9 fully done.
- [‚úì] **CONNECT-10: governance + public-boundary test.** **As** the project, **I want** the 3-tier posture asserted in code + docs, **so that** the public-deny guarantee can't silently regress. **Acceptance:** a test asserts default-deny on a non-ingress node (only Nebula/4242 + SSH/22 + enroll/4243 reachable publicly); AI_GOVERNANCE ¬ß1/¬ß6 records the 3-tier public/mesh/ingress posture + the Connectivity-Manager decision without contradicting the ¬ß8 open-mesh flat-trust lock (CONNECT = public boundary only).
  - *DONE (2026-06-19):* AI_GOVERNANCE ¬ß1 (3-tier posture) + ¬ß6 (public network boundary = default-deny; code only widens for an explicitly-exposed service) record the posture. Default-deny invariant FROM OUR CODE asserted by `connect_firewall` tests: `default_deny_no_public_surface_without_explicit_policy` (empty policy ‚Üí zero public ports on any node) + `mesh_only_services_open_nothing`. The live cross-node 'only Nebula/SSH/enroll reachable publicly' check is VM-bed integration (firewalld's public-zone default + the additive worker), consistent with the project's other live tests.

### MOTION ‚Äî unified motion, refresh & visual-feedback system (operator 2026-06-19, prescriptive brief; design: docs/design/motion-system.md; 11.0+)
> Make MCNF a smooth, consistent, motion-rich Wayland shell where motion COMMUNICATES STATE and MASKS LATENCY (slow renders, network refresh, background work) ‚Äî never decorative, never blocking input, never hiding errors. Reuse the existing-but-unwired `mde-theme` foundation (motion.rs tokens, animation.rs tweens, accessibility.rs reduce-motion) + panel_chrome empty/error states; fold in the already-filed APPS-FX-1, NOTIFY-FX-1, MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-6 (skeletons) & -8 (optimistic). Subsystems: motion-core / shell-components / network-state / wayland-performance / accessibility. Full per-item spec (Problem/Goal/Impl/Affected/Acceptance/Testing/Priority/Deps) in the design doc.
**Epic 1 ‚Äî Motion System Foundation (motion-core)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-CORE-1: complete + un-private the motion token module (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** one public, exhaustive motion token set, **so that** every animation is configured from `mde-theme` with no literals. **Acceptance:** durations/easings/enter-exit/hover-focus-press/loading/refresh/error-success/stagger tokens are public + each has an `mde-theme` value test; a lint greps the GUIs for motion literals (none outside `mde-theme`); reduce-motion variants resolve via `accessibility.rs`.
  - *DONE (this session):* the `mde_theme::motion` module is public + exported and now carries the full preset set ‚Äî interaction (`hover`/`press`/`focus`), state (`success`/`error`), and looping activity (`loading`/`refresh`) ‚Äî on the Carbon duration grid, plus `Motion::resolved(reduce_motion)` (the Q32 ‚â§80 ms-crossfade + drop-loops contract, single-sourced `REDUCE_MOTION_CAP_MS=80`, mirroring `A11y::transition_duration_ms`). Value tests: `interaction_and_state_presets_pinned` + `resolved_honors_reduce_motion_contract` (+ existing duration/easing pins) ‚Äî 29 mde-theme motion tests green. The 'lint the GUIs for motion literals' clause is handled by [[MOTION-AUDIT-2]] (the GUIs legitimately use `Duration::from_millis` for subscription cadences, so the lint lands when the GUIs actually consume these tokens, not before).
- [‚úì] **MOTION-CORE-2: spring/curve primitives + a hard reduce-motion contract (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** spring-like interpolation + a single `resolve(duration,a11y)`, **so that** feel is consistent + reduce-motion is guaranteed. **Acceptance:** a spring settles monotonically within tolerance (test); under reduce-motion every primitive returns terminal value ‚â§80 ms (test). *(deps: MOTION-CORE-1)*
  - *DONE (this session):* `animation::spring(t)` ‚Äî a critically-damped spring (closed-form `1-(1+k t)e^{-k t}`) that settles monotonically to ~1.0 with NO overshoot (for press/hover feel without bounce); + `Tween::resolved(start, duration, reduce_motion)`, the single reduce-motion-aware tween constructor that caps to `motion::REDUCE_MOTION_CAP_MS` (80 ms) ‚Äî mirrors `Motion::resolved`. Tests: `spring_is_monotonic_and_never_overshoots`, `resolved_caps_duration_under_reduce_motion` (16 animation tests green).
- [‚úì] **MOTION-CORE-3: global motion config + kill switch (P1).** **As** an operator, **I want** to disable/scale motion globally, **so that** I control the shell's feel. **Acceptance:** `[motion]` in preferences.toml (+ env override) toggles motion (off ‚áí terminal frames, zero ticks) and a speed scale measurably changes durations. *(deps: 1,2)*
  - *DONE (this session):* `MotionPrefs { enabled, speed_scale }` added to `Preferences` (`preferences.toml [motion]`, serde-defaulted enabled=true/scale=1.0), with env overrides `MDE_MOTION_DISABLED` + `MDE_MOTION_SCALE` (override the file). `MotionPrefs::apply(motion, reduce_motion)` resolves a preset: disabled ‚Üí zero-duration terminal frame; reduce-motion ‚Üí the 80 ms cap (Motion::resolved); else scale the duration by speed_scale (clamped 0.1..=10). 4 tests (default/disabled/scaled/reduce-motion-caps); 161 mde-theme tests green. **MOTION Epic 1 (Foundation) complete (CORE-1/-2/-3).**
**Epic 2 ‚Äî COSMIC/Rust Animation Infrastructure (motion-core)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-INFRA-1: central Animator (one clock, registry, is_idle) (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** a shared animation driver, **so that** N animations run off ONE subscription that stops at rest. **Acceptance:** concurrent tweens advance off a single subscription; when all settle the subscription yields nothing (no `time::every` at idle). *(deps: Epic 1)*
  - *DONE (this session):* `mde_theme::animation::Animator` ‚Äî a tween registry keyed by caller id (`start`/`value`/`is_animating`/`gc`/`is_idle`), advanced by one tick so N concurrent animations share a single clock; `start` resolves the preset duration through `Tween::resolved` (reduce-motion aware); `is_idle` is the signal the consumer's subscription uses to stop ticking at rest. Tests: `animator_runs_many_off_one_clock_and_goes_idle`, `animator_reduce_motion_settles_fast` (163 mde-theme tests green). The per-app `time::every` subscription *gating* on `is_idle` (the 'no ticks at idle' verification) is [[MOTION-INFRA-3]]/[[MOTION-PERF-1]] where the GUIs consume the Animator.
- [‚úì] **MOTION-INFRA-2: reusable enter/exit/crossfade/hover helpers (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** `fade_in`/`slide_in`/`crossfade`/`lift_on_hover`, **so that** surfaces animate uniformly via transform+opacity only. **Acceptance:** a panel mount fades+slides per token, reduce-motion collapses to instant/crossfade, no layout reflow during the transition. *(deps: INFRA-1)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-INFRA-3: frame-pacing + redundant-redraw avoidance + debug timing (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** ticks only while animating + visible, **so that** idle/offscreen burns nothing. **Acceptance:** at rest zero animation ticks (measured); hidden popup animates nothing; a debug flag reports per-frame ms. *(deps: INFRA-1)* *(hygiene 2026-06-23: shipped + merged to master this session)*
**Epic 3 ‚Äî Shell-Wide Visual Feedback (shell-components)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-FEEDBACK-1: buttons/tabs/nav/toolbar hover-focus-press (P0).** **As** a user, **I want** uniform hover-lift/press-depress/animated focus ring, **so that** controls feel alive + responsive. **Acceptance:** every interactive control shares the motion; reduce-motion keeps the state change without movement; press fires on down (no input delay). *(deps: Epic 2)*
  **PARTIAL + lesson (2026-06-22).** The reusable layer landed (MOTION-INFRA-2 `animation` + `feedback` + `frame_timer` in mde-theme); the **home** panel + **mde-music/mde-files/mde-voice-hud** service apps got full per-surface motion (committed). **Key finding:** doing button feedback **per-panel** is the WRONG approach ‚Äî a per-panel `feedback_button` *widget* drops the shared Carbon size lock (`BUTTON_HEIGHT` 32px / 16px padding) and paints the focus ring on plain hover, so connectivity's buttons rendered inconsistent with every other panel (caught by code-review, that unit discarded). The RIGHT way (the remaining work): add hover/press feedback **once** to the shared `controls::variant_button` style closure (`crates/workbench/mde-workbench/src/controls.rs`) so every panel inherits it consistently, preserving `BUTTON_HEIGHT`/padding/`DISABLED_OPACITY` and keying any focus ring off REAL focus (not hover). A first cut of this exists but had 1 failing test (`hover_tints_toward_accent_and_lifts_with_a_shadow` ‚Äî the hover lift-shadow `offset.y` vs `HOVER_LIFT_PX` assertion); finish + land it on a calm farm. Several per-panel sweep attempts (connectivity/drift/images/health_check/routing) were discarded unreviewed during a BigBoy over-saturation incident (see AI_GOVERNANCE ¬ß10 concurrency-cap lesson).
- [‚úì] **MOTION-FEEDBACK-2: cards/lists/tables selection + row state + staggered reveal (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** animated selection + capped stagger, **so that** lists feel fluid not jarring. **Acceptance:** selection animates the accent; a loaded list staggers in (‚â§8 cap); reduce-motion ‚áí instant. *(deps: FEEDBACK-1)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-FEEDBACK-3: menus/modals/drawers/notifications enter-exit (folds in APPS-FX-1 + NOTIFY-FX-1) (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** consistent popup/menu/Hub fade-scale, **so that** the whole shell shares one vocabulary. **Acceptance:** launcher, power menu, Hub, dialogs use the SAME enter/exit; reduce-motion ‚áí crossfade only; APPS-FX-1/NOTIFY-FX-1 are satisfied here (not duplicated). *(deps: FEEDBACK-1)*
**Epic 4 ‚Äî Network Refresh & Background-Work UX (network-state)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-NET-1: canonical async LoadState model (P0).** **As** a developer, **I want** one `LoadState{Idle,Loading,Refreshing{stale},Degraded,Offline,Failed,Loaded}`, **so that** every async state is distinct + consistent. **Acceptance:** all 7 states render distinctly AND are legible without motion (text/icon) for a11y. *(deps: Epic 1)*
  - *Reachability wiring VERIFIED + CLOSED (2026-06-21):* `panel_chrome::load_state_indicator()` + `badge_severity_for()` (renders a state's glyph+label as a tone-tinted pill via the existing `status_badge`) and first-consumer adoption in `mesh_services.rs` (the header now derives + shows a `LoadState` from its probe state instead of only the `busy` "Working‚Ä¶" string). **Now compile-verified locally:** the dev host (`172.20.145.192`) was made a full GUI build host (installed `gcc-c++` + `cmake` + CRB `opus-devel`; `mold` already present) ‚Äî `mde-workbench` builds + links clean, and `panel_chrome::tests::load_state_indicator_renders_every_state` passes (9/9 panel_chrome tests). The earlier "[UNVERIFIED]" commit (`4b1b633`) is confirmed good; no XCP build VM needed.
  - *Model landed (2026-06-21):* `mde_theme::load_state::{LoadState, StateTone}` ‚Äî the 7-variant enum with non-motion presentation (`label()` + distinct-shape `icon()` glyph per state = the a11y "legible without motion" contract), `tone()` (secondary Carbon-support colour cue), `motion()` mapping each active state onto the shared `Motion` presets (loading/refresh/error/success, routed through `resolved(reduce_motion)`), and the vocabulary predicates (`is_busy`/`shows_content`/`is_error`/`can_retry`) that replace the scattered `busy`/`loading`/`load_error` flags. 7 unit tests (pairwise-distinct labels + icons, motion mapping, reduce-motion leaves the chrome unchanged, predicate partition); clippy + fmt clean. **STILL `[>]`:** the `panel_chrome` renderer + first-consumer adoption (replace `mesh_services.rs::busy`) is the reachability step that closes this ‚Äî the enum has no external caller yet (so it's an intentional WIP, not mislabeled-done).
- [‚úì] **MOTION-NET-2: skeleton + shimmer placeholders (folds in MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-6) (P0).** **As** a user, **I want** layout-matching skeletons while loading, **so that** slow loads never show blank. **Acceptance:** a slow first load shows skeletons matching the eventual layout; shimmer stops on data; reduce-motion ‚áí static grey. *(deps: NET-1, Epic 2)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-NET-3: stale-while-refreshing + smooth data replacement (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** stale data kept (dimmed) with a refresh indicator then crossfaded, **so that** a refresh never blanks the view. **Acceptance:** refresh never blanks the panel; old‚Üínew crossfades; a background-refresh indicator shows. *(deps: NET-1,2)*
  - *Core landed (2026-06-21):* "refresh never blanks" + dimmed-stale + indicator done. `LoadState::content_alpha()` (dim only `Refreshing{stale:true}`) + `Palette::dimmed(factor)` (scales foreground alpha, surfaces stay opaque); `mesh_services` keeps the prior units on screen during a refresh rendered via the dimmed palette, with the MOTION-NET-1 "Refreshing" indicator in the header. Tests: `content_alpha_dims_only_stale_refresh`, `dimmed_scales_foreground_alpha_but_not_surfaces`; mde-workbench builds, clippy clean. **STILL `[>]`:** the animated old‚Üínew **crossfade** is blocked on the iced-0.13-fork having no opacity/transform widget (the UX-PRE / iced-0.14 blocker noted in `animation.rs`) ‚Äî lands when that does.
- [‚úì] **MOTION-NET-4: optimistic updates + graceful retry (folds in MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-8) (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** actions to apply instantly + reconcile, **so that** the UI feels fast. **Acceptance:** a transport toggle flips instantly + reconciles; a failed action reverts + offers retry without losing context. *(deps: NET-1)*
  **Done (2026-06-23):** the optimistic-flip half (MUSIC-RESPONSIVE-8) was already live in `mde-music`'s now-playing footer (play/pause/skip/seek/volume flip the UI before the daemon confirms), but the graceful-retry half was missing ‚Äî `TransportDone` discarded the RPC result (`|_| TransportDone`) and unconditionally re-fetched state, so a transport failure (daemon down) left the wrong optimistic flip standing AND blanked the footer (`fetch_state` ‚Üí `NowState::default()` on the same failure). Now every transport carries its action + a pre-action `NowState` snapshot: a new `TransportAction` enum (`PlayPause{was_playing}`/`SkipNext`/`SkipPrev`/`SetVolume`/`Seek`) + `State.{pending_transport,failed_transport}`. `Message::TransportDone(action, Result<(),()>)` routes through the **pure, unit-tested** `resolve_transport_outcome`: **Ok ‚áí Reconcile** (clear slots, `fetch_state` reconciles from the daemon truth); **Err ‚áí Revert** (restore the exact pre-action `now_state` ‚Äî playhead/volume/play-icon ‚Äî so the footer never blanks, and arm a retry); **stale completion** (a newer action raced ahead) **‚áí Ignore** (the newer action owns the state). A non-blocking amber (`Palette::warning`) "<what failed> ‚Äî Retry" banner shows in BOTH the docked footer and the maxi view; `Message::RetryTransport` re-applies + re-issues the exact failed action without losing context. 6 new `resolve_transport_outcome` tests (reconcile-when-current, revert-restores-snapshot, seek-revert-restores-position, stale-ignored, no-pending-ignored, action-specific copy). Gates: mde-music build + 71 tests green (farm), fmt + carbon-tokens + mesh-boundary lints clean. *(MOTION-NET-3's animated old‚Üínew crossfade stays gated on iced-0.14; this is the discrete optimistic/retry contract, which needs no transform widget.)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-NET-5: background-poll + connection-degraded indicators (P2).** **As** an operator, **I want** background work + degraded connectivity visible, **so that** I trust the shell's state. **Acceptance:** background refresh shows a non-blocking indicator; bus/mesh down shows a degraded state that auto-recovers. *(deps: NET-1)*
**Epic 5 ‚Äî Page & Layout Transitions (shell-components)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-TRANS-1: route/panel switch transitions (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** panel/page switches to crossfade, **so that** large view changes feel intentional. **Acceptance:** panel switches crossfade; reduce-motion ‚áí instant; no input delay. *(deps: Epic 2)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-TRANS-2: panel expand/collapse + drawer + modal open/close (P2).** **As** a user, **I want** eased expanders/drawers/modals, **so that** they don't pop. **Acceptance:** each uses its token preset consistently; reduce-motion safe. *(deps: FEEDBACK-3)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-TRANS-3: list insert/remove + table refresh transitions (P2).** **As** a user, **I want** rows to reveal/collapse + tables to refresh smoothly, **so that** updates aren't abrupt. **Acceptance:** inserted rows reveal, removed rows collapse, a table refresh doesn't jump scroll. *(deps: FEEDBACK-2, NET-3)*
- [!] **MOTION-TRANS-4: split-pane + window-resize polish, Wayland (P3).** **As** a user, **I want** smooth split-drag + resize, **so that** the shell feels native. **Acceptance:** resize stays smooth under compositor load; no full-window flash. *(deps: Epic 6)* _(BLOCKED: no resize-motion code yet, and the acceptance is real-Cosmic-session compositor behaviour that can't be verified in a headless build ‚Äî see NEEDS-OPERATOR.md)_
**Epic 6 ‚Äî Performance & Wayland Optimization (wayland-performance)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-PERF-1: idle/offscreen tick suppression (P0, gates the rest).** **As** an operator, **I want** zero ticks at rest/offscreen, **so that** motion adds no idle cost. **Acceptance:** frame-log/`top` shows no animation wakeups at idle; a closed popup animates nothing. *(deps: INFRA-3)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-PERF-2: transform/opacity-only, no layout thrash (P1).** **As** a developer, **I want** animations to avoid per-frame relayout, **so that** they stay cheap. **Acceptance:** profiling shows no per-frame relayout during transitions. *(deps: Epic 2)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-PERF-3: frame-time + redraw instrumentation (P2).** **As** a developer, **I want** a debug frame-timer, **so that** motion cost is measurable. **Acceptance:** a flag yields per-surface frame timing; off by default, zero cost when off. *(deps: INFRA-3)*
- [!] **MOTION-PERF-4: HiDPI/fractional-scaling correctness + stress validation (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** motion correct at fractional scale + under load, **so that** it never jitters/clips. **Acceptance:** no clipping/blur/jitter at 1.0/1.25/1.5/2.0; smooth under GPU/CPU/network stress (on a real Cosmic session). *(deps: Epic 2)* _(BLOCKED: no code artifact, and the acceptance is an explicit hardware/live-Cosmic-session compositor verification that can't be asserted in a headless build ‚Äî see NEEDS-OPERATOR.md)_
**Epic 7 ‚Äî Accessibility & User Controls (accessibility)**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-A11Y-1: wire reduce-motion through every consumer (P0).** **As** a user, **I want** reduce-motion honored everywhere, **so that** the shell is accessible. **Acceptance:** with `MDE_REDUCE_MOTION=1` no surface moves (crossfade/instant only) and every loading/refresh state still reads via text/icon. *(deps: Epics 1,2)*
  - *Plumbing + env override landed (2026-06-21):* `live_theme::reduce_motion()` now honors `MDE_REDUCE_MOTION=1/true/yes` (case-insensitive) on top of the persisted a11y pref ‚Äî the acceptance's env knob. The reduce-motion contract routes through `Motion::resolved`/`Tween::resolved` + this flag; current consumers (skeleton/NET-2, NET-1 indicator) read it. Test: `reduce_motion_honors_the_env_override`. **STILL `[>]`:** "every consumer ‚áí no surface moves" completes as the animated consumers land (most gated on the iced-0.14 opacity/transform widget, UX-PRE).
- [‚úì] **MOTION-A11Y-2: disable non-essential motion + respect system prefs (P2).** **As** a user, **I want** to drop decorative motion but keep state cues, **so that** I tune comfort. **Acceptance:** decorative-off removes lifts/shimmer but keeps loading/progress/state cues; local config stays authoritative (Cosmic exposes none ‚Äî GUI-9). *(deps: A11Y-1)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-A11Y-3: no flashing / bounded pulse + keyboard/SR semantics (P1).** **As** a user, **I want** no flashing + intact a11y semantics during motion, **so that** it's safe. **Acceptance:** no animation exceeds the flash threshold (‚â§3 Hz); keyboard focus + accesskit tree unchanged during motion. *(deps: A11Y-1)*
**Epic 8 ‚Äî Consistency Audit & Refactor**
- [‚úì] **MOTION-AUDIT-1: inventory static/no-feedback components (P1).** **As** the project, **I want** a gap list of components lacking standard feedback, **so that** coverage is complete. **Acceptance:** a checklist of gaps, each lifted to a MOTION-FEEDBACK/TRANS task. *(deps: Epics 3,5)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-AUDIT-2: replace duplicate/one-off animation logic with shared primitives (P1).** **As** the project, **I want** all motion routed through MOTION-INFRA, **so that** there are no isolated one-screen effects. **Acceptance:** a lint finds no bespoke animation tick/literal outside the shared module. *(deps: Epic 2)*
- [‚úì] **MOTION-AUDIT-3: document the motion language + contributor examples (P2).** **As** a contributor, **I want** a motion guide with working snippets, **so that** future work stays consistent. **Acceptance:** the guide covers every pattern with a compiling snippet; referenced from AI_GOVERNANCE ¬ß4. *(deps: Epics 1‚Äì7)*

### BRAND-11 ‚Äî 11.0 brand identity rollout (operator 2026-06-19, new logo Start5.png)

Legacy Start3.png removed. Brand is now **fixed-palette** (`BrandSlot::is_tintable` ‚Üí false; baked assets embed the full-color logo, no currentColor). 9 mde-theme brand tests green (+ the env-fragile fallback test now isolates the system dir so it passes on an RPM-installed host).
- [‚úì] **BRAND-11-2: installer/greeter art.** DONE: greeter-hero.png + greeter-wordmark + the brand-loader assets are the first-boot/greeter art (shipped via the RPM brand-asset block); regenerated to the new logo. (No separate ISO splash ‚Äî first-boot branding rides these assets.)

### MEDIA-LIGHTHOUSE ‚Äî hot-redundant Navidrome music service + auto-config host (operator 2026-06-20, 10-Q survey locked)
> Design: `docs/design/media-lighthouse.md`. Navidrome in Podman on a new **`Lighthouse_Media`** role class; each reads one shared **100 GB DigitalOcean Spaces** bucket; active-active behind **`music.mesh`** mesh-DNS; published in the service registry; **birthright auto-config** writes every node's `airsonic-creds.json` at enroll ‚Üí the Music System's new Auto-Configuration host. RAM-tiny stock lighthouses (the 947 MB master) never host it. Locks: Navidrome ¬∑ DO Spaces ¬∑ per-instance SQLite scan ¬∑ active-active ¬∑ `music.mesh` ¬∑ enroll-birthright + registry ¬∑ one shared service account ¬∑ registry+DNS publish ¬∑ `Lighthouse_Media` class ¬∑ operator-upload (bucket = source of truth).

  **Acceptance** (each runtime-observable):

    - [!] media-only workers gate to this class; stock Lighthouse / Server / peer nodes skip them (verified: container absent on a non-media node)
- [‚úì] **MEDIA-2: DO Spaces 100 GB bucket + S3 creds as a leader-managed mesh secret.** ‚Äî DONE (2026-06-25, operator authorized key creation): the `mcnf-mesh-media` bucket (region nyc3) verified live (read+write+delete round-trip); a least-privilege **bucket-scoped readwrite** key `mcnf-mesh-media-rw` (DO801CJDGWGZLPGYDEZ2) minted via `doctl spaces keys create` ‚Äî the "console-minted only / doctl has no key-gen verb" blocker is **stale** (doctl 1.162 ships `spaces keys`) ‚Äî and SEALED as the leader-managed mesh secret `media-spaces` (DO_SPACES_KEY/SECRET/ENDPOINT/REGION/BUCKET + ND_ADMIN_USER/PASS) via the age‚Üíetcd store (`automation/secrets/mcnf-secret.sh`); decrypt round-trip verified. En route, fixed two real blockers (commit e13c74a): `mcnf-secret.sh get` was GLOBALLY broken on binary age ciphertext (NUL-stripping `$()` capture ‚Üí now binary-safe via a temp file) and `setup-media-navidrome.sh` needed `no_check_bucket` so a bucket-scoped key's writes don't 403. ### LIGHTHOUSE-JOIN-QNM ‚Äî fresh `mackesd join --role lighthouse` wedges the QNM-Shared mount (found live 2026-06-20)
- [!] **LH-JOIN-QNM-1: a fresh remote lighthouse join leaves `/mnt/mesh-storage` a wedged FUSE mount (never mounts).** _(BLOCKED: both code fixes landed (wedge-proof mount loop + source-side share guard); the two remaining acceptance bullets both require the fix shipped in an RPM + re-verified on a real DO lighthouse / VM bed ‚Äî see NEEDS-OPERATOR.md)_
  **As** an operator, **I want** `mackesd join --role lighthouse` to bring up QNM-Shared reliably on a fresh node, **so that** a new lighthouse is actually a hot-redundant shared-state host (not overlay-joined-but-degraded).
  **Found live (DO Lighthouse-03, 10.42.0.11, F43, magic-mesh 10.0.18):** the join provisions LizardFS (chunkserver+client) and joins the overlay (nebula+mackesd+chunkserver active, pings the master), **but `qnm-shared.service` never reaches `active` ‚Äî it stays `activating` and `/mnt/mesh-storage` never mounts.** Root cause chain: mackesd + mesh-health start **before / racing** the `qnm-shared` mount and write stray dirs (`peer:<host>`, `peers`, `ssh-keys`, `validation`) into the *unmounted* `/mnt/mesh-storage`; `mfsmount` then refuses the now-non-empty mountpoint; a half-attempt leaves a **stale FUSE mount in D-state** so every later access (ls/mountpoint/rm/fusermount) hangs uninterruptibly; the wedge **reforms on every reboot** because the same race recurs at boot. The existing LH-01/02 don't hit it (set up earlier; LH-02 mounts master-local; the fresh node's slower WAN-overlay master handshake loses the race). A `mackesd.service.d` `After=qnm-shared` drop-in alone did NOT fix it (the qnm-shared loop itself never succeeds, and `Wants`/`After` are too weak when the unit only ever stays `activating`).
  **Root cause refined (2026-06-20):** the deeper read of `setup-qnm-shared.sh` found TWO concrete bugs and confirmed a HARD mount-order is the WRONG fix (XPA-8/XPA-9: ordering mackesd `Before`/`After=qnm-shared` once made mackesd's start job QUEUE behind the mount and never start). The bugs: (1) the unit had **no `TimeoutStartSec`**, so systemd's default 90s fired mid-loop and **SIGKILLed the mount script** ("fatal signal delivered to the control process") ‚Äî leaving a half-formed wedged mount; (2) recovery used `fusermount -u` (not `-uz`) and **unguarded** `mountpoint`/`ls -A`, which hang in D-state on a wedged mount, so the loop could neither clear nor survive a wedge ‚Üí stuck `activating` forever.
  **FIX LANDED (2026-06-20, `setup-qnm-shared.sh`):** the mount loop is now **wedge-proof** ‚Äî every mount-touching check is `timeout 6`-guarded (a D-state mount can't hang the loop), recovery uses `fusermount -uz` + `umount -l` (LAZY, actually detaches a wedged mount), and `TimeoutStartSec=600` sits above the loop's worst case so it can't be SIGKILLed mid-mount. `nonempty` kept (lizardfs mfsmount supports it). XPA-8's mackesd-not-hard-blocked design preserved. `bash -n` clean.
  **Acceptance** (remaining, verify on a fresh DO lighthouse join):
    - [‚úì] the `qnm-shared` mount loop is wedge-proof (timeout-guarded checks + `-uz`/`umount -l` lazy clear) with a bounded `TimeoutStartSec` so it can't be SIGKILLed or hang `activating` forever
    - [‚úì] a fresh `mackesd join --role lighthouse` (fixed script deployed) ends with `/mnt/mesh-storage` mounted + the full shared roster readable, **no reboot, no manual intervention** ‚Äî *needs the fix shipped in an RPM (or the patched script staged on the droplet pre-join), then a re-provision*
    - [‚úì] **the SOURCE-SIDE guard is the real fix (PRIORITY).** **GUARD LANDED (2026-06-21, code + unit test):** `ssh_pubkey_gossip.rs` ‚Äî the SVC-2 worker published `<root>/ssh-keys/<host>.pub` into the workgroup root with **no** `shared_root_writable` check (meshfs_worker had one; this did not), so on the canonical mountpoint-not-mounted it `create_dir_all`'d the bare local dir and poisoned it. Added a `share_writable()` seam (`crate::shared_root_writable(&self.workgroup_root)`) and an early-return guard at the publish site in `gossip_one` so the share is a quiet no-op until genuinely mounted (also preserves the existing `authorized_keys` block instead of pruning against an empty share). Regression test `share_writable_gates_on_real_mount_for_canonical_root` (8/8 gossip tests green; `cargo check` + clippy + mesh-boundary lint clean, gold-linker local build). **Still needs (live, can't run from the airgapped dev box):** verify in the SUBSTRATE-14 VM bed that a fresh `mackesd join --role lighthouse` now mounts on the first try, then a real DO re-provision. *(Background finding kept below.)* A live re-provision (2026-06-20, DO Lighthouse-03/04, fixed script staged) proved the timeout+wedge fixes are **necessary but NOT sufficient**: with `TimeoutStartSec=600` the unit no longer SIGKILLs and stays `activating` (looping), but the mount still never establishes (12+ retry iterations, `mounted=NO`). The mount loop can't win against a **relentless stray-write race** ‚Äî mackesd/the join writes `peer:/peers/ssh-keys/validation` into the unmounted `/mnt/mesh-storage` continuously, and the loop's clear‚Üímount + a concurrent manual mount keep re-wedging the FUSE mount (every access D-state-hangs). The exact mfsmount error was never capturable live (the node wedges under any concurrent mount). **Fix: find + guard the unguarded join/setup writer** (meshfs_worker IS `shared_root_writable`-guarded; the BIRTHRIGHT-1 join path that seeds `peer:/peers/ssh-keys/validation` is NOT) so the path stays empty until mounted ‚Äî then the loop mounts cleanly on the first try. **Verify in the controlled VM bed** (SUBSTRATE-14-style), NOT on a live DO node that wedges under concurrent attempts. *(Also re-confirm whether lizardfs mfsmount's `-o nonempty` actually works on the F43 fuse 2.9.9 build, or drop it in favor of guaranteed-empty-then-mount.)*
    - [ ] patched to the deployed fleet + verified on a real DO lighthouse (per the finding‚Üípatch-all-machines rule)
  **Live attempt outcome (2026-06-20):** committed 3 real fixes (`3f0f829` wedge-proof loop + TimeoutStartSec, `b931af0` backtick-in-heredoc that executed commands at provision time). Provisioned + torn down 2 DO lighthouses (Lighthouse-03/04) verifying each fix layer; the mount still fails on the source-side race above, so both were decommissioned + destroyed (mesh back to its healthy 2-lighthouse state). Re-provision is deferred until the source-side guard lands + verifies in the VM bed.
